The Argument from 'Al-Kabad'
A rhetorical argument using astrologers' own belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses astrologers' own belief in an unseen star to argue for the existence of other unknown celestial influences.

Core Idea
If astrologers accept one unseen influence, they cannot reject others.

This brief but powerful argument turns the astrologers' own assumptions against them. The author points out that astrologers have already affirmed a mysterious star called 'al-kabad' and given it influence. By their own logic, they cannot deny the possibility of many other hidden stars impacting astrological predictions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the author presents this as the 'fourth' argument, implying a series. The argument is a single rhetorical question.
The term 'al-kabad' is unfamiliar; it is a hypothetical construct used for argument.
2
Identify the rhetorical strategy
See how the author first states what the astrologers affirm (al-kabad and its influence) and then asks a logical question. This is a tu quoque or consistency argument: if you accept X, you must accept Y.
The author does not need to prove the existence of al-kabad; he takes it as given by astrologers.
3
Reflect on the logical force
Consider why the author uses this argument. It exposes an inconsistency: astrologers are selective about which unseen influences they accept. The argument is not about the reality of al-kabad but about the principle of consistency.
This argument is effective because it uses the opponent's own material.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع : إن أصحاب الأحكام أثبتوا شيئاً ، يسمونه بالكبد ، وأثبتوا حظا من التأثير له ، وإذا جاز ثبوته ، فلم لا يجوز ثبوت غيره ؟
The fourth: The astrologers have affirmed something which they call 'al-kabad' (the liver), and they affirmed a portion of influence for it. And if its existence is allowed, then why is the existence of other [unknown stars] not allowed?
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This short fourth argument is a rhetorical point: astrologers themselves believe in an invisible star named 'al-kabad' (probably a hypothetical point or star) and ascribe influence to it. If they accept such an unseen entity, they logically cannot deny the existence of other unknown stars that might affect astrological predictions. The argument is that consistency demands acknowledging many hidden celestial bodies.

Key Terms
الكبد
حظ من التأثير
أصحاب الأحكام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Al-kabad is a star that actually exists
B) If astrologers accept one unseen influence, they should accept others
C) Al-kabad has no influence
D) Astrologers deny unknown stars

Key Takeaway
The author astutely uses astrologers' own belief in 'al-kabad' to argue that they must accept the existence of many other unknown stars influencing the world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Zodiacal Natures and the Necessity of Unknown Stars
A logical proof that variations in zodiacal effects require hidden stars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the uniformity of the celestial sphere leads to the conclusion that unseen stars must exist to explain differences in zodiacal influences.

Core Idea
Differences in zodiacal effects prove the existence of hidden stars.

This lesson presents a powerful argument from classical Islamic cosmology that uses logical deduction to infer the existence of unseen celestial bodies. The author shows that if the celestial sphere is a simple substance, then zodiacal signs must share the same essence, implying that any variation in planetary influences must be due to hidden stars. We will walk through the steps of this argument and see how it connects to larger debates.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the gist of the argument. Notice the logical structure: premises, contradiction, and resolution.
2
Identify the key premises
Spot the key premises: the celestial sphere is a simple substance; therefore zodiacal signs must have the same essence; therefore a planet's influence should be uniform across signs.
3
Examine the contradiction
Notice that this conclusion contradicts the observed facts of astrology (different influences in different signs). This forces a choice between two explanations.
4
Understand the conclusion
See why the author rejects the idea that signs have different essences (it implies composition, contradicting simplicity) and accepts the existence of unseen stars as the cause of differences.
This is the desired conclusion that supports the existence of hidden celestial bodies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الخامس : في بيان أن الأمر كما ذكرناه : إن الفلاسفة أطبقوا على أن الفلك جوهر بسيط ، وإذا ثبت هذا ، فنقول : يجب أن تكون طبائع البروج متساوية في تمام الماهية ، وإلا لزم التركيب ، وإذا ثبت هذا ، فتأثير الكوكب حال كونه في برج ، يجب أن يكون مساوياً لتأثيره حال كونه في سائر البروج ، لما ثبت في العقول أن حكم الشيء حكم مثله . ومعلوم أن ذلك على خلاف علم النجوم ، فأما أن يقال : إن طبائع البروج مختلفة بحسب الماهيات ، فذلك قول مردود عند الفلاسفة . أو يقال : إنه حصل في كل برج كواكب صغيرة لا نراها ولا نشاهدها، ولأجل حصول تلك الكواكب في تلك البروج ، صارت طبائع البروج مختلفة في التأثرات . وذلك هو المطلوب
The fifth aspect: In explaining that the matter is as we have stated: The philosophers have agreed that the celestial sphere is a simple substance. If this is established, then we say: The natures of the zodiacal signs must be equal in complete essence; otherwise composition would follow. If this is established, then the influence of a planet while in a sign must be equal to its influence while in other signs, because it is established in intellects that the judgment of a thing is the judgment of its like. And it is known that this contradicts the science of the stars. So either it is said that the natures of the signs are different according to their essences – that is a rejected statement among the philosophers – or it is said that in each sign there are small stars that we do not see or perceive, and because of the presence of those stars in those signs, the natures of the signs become different in effects. And that is the desired conclusion.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This fifth argument is a logical proof. Premise: Philosophers agree the celestial sphere (al-falak) is a simple substance (jawhar basit). If so, the zodiacal signs (al-burūj) must have identical essences (mahiyya), otherwise they would be composite. If essences are identical, then a planet's effect in one sign should be the same as in any other, because like things have like effects. But this contradicts the known facts of astrology, where planets differ by sign. There are two options: either the signs have different essences – but philosophers reject this because it implies composition – or there are unknown small stars in each sign that cause the difference. The author concludes this second option is the correct one, proving his point about unknown stars.

Key Terms
فلك
جوهر بسيط
طبائع البروج
الماهية
تأثير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument is a critique of astrology.
Correction: The argument actually uses astrological observations as evidence for the existence of unseen stars, rather than rejecting astrology itself.

Checkpoint
According to the argument, why must zodiacal signs have the same essence?
A) Because philosophers said so without reason
B) Because the celestial sphere is a simple substance, so its parts cannot differ in essence
C) Because planets are simple substances
D) Because astrologers agree on this

Key Takeaway
The observed differences in planetary influences across zodiacal signs can only be explained by the presence of unseen stars in each sign.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author deduces the existence of unseen stars from observed effects. Are you living as though unseen realities (like Allah, angels, the Last Day) are just as certain as what you see? What would change if you truly acted on that certainty?
?
In this argument, the philosopher's assumption of a simple sphere is challenged by empirical data. When your own assumptions conflict with evidence, do you adjust your beliefs, or do you reject the evidence? Can you think of a belief you hold that needs reexamination?
?
Just as hidden stars explain the differences in zodiacal effects, what 'hidden' spiritual root causes might explain the patterns in your own life (e.g., recurring sins, lack of barakah)? Are you willing to seek them out and address them?

The Empirical Argument from Astrological Errors
Sanusi presents an empirical argument from astrological errors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the frequent failure of astrological predictions serves as evidence for the existence of unknown celestial bodies according to this author.

Core Idea
Astrology's repeated mistakes point to stars we have not yet seen.

The author presents a sixth argument, one that is grounded in observable experience. He notes that astrological forecasts very often go wrong. Rather than dismissing such errors as random chance, he offers a specific explanation: the influence of stars that are unknown to us. This passage invites us to think about how empirical anomalies can be interpreted as clues to hidden realities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the concise style and the causal link made by 'إن' and 'وما ذاك إلا بسبب'.
2
Identify the observation
Find the empirical premise: astrological indicators (الدلائل النجومية) often become disordered and corrupted. This is the fact the author starts from.
The verbs تختل وتفسد indicate a pattern, not a rare event.
3
Understand the inference
The author then states the cause: unknown stars (كواكب لا تعرفها) that exist and affect the outcomes. This is an inference from the observed failure to an unseen reality.
The phrase 'بسبب ما ذكرنا' refers back to earlier arguments about unknown stars.
4
Reflect on the argument's nature
This is an a posteriori argument (min al-'ālam ilā al-khāliq). It uses empirical evidence to support a metaphysical claim. Consider how this differs from purely rational proofs.
5
Connect to the broader context
This is the sixth of several proofs for unknown celestial bodies. Think about how this empirical argument complements the rational ones given before.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه السادس : إن الدلائل النجومية قد تختل وتفسد في كثير من الأوقات ، وما ذاك إلا بسبب ما ذكرنا . أنه حصلت هناك كواكب لا تعرفها ولأجلها تختلف أحوال هذه الآثار والله أعلم
The sixth aspect: The astrological indicators often become disordered and corrupted on many occasions, and that is only because of what we mentioned – that there exist stars there that we do not know, and because of them the states of these effects differ. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This sixth argument is empirical: astrological predictions (dalā'il nujūmiyya) frequently fail (takhtall wa tafsud). The author attributes these failures to unknown stars that disrupt the expected influences. This is presented as further evidence for the existence of celestial bodies beyond human observation.

Key Terms

تختل
تفسد
كواكب لا تعرفها

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author is rejecting astrology entirely.
Correction: The author accepts astrological indicators as real but argues that their frequent failure points to the influence of unknown stars, not that astrology is invalid.

Checkpoint

A) Human error
B) The will of God

Key Takeaway
The frequent corruption of astrological signs is taken as evidence for the existence of stars beyond human knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

This passage suggests that failures point to hidden realities. What hidden realities might your own failures be pointing you toward—things you do not yet know but need to acknowledge? ?

Do you flee from confusion, or do you ask what hidden causes might be at work? This lesson challenges you to treat disorder as a window into the unseen. Will you look for what you might be missing? Make a concrete decision to pause before dismissing confusion as meaningless.
?
Sanusi ends with 'And God knows best.' True knowledge belongs to Allah. In what area of your life have you pretended to have more certainty than you actually possess? How does this admission of ignorance transform your heart? This week, identify one claim you've been too sure about and replace it with 'Allahu a'lam.' Let that phrase humble you.

Three Reasons Fixed Stars Are Stronger than Planets
Author enumerates three reasons for fixed stars' superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three arguments the author presents for why fixed stars are stronger than planets, and how each reason builds on principles of causality, multiplicity, and motion.

Core Idea
Fixed stars are superior in proximity to God, number, size, and stillness.

In this passage, the author presents the third of three proofs for the superiority of fixed stars over planets. He enumerates three clear reasons: closeness to the First Principle, multiplicity and size, and slowness of motion. Each reason draws on established principles of natural philosophy and theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own words introduce the three reasons.
Notice the structure: a general statement followed by three numbered points.
2
Identify the three reasons
Find each of the three reasons in the text. Mark how the author introduces each one (أولها، ثانيها، ثالثها).
Each reason is a separate argument for why fixed stars are stronger.
3
Understand the logic of each reason
For each reason, ask: What principle does the author use? (proximity to First Principle, multiplicity, size, slowness). How does that principle lead to greater strength?
The author assumes that proximity to the source of perfection, numbers, size, and lasting alignment all confer strength.
4
See the conclusion
Read the final sentence: the evidence establishes that fixed stars are stronger and more perfect in influence. Notice how the three reasons together build this conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الثالث في بيان أن الثوابت أقوى من السيارات : هو أنها أكمل من السيارات في أمور ثلاثة :
أولها : أنها أقرب في درجة المعلولية ، والعبودية إلى المبدأ الأول من هذه السيارات ، وذلك القرب هو المنبع لكل الكمالات
وثانيها : أنها كثيرة في العدد جداً ، والكثرة مظنة القوة ، وأيضاً : فالثوابت التي في العظم الأول [أكبر (۱) ] قدراً من كل السيارات إلا الشمس . والعظم في الجرمية ، يفيد العظم في القوة
وثالثها : أنها أبطأ حركة . فيكون بقاؤها في الدرجة الواحدة أدوم . وقد علمت في الطبيعيات : أن دوام المسامتة ، يوجب كمال القوة . فثبت بهذه البيانات : أن الكواكب الثابتة أقوى قوة ، وأكمل تأثيراً من السيارات
And the third aspect in explaining that the fixed stars are stronger than the planets: is that they are more perfect than the planets in three matters:
First: that they are closer in degree of effecthood and servitude to the First Principle than these planets, and that proximity is the source of all perfections.
Second: that they are very numerous in number, and multiplicity is a place of strength, and also: the fixed stars which are in the first magnitude are greater in measure than all the planets except the sun. And greatness in corporeality benefits greatness in strength.
Third: that they are slower in motion. So their remaining in one degree is more lasting. And you have learned in the natural sciences: that the duration of alignment necessitates perfection of strength. So it is established by these evidences: that the fixed stars are stronger in strength and more perfect in influence than the planets.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage presents the third argument for the superiority of fixed stars over planets. It is an enumerative argument listing three reasons why fixed stars are more perfect and powerful. The author first states that fixed stars are closer to the First Principle in terms of being effects and servants, and this proximity is the source of all perfections. Second, fixed stars are vastly more numerous, and multiplicity implies strength; additionally, the fixed stars of the first magnitude are larger than all planets except the sun, and corporeal size indicates strength. Third, fixed stars move more slowly, so they remain in one position longer; from natural philosophy, lasting alignment produces perfect strength. The author concludes that these evidences prove the fixed stars are stronger and more effective than the planets.

D) Their smaller size

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author says multiplicity and size indicate strength. But in your spiritual life, is it true that doing many things makes you stronger? Or is there a kind of spiritual strength that comes from focusing on one thing deeply? Which do you actually practice?

Astrologers' Limited Knowledge of Fixed Stars
Author notes astrologers agree fixed stars give strong effects but know little.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why astrologers' limited knowledge of fixed stars' natures leads to confusion in their science.

Core Idea
Astrologers admit ignorance about fixed stars, undermining their own predictions.

This passage highlights a paradox: astrologers agree that fixed stars have powerful effects when aligned with ascendants, yet they also admit to knowing very little about the specific natures of those stars. The author uses this self-proclaimed ignorance to expose a fundamental weakness in astrological claims. We'll explore how this concession leads to confusion and difficulty in the practice of astrology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once, then follow along with the English translation. Notice the two points of agreement among astrologers.
The passage is concise; each sentence carries weight.
2
Identify the two agreements
The passage presents two things astrologers agree on: (1) fixed stars give strong effects when on specific ascendants, and (2) they know only a little of the stars' natures. See how these two points connect.
The first agreement establishes power, the second limits knowledge.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that because of limited knowledge, confusion and difficulty appear in astrology. Ask yourself: Does this undermine the reliability of astrology?
This connects to the learning objective about why the science is flawed.

Source Text

Three Difficulties in Planetary Astrology
The author enumerates three difficulties in planetary astrology and justifies its study.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational challenges that make perfect knowledge of planetary astrology impossible, and why it is still worthwhile to study it.

Core Idea
Planetary astrology faces insurmountable complexities, yet its partial knowledge benefits human welfare.

The author acknowledges that even if we know the natures of planets, several obstacles prevent complete knowledge. He lists three difficulties: infinite combinations, overriding influences, and variable sublunary matter. Despite these, he argues that the science is still valuable and obligatory to study.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author grants the natures of planets as known, then raises difficulties.
2
Identify the three difficulties
Find each of the three difficulties presented. Note how each one is introduced and what the specific obstacle is.
The first difficulty concerns infinite combinations, the second past conditions, the third material cause.
3
Understand the conclusion
Read the final part where the author explains why astrology should still be studied despite these difficulties. Note the principle 'what cannot be grasped entirely should not be abandoned entirely'.
This principle is a key takeaway for dealing with complex knowledge.
4
Reflect on the misconception
Consider the common misunderstanding that the third difficulty is about free will. The passage actually talks about variability in sublunary matter affecting outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الأول : إن إمتزاجات الكواكب ، ومناسباتها بحسب كل : حد ، ووجه ، ومثله ومنزل من منازل القمر ، ودرجة معينة من الدرجات الثلثمائة وستين . تصير غير متناهية ، وما لا ينتهي لا يمكن معرفته ؟
والثاني : هب أن مواضع الكواكب وامتزاجاتها صارت معلومة ، إلا أن احكام طوالع الوقت قد تندفع بحسب الطوالع الأصلية ، وبحسب الأحوال الماضية في الفلك. ومن الذي يمكنه الوقوف على جميع الأحوال الماضية في الفلك ؟
والثالث : إنه كما يعتبر في حصول الأثر ، حصول العلة الفاعلية فكذلك يعتبر في حصوله العلة القابلية ، ولهذا السبب اتفق المنجمون على أنه إذا ولد على الطالع الواحد : ابن مالك ، وابن قصاب . أو خباز [ فإنه لا يتساوى أثر ذلك الطالع فيهم . فعلمنا : أن آثار الطوالع تختلف بحسب اختلاف أحوال المادة السفلية ، لكن المواد السفلية سريعة التغير ، شديدة التبدل فكيف يمكن الوقوف على أحوالها ؟ فهذا ضبط الوجوه المذكورة في بيان أن الوقوف على أحوال هذا العالم بالتمام . والكمال صعب ، إلا أن العقلاء اتفقوا على أن ما لا يدرك كله ، لا يترك كله ، فهذا العلم وإن كان صعب المرام من هذه الوجوه ، إلا أن الاستقراء يدل على حصول النفع العظيم منه . وإذا كان كذلك ، وجب الاشتغال بتحصيله ، والاعتناء بشأنه، فإن القليل منه كثير ، بالنسبة إلى أحوال مصالح البشر [ والله أعلم (۲) ] .
And as for the planets: we say: suppose that their natures have become known, yet difficulty remains from aspects:
First: that the combinations of the planets and their relations according to every bound, face, image, and mansion of the moon, and a specific degree from the three hundred sixty degrees become infinite, and what does not terminate cannot be known.
Second: suppose that the positions of the planets and their combinations have become known, except that the judgments of the temporal ascendants may be repelled by the original ascendants and by the past conditions in the celestial sphere. And who can stand upon all the past conditions in the celestial sphere?
Third: just as in the occurrence of the effect, the occurrence of the efficient cause is considered, so likewise in its occurrence the material cause is considered, and for this reason the astrologers agreed that if a son of a king and a son of a butcher or a baker are born under the same ascendant, the effect of that ascendant is not equal in them. So we know that the effects of the ascendants differ according to the difference of the conditions of the sublunary matter, but the sublunary matters are quick to change and intensely variable, so how can one stand upon their conditions? So this is the summary of the mentioned aspects in explaining that standing upon the conditions of this world fully and perfectly is difficult, except that the rational people agreed that what cannot be grasped entirely should not be abandoned entirely. Thus this science, although it is difficult of access from these aspects, yet induction indicates the attainment of great benefit from it. And if that is so, it is obligatory to occupy oneself with acquiring it and to pay attention to its matter, for a little of it is much relative to the conditions of human welfare. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage enumerates three difficulties in planetary astrology and concludes with a justification for studying it despite these difficulties. The author begins by granting that the natures of planets are known, but then lists three problems. The first difficulty is that the combinations and relationships of planets according to various factors (such as bounds, faces, images, lunar mansions, and specific degrees) are infinite, and infinite things cannot be known. The second difficulty is that even if positions and combinations are known, the judgments of temporal ascendants can be overridden by original ascendants and past celestial conditions, and no one can know all past conditions. The third difficulty is that the effect depends not only on the efficient cause (the ascendant) but also on the material cause (the sublunary matter). Astrologers agree that different people born under the same ascendant receive different effects because sublunary matter varies, and this matter is rapidly changing and variable. Thus, complete knowledge of this world is extremely difficult. Nevertheless, the author notes that rational people agree that what cannot be fully grasped should not be abandoned entirely. Induction shows great benefit in astrology, so it is obligatory to study and attend to it, as even a little knowledge greatly benefits human welfare.

Key Terms
السيارات
إمتزاجات الكواكب
الطوالع
العلة الفاعلية
العلة القابلية
المادة السفلية
الاستقراء
مصالح البشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The third difficulty is about free will and moral responsibility.
Correction: The third difficulty is about the material cause: sublunary matter (e.g., human bodies) varies, causing different effects from the same ascendant. It is not about free will but about variability in empirical conditions.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason given for the third difficulty in planetary astrology?
A) Infinite combinations of planets
B) Overriding by original ascendants
C) Differences in sublunary matter affecting the material cause
D) Lack of knowledge of planetary natures

Key Takeaway
The three difficulties—infinite combinations, overriding ascendants, and variable sublunary matter—show that complete astrological knowledge is impossible, but partial knowledge is still beneficial and obligatory to pursue.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what area of your life have you abandoned a pursuit because you couldn't master it completely? How does this lesson challenge you to reconsider that decision?
?
The third difficulty highlights that the same cause (ascendant) produces different effects depending on the recipient's disposition. How does this remind you that your inner state—your heart, character, and intentions—shapes how divine provisions affect you? What can you actively do today to improve your receptivity?
?
The author says a little knowledge is much relative to human welfare. What small, consistent step can you take this week to learn a beneficial science (religious or worldly) that you have neglected, trusting that even a little brings great good?

The First Condition: Firm Belief Is Essential
Sanusi enumerates the first condition and its three reasons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first universal condition for astrological works to be effective: that firm belief (conviction) is mandatory, and you will grasp the three rational reasons given for this condition.

Core Idea
Conviction cooperates with celestial spirits; doubt blocks their aid.

The author has been discussing the general conditions for the practice of astrological works. He now introduces the first condition: faith in one's actions. This may seem obvious, but he provides three deep reasons why doubt nullifies benefit. Before we look at the passage, consider why internal certainty matters even more than external precision.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the English translation. Let the author's own argumentative flow come through before you interpret.
Notice the phrase 'لابد من رعاية أمور' which sets up the conditions.
2
Identify the condition itself
Locate the first condition: that performing these works with doubt yields no benefit. Understand the core assertion before moving to the reasons.
The condition is stated in the second sentence.
3
Understand each reason analogically
The author gives three reasons. For each, note the analogy used: (1) human spirits supporting higher spirits like matter supports bodies, (2) king and distrustful subject, (3) doubt leads to negligence. See how each justifies the condition.
The Ptolemy quote 'Astrology is from you and from it' encapsulates the first reason.
4
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself: How does this condition change the understanding of astrological practice? It highlights the inner state of the practitioner as critical, not just technical accuracy.
This condition applies to any spiritual work, not just astrology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في الشرائط الكلية المعتبرة في رعاية هذا النوع اتفق المحققون على أنه لابد من رعاية أمور : الشرط الأول : أن من أتى بشيء من هذه الأعمال ، ثم يكون شاكاً فيه ، لم ينتفع به . والسبب فيه وجوه : الأول : إن تأثيرات أرواح الكواكب أقوى من تأثيرات أجسادها ، فإذا قوى الاعتقاد في صحة الأعمال صارت الأرواح البشرية معاضدة للأرواح العلوية ، كما صارت المواد السفلية معاضدة للأجرام العلوية ، فلا جرم تقوى التأثيرات . أما إذا لم يحصل الاعتقاد القوي ، زالت المؤثرات الروحانية ، وبقيت الجسمانية خالية عن الروحانيات فلا جرم ضعف الأثر ، ولهذا السبب قال بطليموس : وعلم النجوم منك ومنها . والسبب الثاني : إن الروحانيات العلوية مطلعة على ما في قلوبنا ، وكما أن في هذا العالم من راجع ملكاً ، والتمس منه شيئاً ، ثم أنه ظهر لذلك الملك أن ذلك الرجل لا يثق بقوله ، ولا يلتفت إلى فعله ، فإنه ذلك الملك لا يسعى في تحصيل حاجته . فكذا ههنا . والسبب الثالث : إنه إذا لم يعتقد في صحة تلك الأعمال . فالظاهر : أنه لا يبالغ في جميع تلك الشرائط ، فلا جرم يفوت المقصود .
Concerning the universal conditions observed in practicing this type: the investigators agreed that it is necessary to observe matters: The first condition: that whoever performs something of these works while being doubtful about it will not benefit from it. The reason for this has aspects: The first: the influences of the spirits of the planets are stronger than the influences of their bodies. So when belief in the correctness of the works becomes strong, the human spirits become supportive of the higher spirits, just as lower materials become supportive of the celestial bodies, and consequently the influences become strong. But if strong belief does not occur, the spiritual influences disappear, and the physical ones remain devoid of spiritual ones, so inevitably the effect weakens. For this reason Ptolemy said: 'Astrology is from you and from it.' The second reason: the higher spiritual beings are informed of what is in our hearts. Just as in this world, if someone consults a king and asks him for something, then it becomes apparent to that king that the man does not trust his word nor pay attention to his action, then that king does not strive to fulfill his need. So likewise here. The third reason: if he does not believe in the correctness of those works, then apparently he will not be thorough in all those conditions, so inevitably the objective is missed.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage introduces the first of three universal conditions for the efficacy of astrological works. The author states that doubt nullifies benefit. Three reasons follow:

First reason: The spirits of planets are stronger than their bodies. Strong human belief makes human spirits cooperate with celestial spirits, like matter helps celestial bodies. Weak belief removes spiritual help, leaving only weak physical effects. The author cites Ptolemy's saying that astrology is partly from the practitioner and partly from the stars.

Second reason: Higher spiritual beings know our hearts. If a king sees a supplicant distrusts him, he does not help. Similarly, if a practitioner doubts, the spirits do not aid.

Third reason: Lack of belief leads to negligence in fulfilling conditions, thus failure.

Each reason underscores that firm conviction is essential for spiritual cooperation.

Key Terms
الشرط
الاعتقاد
أرواح الكواكب
المؤثرات الروحانية
بطليموس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that only external actions matter in astrological practices.
Correction: The passage shows that internal conviction is a prerequisite; without it, even correct external actions yield no benefit.

Checkpoint
According to the first reason, why does strong belief strengthen the effects of spiritual works?
A) Because it makes the human spirits oppose the higher spirits.
B) Because it makes the human spirits supportive of the higher spirits, just as lower materials support celestial bodies.
C) Because it makes the practitioner more physically powerful.
D) Because it causes the planets to change their positions.

Key Takeaway
Firm belief is not just a psychological state but a spiritual condition that enables cooperation with higher celestial forces.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of an important goal you are pursuing right now. To what extent do you truly believe it will succeed? Are there areas of hidden doubt that might be sabotaging your efforts? What concrete step can you take today to strengthen your conviction?
?
The second reason says higher beings know what is in our hearts. When you ask Allah for something in prayer, do you genuinely trust that He will respond? If not, what does that reveal about your faith? Will you ask Him for forgiveness and help to overcome that doubt?
?
Consider a spiritual practice you perform routinely, such as prayer or charity. Have you ever gone through the motions without truly believing it makes a difference? According to this lesson, such doubt may strip the act of its benefit. Will you commit to renewing your belief before your next act of worship?

The Second Condition: Perseverance Without Immediate Results
The author states the second condition and illustrates it with analogies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second condition of spiritual practice: the obligation to persist in offerings even when no immediate effect is observed, and the rationale behind this persistence.

Core Idea
Persistence is more important than immediate results.

This lesson introduces the second condition required for those engaging in spiritual exercises: perseverance. The text emphasizes that the practitioner must continue their offerings and rituals even when no visible effect appears. Drawing on the example of Aristotle and analogies of a lover and a courtier, the passage teaches that steadfastness is the key to eventual success.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice that it begins with 'الشرط الثاني' and then explains the condition.
Pay attention to the analogies at the end.
2
Identify the key obligation
What does the passage say is obligatory when offerings yield no effect? Find the phrase 'فالواجب أن لا ينقطع'.
The obligation is to not desist or abandon.
3
Analyze the analogies
Reflect on the analogies: Aristotle's example, the lover, and the courtier. What common theme do they share?
All illustrate persistence despite lack of reward.
4
Understand the rationale
The author says that if one knows how to approach an earthly king, one can endure hardship. How does this reasoning support the condition?
5
Apply the lesson
Consider how this principle of perseverance can apply to other areas of life or spiritual practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرط الثاني : إنه إذا قرب للأرواح ، أنواعاً من القرابين ، ولم يجد منها أثراً . فالواجب أن لا ينقطع عن ذلك العمل، وأن لا يتركها ، فإن من عرف أنه كيف يمكنه التقرب إلى الملك العظيم [ من ملوك الأرض ] علم أن تحمل العناء الكثير في هذا العلم : هين . قال أرسطو طاليس : وكنت مشتغلاً بهذا العلم صباحاً ومساء فإن وجدت أثراً حمدته، وإن لم أجد الأثر لم أسيء الظن به وإن طالت المدة وتراخت الأيام ورب شيء كان يعسر ، ثم إني كنت ما أنقطع عن المطلوب حتى أبلغه ويجب أن يكون سبيل الطالب لهذا العلم ، سبيل العاشق ، إذا لم يسامحه معشوقه . وسبيل من أراد الوصول إلى خدمة ملك ولا يقبله ، فإنه يبذل غاية الجهد ، رجاء الفوز بالمطلوب . فههنا أولى
The second condition: that when one offers for the spirits various types of offerings and does not find any effect from them, it is obligatory not to desist from that work and not to abandon them. For whoever knows how one can draw near to the great king among kings of the earth knows that enduring much hardship in this science is easy. Aristotle said: 'I was engaged in this science morning and evening; if I found an effect I praised it, and if I did not find an effect I did not think ill of it, even if the period was long and the days were slow, and perhaps something was difficult, then I did not cease from the sought until I attained it.' And it is necessary that the way of the seeker of this science be the way of the lover when his beloved does not treat him gently, and the way of one who desires access to the service of a king and is not accepted, for he exerts utmost effort hoping to win the sought. So here it is more fitting.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage presents the second condition: persistence. When offerings fail to produce a visible effect, one must not give up. The author gives two analogies:

First, Aristotle is quoted: He practiced this science constantly. If he found an effect, he praised; if not, he did not think ill of it, persevering until success.

Second, the seeker should be like a lover who does not give up when his beloved is unkind, or like a courtier who strives even when rejected, hoping eventually to be accepted.

The author concludes that perseverance is all the more necessary in spiritual work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Immediate results are expected from spiritual offerings.
Correction: The passage teaches that one must persist even without immediate effect, not abandoning the practice.

Checkpoint

A) Abandon the practice immediately.
B) Try different offerings.
C) Not desist from the work and continue patiently.
D) Blame the spirits for failure.

Key Takeaway
Perseverance in spiritual practice is obligatory even when no effect is visible, as demonstrated by the examples of Aristotle, the lover, and the courtier.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Is there an area of your deen where you have secretly concluded that your efforts are wasted? Read the words of Aristotle: 'if I did not find the effect I did not think ill of it.' What lie have you believed about your own persistence? Write down one concrete action you will take today to reverse that belief.

The Third Condition: Effort Cooperates with Astrology
Sanusi explains the third condition and categorizes people by astrological predisposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the author’s third condition qualifies astrological determinism by showing that people’s charts vary in support, and that perseverance can overcome lack of astrological help.

Core Idea
Natal charts are not the whole story; effort and perseverance complete the picture.

Many people mistakenly believe that everything is fixed by one’s natal chart. The author introduces a crucial third condition: the role of individual effort. He explains that while some people have charts that strongly support success, others have neutral charts and can still achieve through hard work. This passage sets the stage for a balanced view of fate and free will.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage ends mid-sentence without the third rank.
2
Identify the misconception
The author begins by stating what some people think. Identify that belief and understand why it is being challenged.
The misconception is that one's fate is entirely determined by the natal chart.
3
Examine the first rank
The first rank includes those whose charts show predisposition. Notice that even for them, success is not absolute – degrees of attainment vary infinitely.
This shows that charts set potential, not fixed outcomes.
4
Focus on the second rank
The second rank has neutral charts – neither help nor hinder. The key point is that perseverance (المواظبة) leads to a complete share.
This directly counters the misconception: effort matters.
5
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this is called the 'third condition' – it implies there are prior conditions. Think about how this balances determinism with human agency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرط الثالث : إن من الناس من يظن أن الإنسان لا ينال إلا ما دل عليه طالعه . وأعلم أن الناس في هذا الباب على ثلاث مراتب : فالمرتبة الأولى : الذين تدل طوالعهم الأصلية على كونهم مستعدين لهذا العلم . وهؤلاء إذا اشتغلوا بهذا العلم، وصلوا إلى المطلوب . إلا أنه لما كانت مراتب القوة والضعف غير متناهية في الصلاحية ، كانت مراتب الحصول غير متناهية . المرتبة الثانية : الذين لم يحصل في طوالعهم [ لا ما يعين ، ولا ] ما يمنع [ وهؤلاء إن واظبوا على العمل . وصلوا إلى نصيب كامل .
The third condition: among people there are those who think that a person does not attain except what his natal chart indicates. And know that people in this matter are of three ranks: The first rank: those whose original natal charts indicate that they are predisposed to this science. These, if they engage in this science, attain the desired. However, since the degrees of strength and weakness in suitability are infinite, the degrees of attainment are infinite. The second rank: those in whose natal charts there is neither what helps nor what prevents. These, if they persevere in work, attain a complete share.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage presents the third condition: the idea that some think success depends solely on one's natal chart. The author then dispels that by introducing three ranks of people:

First rank: Their charts show predisposition; if they work, they succeed. But the degrees of success vary infinitely due to varying suitability.

Second rank: Charts neither help nor hinder; with perseverance, they gain a full share.

The passage ends without detailing the third rank, possibly because it continues on the next page. The emphasis is that effort (work and perseverance) cooperates with astrological predisposition.

Key Terms
الشرط الثالث
الطالع
المراتب
الاستعداد
المواظبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A person's fate is entirely fixed by their natal chart; effort is irrelevant.
Correction: The author shows that charts vary: some indicate predisposition, others are neutral. In neutral cases, perseverance ensures success.

Checkpoint
According to the third condition, what distinguishes the second rank of people?
A) Their charts are entirely favorable.
B) Their charts neither help nor prevent, and they can attain a complete share through perseverance.
C) They are hopeless because their charts are unfavorable.
D) They must rely on others to interpret their charts.

Key Takeaway
Natal charts may indicate predisposition or neutrality, but effort and perseverance determine the actual outcome.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of the three ranks do you honestly believe you fall into regarding your pursuit of religious knowledge? Are you using your perceived lack of natural aptitude as an excuse to slacken your efforts, or your perceived natural gift as a reason to become complacent?
?
If tomorrow you discovered that your natal chart was completely neutral regarding your ability to understand and practice the deen, would you still persevere with the same intensity? What does your answer reveal about where you place your ultimate trust?
?
The passage states that even for the predisposed, degrees of attainment are infinite. Why do you settle for such a small portion when the potential is limitless? What specific effort have you been withholding because you assumed your chart did not support it?

The Third Rank and the Dignity of This Science
Author discusses the third rank and gives a cautionary analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author warns against dismissing this science based on personal failure, and appreciate its lofty rank that elevates a person to angelic status.

Core Idea
Perfection in this science is rare; failure in base crafts doesn't disprove them, so how much more so for this highest science.

The author now moves to a warning about the high station of this science. He insists that attaining it lifts one to angelic ranks, but cautions that not everyone will succeed. He uses a powerful analogy from everyday life to protect the science from hasty rejection.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage and Translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Let the author's flow sink in before analyzing.
Notice the shift from defining the third rank to extolling the science.
2
Identify the Two Main Points
The author makes two key claims: first, the high rank of this science (elevation to angelic realm), and second, the warning not to invalidate it due to some people's failure.
3
Examine the Analogy
The author uses an analogy: base crafts that people fail to master despite years of effort. Ask yourself why this analogy is effective in defending the science.
The logic is a fortiori: if low crafts are not disproven by failure, then even more so the highest science.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمرتبة الثالثة : الذين حصلت في طوالعهم ما يمنع ) ومراتب الدلائل المانعة غير متناهية ، فكذلك مراتب الامتناع غير متناهية . واعلم أن الوصول إلى هذا العلم، يوجب خروج الإنسان من حد الإنسانية ، ودخوله في عالم الملائكية . والكمال في كل شيء عزيز ، ولا سيما في أكمل الكمالات، وأعلى الدرجات. ولا ينبغي أن يعتقد الرجل : أن كل أحد هو أهل لهذا العلم ، فإذا اشتغل واحد بهذا العلم ، ولم يفز منه بطائل ، فلا أن يجعل ذلك دليلاً على بطلان هذا العلم، فإنا نرى الحرف الخسيسة ، والصنائع النازلة قد يتعب الإنسان نفسه في تعلمها سنين ، ثم إنه لا يتعلمها كما ينبغي فإذا كان هذا شاهداً في أخس الحرف ، فكيف الحال في أعلى الصنائع
And the third rank: those in whose ascendants occurs what prevents... and the ranks of preventing proofs are infinite, so likewise the ranks of prevention are infinite. And know that attaining this science necessitates the exit of man from the boundary of humanity and his entry into the world of angelicness. And perfection in everything is rare, especially in the most perfect of perfections and the highest of degrees. And it is not fitting for a man to believe that everyone is qualified for this science, for if someone occupies himself with this science and gains no profit from it, he should not make that a proof of the invalidity of this science. For we see that lowly crafts and base industries – a man may tire himself in learning them for years, yet he does not learn them as he ought. So if this is witnessed in the basest of crafts, how then is the case in the highest of industries?
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is an introduction and a warning. The author first mentions the third rank (of practitioners) whose ascendants contain something that prevents, and states that the ranks of preventing proofs and the ranks of prevention are both infinite. Then he emphasizes the high status of this science: it elevates man beyond humanity into the angelic realm. He notes that perfection is rare, especially in the highest matters. A key warning follows: one should not conclude that the science is false because some fail to master it. He gives an analogy: base crafts often take years to learn and still are not mastered, so how much more so for the highest science? This guards against hasty rejection.

Key Terms
المرتبة الثالثة
طوالع
الدلائل المانعة
الملائكية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That personal failure to master this science proves it is false.
Correction: The author uses an analogy of base crafts: if lowly crafts take years and are still not mastered, that doesn't disprove them; so even more so for this highest science.

Checkpoint
What analogy does the author use to argue that failure to master this science does not prove its invalidity?
A) The difficulty of learning astronomy.
B) Base crafts that people fail to master despite years of effort.
C) The angelic nature of the practitioner.
D) The infinite ranks of preventing proofs.

Key Takeaway
This science is so elevated that perfection in it is rare; failure is not evidence against its truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you personally felt like giving up on seeking deeper religious knowledge because you didn't see immediate results? How does the analogy of base crafts and the highest industry hold a mirror to your impatience?
?

?
Do you ever judge the truth of a teaching by the failure of its adherents? How does the a fortiori argument in this passage expose the injustice of that judgment? Will you commit to evaluating this science on its own merits rather than on flawed examples?

The Fourth Condition: Exaggeration in Perfection
Author states the fourth condition and enumerates three reasons.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why practitioners of this science must maintain extreme secrecy and perfection, and the three rational reasons given for this condition.

Core Idea
Secrecy and perfection protect the practitioner and the order of the world.

The author now turns to the fourth condition for this science: exaggeration in perfection, meaning utmost care and secrecy. He provides three compelling reasons for this requirement, ranging from the nature of rational souls to the preservation of world order. Let us explore each reason and understand the logical necessity behind this condition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the three numbered reasons and the overall structure.
The author uses 'الاول', 'الثاني', 'الثالث' to enumerate the reasons.
2
Analyze each reason individually
For each reason, identify the key claim and the logical connection to the condition. The first reason discusses rational souls and the effect of discovery; the second focuses on world order; the third on rarity and concealment.
3
Synthesize the reasons
Consider how these three reasons together justify the condition. Reflect on the common misconception that secrecy is selfish, while the author shows it preserves both the practitioner and the world system.
The common misunderstanding is that the condition is about selfishness, but it is about preserving the world's order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرط الرابع : اتفقوا على أن من شرائط هذا العلم : المبالغة في الكمال ، والسبب فيه وجوه : الأول : إن النفوس الناطقة ، قد ثبت أنها من جنس الأرواح الفلكية ، فتكون مؤثرة . وهذه الصناعة لو تمت ، أفادت السلطنة التامة على الأرواح والأجساد ، فإذا وقف الغير على أن إنساناً اشتغل بهذه الأعمال ، حصلت النفرة الشديدة في قلوبهم، والرغبة التامة في إبطال تلك الأعمال وإفسادها ، فتبطل تلك الأعمال بالكلية . والثاني : إن إشاعة هذا العلم : على خلاف مصالح العالم . لأن استيلاء الرجل الواحد على كلية العالم : أمر على خلاف نظام العالم . الثالث : إن الشيء إذا كان عزيزاً بولغ في حفظه وكتمانه ، فعدم المبالغة في الحفظ والكتمان ، يدل على أنه لا وقع له عنده ، وقد بينا : أن ضعف الاعتقاد فيه ، يوهن هذه الأعمال
The fourth condition: They agreed that among the conditions of this science is exaggeration in perfection. And the reason for it has aspects: First: The rational souls have been established to be of the kind of celestial spirits, so they are effective. And this craft, if perfected, brings complete dominion over spirits and bodies. So if others come to know that a man occupies himself with these works, severe aversion arises in their hearts and complete desire to nullify those works and corrupt them, so those works are completely invalidated. Second: Publicizing this science is contrary to the interests of the world, because the domination of one man over the whole world is contrary to the order of the world. Third: If a thing is rare, one exaggerates in preserving and concealing it; lack of exaggeration in preservation and concealment indicates that it has no importance for him, and we have shown that weakness of belief in it weakens these works.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth condition: 'exaggeration in perfection' (المبالغة في الكمال). The author gives three reasons (وجوه) for this condition. First, rational souls (النفوس الناطقة) are akin to celestial spirits and thus effective; if this craft is perfected it grants dominion over spirits and bodies, so if others become aware of it they will try to destroy it. Second, publicizing this science upsets the order of the world, as one man ruling everything would disrupt the world's system. Third, rare things are kept secret; laxity in concealment shows lack of esteem, and weak belief undermines the works. Thus the condition requires utmost care and secrecy.

Key Terms

النفوس الناطقة
الأرواح الفلكية
السلطنة التامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The condition of secrecy is due to selfishness or elitism.
Correction: The reasons given show that secrecy is necessary to prevent opposition, maintain world order, and preserve the value of the rare science.

Checkpoint

A) Out of envy.
B) Because the practitioner would gain complete dominion over spirits and bodies.
C) Because the practitioner neglected perfection.
D) Because the practitioner publicized his work.

Key Takeaway
The fourth condition requires practitioners to be extremely cautious and secretive, because public knowledge would lead to opposition, disrupt world order, and betray the rarity of the science.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Fifth Condition: Night Practice for Talismanic Works
Author enumerates the fifth condition with supporting authorities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the cosmological and practical reasons why night practice is preferred for talismanic operations, as taught by Aristotle and Hermes.

Core Idea
Night practice shields talismanic power from the sun's dominance and human eyes.

Sanusi now presents the fifth condition for effective talismanic work: performing it at night is superior to daytime. He supports this with quotes from two ancient authorities: Aristotle, who explains how the sun's power subdues spirits and daytime senses distract the heart, and Hermes, who emphasizes hiding work from eyes and sunlight. This condition is rooted in spiritual and physical principles, not mere custom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation carefully. Notice the structure: a condition statement followed by two authorities' quotes and a practical instruction.
The passage uses technical terms like النيرنج (talisman) and جمعية القلب (concentration of the heart).
2
Identify Aristotle's two reasons
Find Aristotle's two arguments: (1) the sun is a conquering sultan that overcomes spirits, and (2) daytime senses are occupied, hindering heart concentration.
Aristotle's reasoning blends cosmology (solar power) and psychology (sensory distraction).
3
Understand Hermes' principle
Hermes states that the best work is hidden from human eyes and sunlight, because eyes attract talismanic power and sunlight nullifies it.
This explains why night and secrecy are crucial.
4
Note the practical instruction
Hermes specifically instructs to work deterministic talismans and knots of desire at night, and to beware of eyes and shiny objects.
The instruction ties theory to practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرط الخامس : اتفقوا على أن ممارسة هذه الأعمال في الليل ، أولى منها في النهار . قال أرسطو : إن الشمس سلطان قاهر ، فهو بكمال سلطنته يقهر جميع الأرواح ، ولا يقوى شيء منها على الفعل . وأيضاً : الحواس في النهار ، تكون مشغولة بالمحسوسات ، فلا تحصل جمعية القلب ، وفي الليل تكون الحواس معطلة ، فكانت جمعية القلب في الليل أكمل . وقال هرمس : إن خير ما يعمل به العامل ، هو ما يخفى عن أعين البشر وشروق الشمس . لأن عيون البشر جاذبة بروحانيتها قوة النيرنج وشروق الشمس قوة تبطل قوة النيرنجات . ثم قال : اعمل نيرنجات القطعية وعقد الشهوة ، ودخنها كلها بالليل ، واحترز فيها عن العيون واللامعة
The fifth condition: They agreed that practicing these works at night is preferable to doing them in the daytime. Aristotle said: 'The sun is a conquering sultan, so by the perfection of its sultanhood it conquers all spirits, and none of them has power to act. Also: the senses in the daytime are occupied with sensible things, so the concentration of the heart is not obtained, and in the night the senses are inactive, so the concentration of the heart in the night is more perfect.' And Hermes said: 'The best that the worker works with is what is hidden from the eyes of humans and the rising of the sun. Because the eyes of humans attract by their spirituality the power of the talisman (al-niranj), and the rising of the sun is a force that nullifies the power of talismans (al-niranjat).' Then he said: 'Work deterministic talismans and the knots of desire, and fumigate them all at night, and beware in them of eyes and what shines'
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth condition: practicing at night is better than daytime. Two authorities are cited: Aristotle and Hermes. Aristotle gives two reasons: (1) The sun is a conquering ruler that overwhelms all spirits, preventing them from acting. (2) During the day the senses are busy with sensory things, so the heart cannot concentrate; at night the senses are idle, allowing perfect concentration (جمعية القلب). Hermes adds that the best work is hidden from human eyes and sunlight, because human eyes attract the power of the talisman (النيرنج) through their spirituality, and sunlight nullifies talismanic force. He then instructs to work deterministic talismans and love-knots at night, avoiding eyes and shiny things. Thus the condition ties practical advice to cosmological and physical principles.

Key Terms
النيرنج
النيرنجات
جمعية القلب
السلطان القاهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The preference for night practice is merely a cultural or ritual preference without reason.
Correction: Sanusi provides specific spiritual and physical reasons: the sun's dominance over spirits, sensory distraction during the day, and the attractive power of human eyes and sunlight that nullify talismanic force.

Checkpoint
According to Aristotle, why is the heart's concentration more perfect at night?
A) Because the sun's heat is gone.
B) Because the senses are inactive.
C) Because the spirits are stronger.
D) Because the moon aids concentration.

Key Takeaway
Night practice is preferred because the sun's dominance and sensory distractions are minimized, and secrecy protects talismanic power from eyes and sunlight, as taught by Aristotle and Hermes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What distractions during your daily life prevent you from achieving 'جمعية القلب' (concentration of the heart) in your spiritual practices? At night, when the senses are inactive, do you use that time for spiritual work, or do you fill it with other distractions?
?
The passage warns of human eyes attracting talismanic power. In what ways do you seek validation from others' eyes? How might your spiritual practice be weakened by seeking recognition rather than hidden sincerity?
?
Hermes instructs to beware of 'eyes and what shines'. What are the 'shiny' things in your life that attract your attention and distract you from deeper spiritual work? How can you protect your concentration from them?

The Sixth Condition: Devotion to Goodness Perfects Your Work
Author states the sixth condition and its rationale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sixth condition for perfecting spiritual work: that the practitioner's earnest turning to goodness and righteousness directly enhances the perfection of his work, because good is the predominant force in creation.

Core Idea
Goodness is the dominant force; aligning with it strengthens your work.

This passage presents the sixth condition agreed upon by the scholars of spiritual practice. It asserts a direct causal relationship between the practitioner's devotion to good works and the perfection of his practice. The rationale is rooted in the nature of the world: good predominates over evil, so aligning with the stronger side amplifies one's work.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without translating. Then read the literal translation. Notice the key terms: 'إقبال', 'البر', 'الخير', 'الغالب', 'المغلوب'.
The passage is short but dense with meaning.
2
Identify the two main claims
First claim: The more the practitioner turns to goodness, the more perfect his work. Second claim: Because good predominates over evil in the world. Identify these in the Arabic.
3
Connect the condition to its rationale
Ask yourself: Why does turning to goodness make the work more perfect? The answer is cosmological: good is the dominant force. Aligning with it strengthens the work. This is the key insight.
The condition is not just moral advice; it is based on the nature of reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرط السادس : أجمعوا على أن صاحب هذا العمل ، كلما كان إقباله على أبواب البر والخير أكثر أعماله أكمل ، لأن الغالب على طبيعة العالم هو الخير ، وأما الشر فمغلوب ، فإذا اعتضد عمله بالجانب القاهر الغالب ، كان ذلك العمل : أكمل وأفضل
The sixth condition: They all agreed that the practitioner of this work, the more his turning to the doors of righteousness and goodness, the more perfect his works are. Because the predominant over the nature of the world is good, and as for evil, it is overcome. So if his work is strengthened by the overcoming, predominant side, that work is more perfect and better.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage states the sixth condition: the practitioner's devotion (إقبال) to acts of righteousness and goodness (أبواب البر والخير) directly enhances his works. The reason is cosmological: the nature of the world is predominantly good (الخير غالب), while evil (الشر) is overcome (مغلوب). Therefore, if the practitioner aligns his work with the dominant and conquering side (الجانب القاهر الغالب), his work becomes more perfect and better. The condition ties moral virtue to practical efficacy.

Key Terms
البر
الخير
الغالب
المغلوب
الجانب القاهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many think good works are merely rewarded by God but do not directly affect the efficacy of one's spiritual practice.
Correction: The author asserts a causal link: good works strengthen the practitioner's work because they align with the predominant force of good in the world, making the work more perfect.

Checkpoint

A) Because goodness brings divine reward.
B) Good is the predominant force in the world, so aligning with it strengthens the work.
C) Evil is non-existent, so only good works.
D) Because practitioners are inherently good.

Key Takeaway
Aligning one's work with goodness directly enhances its perfection because goodness is the dominant force in the nature of the world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Think of a recent action you did. Did you turn towards the 'doors of righteousness' or away from them? If away, what held you back? Will you make a firm resolve to turn towards goodness now?

Seventh Condition: Dietary Restriction
Author states the seventh condition – avoiding animal food to prevent bodily desires.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the seventh condition restricts animal food and how diet affects spiritual orientation.

Core Idea
Diet controls the soul's attachment to bodily pleasures.

This lesson presents the seventh condition for spiritual practice: abstaining from animal food. The author explains that human souls are inherently drawn to sensory pleasures, and indulging them turns us away from higher spiritual pursuits. Understanding this principle helps us see dietary discipline as a tool for spiritual focus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the direct style: the condition is stated, then the reason is given with a cause-effect relationship.
The phrase 'الجانب الأعلى' refers to the higher spiritual realm.
2
Identify the condition and its scope
The condition forbids eating anything from animals and limits food to bread, salt, and plants. Ask yourself: why specifically animal food? The answer lies in the next step.
3
Understand the reason: the soul's attraction to pleasures
The author explains that human souls (النفوس البشرية) are deeply attached to bodily pleasures. When they obtain such pleasures, they indulge and turn away from the higher side (الجانب الأعلى). Conversely, deprivation turns the soul back to its original innate center (المركز الفطري).
This is a psychological and spiritual principle: fulfillment of desire strengthens attachment; abstinence fosters detachment.
4
Reflect on the practical implication
Consider how this condition aims to maintain spiritual focus. By avoiding rich animal foods, the practitioner reduces sensory stimulation and redirects attention inward. The 'innate center' suggests a natural disposition toward the divine when not clouded by indulgence.
5
Clarify a common misunderstanding
Some might think this condition is about ritual purity. The passage makes clear it is about controlling the soul's inclination toward bodily pleasures, not about impurity. The correction helps us appreciate the psychological depth of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرط السابع : أن لا يأكل من الحيوانات شيئاً ، ويقتصر على الخبز والملح ونبات الأرض. والسبب فيه : أن النفوس البشرية مشغوفة باللذات الجسدانية ، فإذا وصل إليها ، أقبل عليها ، وغاص فيها ، وانصرف عن الجانب الأعلى وإذا لم يجدها وبقي محروماً عنها ، عاد بطبعه إلى الجانب الأصلي والمركز الفطري
The seventh condition: That he eat nothing from animals, and limit himself to bread, salt, and plants of the earth. And the reason for it is that human souls are enamored with bodily pleasures, so if they reach them, they turn to them, plunge into them, and turn away from the higher side. And if they do not find them and remain deprived of them, they return by their nature to the original side and the innate center.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage gives the seventh condition: abstain from animal food, restricting oneself to bread, salt, and plants. The reason: human souls (النفوس البشرية) are deeply attached to bodily pleasures (اللذات الجسدانية). If such pleasures are available, the soul indulges and turns away from the higher (spiritual) realm. If deprived, the soul naturally returns to its original and innate center (المركز الفطري). Thus diet is a tool to control sensory desires and maintain spiritual orientation.

Key Terms
الحيوانات
اللذات الجسدانية
الجانب الأعلى
المركز الفطري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That dietary restriction is about ritual purity rather than controlling the soul's inclination.
Correction: The passage clearly states the reason is the soul's attachment to bodily pleasures, not impurity. The condition aims to prevent distraction from the higher spiritual realm.

Checkpoint

A) It is unhealthy.
B) It is harmful for the talismans.

D) Animals are impure.

Key Takeaway
Dietary restriction helps control the soul's attachment to bodily pleasures, allowing it to return to its natural spiritual orientation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you felt a genuine pull away from spiritual practice because you were preoccupied with a bodily pleasure? What was that pleasure, and how did it affect your relationship with Allah? Will you commit today to a 24-hour fast from that specific pleasure to test the resilience of your soul?
?

Are you willing to experience that discomfort to see if your soul does indeed turn back to its innate center?
?
The author says the soul returns to its original side when deprived. But are you truly willing to let go of a physical comfort to let your soul find its natural orientation? Identify one small dietary sacrifice you can make this week—not for health, but purely to observe the effect on your spiritual focus. Will you do it starting today?

Fifth Condition: Night Practice Is Preferable
Lists the fifth condition with quotes from Aristotle and Hermes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reasoning behind the classical consensus that night practice is superior for certain spiritual or talismanic works, as cited by Aristotle and Hermes.

Core Idea
Night amplifies focus and protects spiritual power from the sun's dominance and human gaze.

This passage continues the conditions for performing certain powerful works. The fifth condition addresses timing: why night is unanimously considered better than day. The author supports this with two ancient authorities, Aristotle and Hermes, each providing distinct reasons—one based on solar dominance and sensory distraction, the other on the vulnerability of talismanic power to sunlight and human eyes. Let's explore their arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice that the passage begins with a consensus statement, then quotes two authorities.
The passage uses the term 'nīranjāt' which refers to talismans or magical objects.
2
Understand Aristotle's reasoning
Aristotle gives two reasons: the sun conquers spirits, and daytime senses distract. Why would these make night better?
This reflects a classical view of solar influence on spiritual activity.
3
Understand Hermes' reasoning
Hermes emphasizes concealment from human eyes and sunlight. According to him, human eyes have spiritual attraction that draws power from talismans, and sunlight nullifies it.
Hermes is a legendary figure associated with hermetic wisdom.
4
Reflect on the practical advice
The passage ends with instructions: perform decisive talismans and desire knots at night, avoiding eyes and shiny things. Consider how this follows from the earlier reasons.
This is a specific application of the condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرط الخامس : اتفقوا على أن ممارسة هذه الأعمال في الليل ، أولى منها في النهار . قال « أرسطو » : ( إن الشمس سلطان قاهر ، فهو بكمال سلطنته يقهر جميع الأرواح ، ولا يقوى شيء منها على الفعل . وأيضاً : الحواس في النهار ، تكون مشغولة بالمحسوسات ، فلا تحصل جمعية القلب ، وفي الليل تكون الحواس معطلة ، فكانت جمعية القلب في الليل أكمل ) . وقال « هرمس » : « إن خير ما يعمل به العامل ، هو ما يخفى عن أعين البشر وشروق الشمس . لأن عيون البشر جاذبة بروحانيتها قوة النيرنج وشروق الشمس قوة تبطل قوة النيرنجات ) ثم قال : اعمل نيرنجات القطعية وعقد الشهوة ، ودخنها كلها بالليل ، واحترز فيها عن العيون واللامعة :
The fifth condition: They agreed that performing these works at night is more appropriate than in the daytime. Aristotle said: 'The sun is a conquering sultan, so by the perfection of its sultanate it conquers all spirits, and none of them has power to act. Also, the senses during the day are occupied with sensible objects, so the concentration of the heart does not occur, while at night the senses are inactive, so the concentration of the heart at night is more complete.' Hermes said: 'Indeed, the best thing a worker works with is what is hidden from the eyes of humans and the rising of the sun. Because the eyes of humans attract, by their spirituality, the power of the talismans, and the rising of the sun is a power that nullifies the power of the talismans.' Then he said: 'Perform the decisive talismans and the knots of desire, and fumigate them all at night, and be cautious in them about eyes and shiny things.'
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth condition for the practice of these astrological or magical works. It begins by stating the consensus of practitioners that performing these works at night is superior to daytime. The author then quotes two authorities, Aristotle and Hermes, to support this. Aristotle's reasoning is twofold: first, the sun as a powerful ruler overcomes all spirits, preventing them from acting; second, during the day the senses are occupied, disrupting heart concentration, whereas at night senses are inactive, allowing better focus. Hermes adds that the best work is hidden from human eyes and sunlight. He explains that human eyes attract the power of talismans (nīranjāt) through their spirituality, and sunlight nullifies that power. Therefore, he advises performing decisive talismans and desire knots at night, avoiding eyes and shiny objects.

نيرنجات
جمعية القلب
روحانيتها

Key Takeaway
Night practice is considered superior because the sun's power and human sensory distractions are absent, allowing undiluted spiritual concentration and protecting talismanic force.

The Sixth Condition: Virtue of the Practitioner
States the sixth condition with its metaphysical justification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sixth condition for the practitioner of spiritual works and why his virtue directly enhances the perfection of his work.

Core Idea
Virtue aligns with the dominant goodness in nature, perfecting the work.

This lesson presents the sixth condition for the practitioner of certain spiritual works. The author states a consensus: the more the practitioner turns toward righteousness and goodness, the more perfect his work becomes. This is grounded in a metaphysical principle about the predominance of goodness over evil in the nature of the world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Notice the concise style and the logical flow from condition to justification.
2
Identify the condition and its justification
The passage states a condition: the practitioner's virtue leads to better work. It then gives a reason: goodness is predominant in the world's nature. Identify these two parts.
The phrase 'لأن الغالب على طبيعة العالم هو الخير' gives the reason.
3
Reflect on the metaphysical principle
Consider the claim that goodness dominates the world and evil is overcome. How does this principle support the condition? The practitioner who aligns with the dominant force (goodness) achieves more perfect work.
This reflects a key kalam view of the world's nature.
4
Apply to your understanding
Think about why moral character is emphasized in spiritual practices. This condition shows that effectiveness is tied to virtue, not just technique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth condition, which concerns the moral character of the practitioner. The consensus is that the more the practitioner turns toward righteousness and goodness, the more perfect his works become. The reason given is that goodness is predominant in the nature of the world, while evil is overcome. Therefore, if the practitioner aligns his work with the dominant side (goodness), his work becomes more complete and superior. This condition emphasizes the importance of virtue for efficacy in these practices.

Eighth Condition: Dignity of Spiritual Matters
Forbids using spiritualities for trivial things and excessive reliance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why spiritual forces must be used only for great purposes and with reverence, and why trivializing them is harmful.

Core Idea
Respect spiritual forces by using them only for worthy purposes.

This condition focuses on the adab (etiquette) required when dealing with spiritualities (al-rūḥāniyyāt). It warns against using them for common or base needs and cautions against constantly turning to them for every desire. The passage sets a clear boundary for their appropriate use, emphasizing respect and moderation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic condition once, then its translation. Notice the direct prohibitions and the reasoning given.
The passage is short but carries two clear rules.
2
Identify the two prohibitions
Find the two things the practitioner is told to avoid: using spiritualities for base things, and returning to them for every desire.
Each prohibition has a reason attached.
3
Reflect on the reasoning
Consider why such actions are forbidden: they resemble bad manners (sū' al-adab) and may lead to destruction (halāk). Ask yourself what kind of 'destruction' is meant.
4
Apply to practice
Think of examples of trivial requests that would violate this condition. How does this condition safeguard the seeker's spiritual journey?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage presents the eighth condition, which concerns the appropriate use of spiritual forces (al-rūḥāniyyāt). The practitioner is instructed not to employ these spiritual entities for base or trivial matters, but only for grand and precious purposes, in a manner suitable to the dignity of both the practitioner and the spiritual being. Moreover, he must avoid constantly resorting to them for every wish, as such behavior is akin to poor etiquette and could result in the seeker's destruction. This condition stresses reverence and moderation.
