The Ninth Condition: Four Requisites for the Practitioner
Enumerates four essential requisites for the practitioner.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four essential qualities required for a practitioner of the spiritual arts as outlined in the ninth condition.

Core Idea
The practitioner's soul needs divine knowledge, cosmology, ethics, and spiritual liveliness.

The author presents the ninth condition in detail, specifying that the practitioner must possess four integrated qualities. These range from theoretical knowledge of divine sciences and astronomy to practical ethics and a responsive spiritual soul. The rarity of combining them all highlights the high standard required.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once through. Then read the translation to grasp the full meaning.
The passage is cut off at the end; focus on the clear enumeration.
2
Identify the four requisites
List the four main qualities: divine sciences, astronomy (with three subparts), ethics, and a living soul.
Notice the logical progression from theory to practice.
3
Understand the reason for each
For each requisite, note why it is important according to the text: divine sciences give unique power, astronomy aids spiritual attraction, ethics purify the soul, and a living soul responds to spiritual realities.
4
Reflect on the rarity of combination
Consider the author's remark that gathering all four in one person is extremely rare. What does that imply about the practitioner?
This connects to the high standards of the craft.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرط التاسع : أن يكون المباشر لهذه الأعمال جامعاً لأمور أربعة : أولها : أن يكون عالماً بالعلوم الإلهية ، متفقهاً فيها . لأنه يحصل للنفس من هذا العلم ، نوع من القوة ، لا يحصل البتة من سائر العلوم. وثانيه : أن يكون عالماً بجميع الأقسام الثلاثة من علم النجوم فالأول : أن يكون عالماً بهيئة السموات والأرض . فإن علمه بذلك ، مما يفيد انجذاب روحانيته إلى الجانب الأعلى . والثاني : أن يكون متيقناً من معرفة الزيجات . حتى يمكنه أن يعرف مواضع الكواكب على الحقيقة . الثالث : أن يكون متبحراً في علم الأحكام ، حتى يمكنه أن يعرف آثار الكواكب، في حالتي البساطة والتركيب . والنوع الثالث من العلوم المهمة لصاحب هذه الصناعة : علم الأخلاق حتى يكون عالماً بأن الأخلاق الفاصلة وأن الأخلاق المذمومة ، ما ؟ فيمكنه تطهير النفس عن الأخلاق المذمومة، وتزيينها بالأخلاق الفاضلة . والنوع الرابع من الأمور المهمة في هذا الباب : أن تكون نفسه نفساً حية لا ميتة والمراد من النفس الحية : النفس التي إذا لاح لها شيء من عالم الروحانيات انبعثت و اشتاقت و اضطرب قلبه وخشعت نفسه . ولما كان اجتماع هذه الأمور الأربعة في الإنسان الواحد، كالنادر ، [ لا
The ninth condition: That the direct doer of these works should combine four matters: First: That he be knowledgeable in the divine sciences, discerning in them. Because from this science, a type of power is obtained for the soul that is not obtained at all from other sciences. Second: That he be knowledgeable in all three divisions of the science of the stars. The first [subdivision]: That he be knowledgeable in the configuration (hay'a) of the heavens and the earth. Indeed, knowledge of that helps attract his spirituality to the higher side. The second: That he be certain in knowledge of the astronomical tables (al-zījāt) so that he can know the positions of the planets in reality. The third: That he be well-versed in the science of astrological judgments (al-aḥkām) so that he can know the effects of the planets in both simplicity and combination. The third type of sciences important for the master of this craft: the science of ethics (al-akhlāq), so that he knows what the separating virtues and the blameworthy ethics are? So that he can purify the soul from blameworthy ethics and adorn it with virtuous ethics. The fourth type of important matters in this chapter: That his soul be a living soul, not dead. And by 'living soul' is meant the soul that, when something from the world of spiritualities appears to it, it becomes excited, yearns, its heart trembles, and its soul becomes humble. And since the gathering of these four matters in one person is as rare [as...]
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage presents the ninth condition, which is the most detailed, listing four essential requisites for the practitioner. The first is knowledge of divine sciences (al-ʿulūm al-ilāhiyya), as it imparts a unique power to the soul not found in other sciences. The second is comprehensive knowledge of astrology (ʿilm al-nujūm) in three subdivisions: (a) knowledge of the configuration of the heavens and earth, which aids spiritual attraction upward, (b) precise knowledge of astronomical tables to determine planetary positions, and (c) deep knowledge of astrological judgments to understand planetary effects in simple and compound configurations. The third is knowledge of ethics (ʿilm al-akhlāq) to distinguish virtuous from blameworthy traits, enabling the purification and adornment of the soul. The fourth is having a 'living soul'—one that responds eagerly and humbly upon glimpsing spiritual realities. The author notes that combining all four in one person is extremely rare, and the passage cuts off mid-sentence.

العلوم الإلهية
علم النجوم
الزيجات
علم الأحكام
علم الأخلاق
النفس الحية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The ninth condition endorses astrology as valid Islamic knowledge.
Correction: The text is descriptively reporting the views of practitioners of these arts, not necessarily endorsing them as part of Islamic theology.

Checkpoint

Required Knowledge for the Practitioner
Razi enumerates required knowledge for practitioners of celestial science.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extensive knowledge Razi deems necessary for one who practices the science of planetary influences, with special emphasis on lunar conditions.

Core Idea
The practitioner must master lunar fortunes, planetary natures, and their associations.

Razi has established the fundamental principle about celestial influences. Now he draws the practical conclusion: the practitioner must possess a vast and detailed knowledge. This passage lists the essential domains of that knowledge, from the natures of planets to their associations with earthly elements, and highlights the moon's conditions as the most critical.

Guided Path
1
Identify the foundational principle
Recognise that Razi begins by referring back to a previously established principle, then derives what the practitioner must know.
The phrase 'إذا عرفت هذا الأصل' signals a conclusion from earlier arguments.
2
List the required knowledge areas
Read through the passage and note each category: natures of wandering planets, fixed stars, mixing them, lunar fortune/misfortune divisions, planetary fortunes/misfortunes, and then detailed attributes and associations.
The passage uses 'يجب أن يكون عالماً' and 'يجب عليه' to mandate each area.
3
Focus on the most important matter
Notice the phrase 'وأهم المهمات عنده' – Razi singles out knowledge of all possible divisions of the moon's fortune and misfortune as the highest priority.
This emphasis on lunar conditions is a key teaching point.
4
Understand the purpose of this knowledge
Razi explains that this knowledge enables the practitioner to choose the appropriate planet and lunar condition for an operation.
The goal is practical application: 'عند الشروع في عمل'.
5
Comprehend the comprehensive scope
The final part extends knowledge to attributes (fortune/misfortune, masculinity/femininity, heat/cold) and associations with minerals, plants, animals, and body parts.
The more thorough the knowledge, the more effective the practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا عرفت هذا الأصل، ظهر أن الشارع في هذا العلم ، يجب أن يكون عالماً بطبائع الكواكب السيارة ، وبطبائع الكواكب الثابتة ، وبكيفية مزج بعضها بالبعض . وأهم المهمات عنده : أن يكون عالماً بجميع الأقسام الممكنة في سعودة القمر ، وفي نحوسيته ، وأن يكون عالماً بجميع سعادات الكواكب ونحوساتها ، حتى إذا أراد الشروع في عمل ؛ أمكنه أن يراعي حال قوة الكوكب المناسب لذلك العمل، ويراعي حال القمر ، حتى يكون موصوفاً بالصفات اللائقة بذلك العمل . إذا عرفت هذا فنقول : يجب عليه الاستقصاء في صفات كل واحد من الكواكب في سعودته ونحوسته ، وذكورته وأنوثته ، وحرارته وبرودته . ويجب عليه الاستقصاء في معرفة ما لكل واحد من الكواكب من أقسام المعادن والنبات والحيوان [ ومن أقسام أعضاء الإنسان والحيوان ] وكلما كان أكثر إحاطة في هذه الأقسام ، كان انتفاعه به أكمل، وقدرته على هذه الأعمال أصدق .
And if you know this principle, it becomes clear that the practitioner in this science must be knowledgeable about the natures of the wandering planets, the natures of the fixed stars, and the manner of mixing some with others. And the most important of matters for him is that he be knowledgeable about all the possible divisions regarding the moon's fortune and its misfortune, and that he be knowledgeable about all the fortunes and misfortunes of the planets, so that when he wishes to begin an operation, he can take into account the state of the strength of the planet suitable for that operation, and take into account the state of the moon, so that it is described with the qualities appropriate for that operation. If you know this, we say: he must thoroughly investigate the attributes of each of the planets regarding its fortune and misfortune, its masculinity and femininity, its heat and cold. And he must thoroughly investigate the knowledge of what each planet has from the categories of minerals, plants, and animals [and from the categories of human and animal organs]. And the more comprehensive he is in these categories, the more complete his benefit from it, and the truer his ability in these operations.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage draws a conclusion from the previous proofs. Since the sun and moon are so important, the practitioner of this science (astrology/astronomy) must have comprehensive knowledge: he must know the natures of all planets (both wandering and fixed), how they mix, and especially all the possible states of the moon's fortune and misfortune. He must also know the fortunes of all planets. When starting an operation, he should consider the strength of the relevant planet and the condition of the moon. Furthermore, he must investigate each planet's attributes (fortune/misfortune, masculinity/femininity, heat/cold) and their associations with minerals, plants, animals, and even human and animal body parts. The more thorough his knowledge, the more accurate and effective his work.

Key Terms
طبائع الكواكب
سعودة القمر
نحوسة
الشارع في هذا العلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that knowledge of planetary natures in general is the most important requirement for the practitioner.
Correction: Razi explicitly states that the most important matter is knowledge of all possible divisions of the moon's fortune and misfortune, not general planetary natures.

Classification of Planets by Qualities and Effects
Razi classifies the seven planets into four groups by temperature, moisture, and benefic/malefic nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi classifies the seven planets into four groups based on their qualities (hot/cold, dry/moist) and their beneficial or harmful nature.

Core Idea
Planets are classified by qualities and effects—each group has a distinct signature.

Razi presents a compact but essential classification used in astrological practice. Understanding these groupings is crucial for interpreting planetary influences. In this passage, he organizes the seven wandering planets into four categories, noting both their elemental qualities and their tendencies toward good or harm.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the rhythm of the four groups.
The passage uses parallel structure for each group.
2
Identify the four groups
Find the four pairs/triplets of planets and note their assigned qualities: hot-dry, hot-moist, cold-moist, cold-dry.
3
Note the benefic/malefic distinction
Within each group, observe which planets are beneficial (مصلح) and which are harmful (مفسد). The Sun and Jupiter are beneficial; Mars and Saturn are harmful; etc.
This distinction is key for practical astrology.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself why this classification matters. It helps astrologers determine planetary influences based on elemental qualities and their good or bad effects.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما السيارات : فنقول : الشمس والمريخ حاران يابسان ، لكن الشمس بحرها ويبسها مصلحة والمريخ مفسد . وأما المشتري والرأس ، فهما حاران رطبان ، لكن المشتري في غاية الصلاح، والرأس ليس كذلك . وأما الزهرة والقمر فهما باردان رطبان ، لكن إصلاح الزهرة أكثر . وأما زحل وعطارد والذنب ، فهي باردة يابسة ، إلا أن عطارد مصلح ، وزحل والذنب مفسدان .
As for the wandering planets, we say: the sun and Mars are hot and dry, but the sun's heat and dryness are beneficial, while Mars is harmful. As for Jupiter and the Head (of the dragon), they are hot and moist, but Jupiter is extremely beneficial, while the Head is not so. As for Venus and the moon, they are cold and moist, but Venus's beneficence is greater. As for Saturn, Mercury, and the Tail (of the dragon), they are cold and dry, except that Mercury is beneficial, while Saturn and the Tail are harmful.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage classifies the seven planets of traditional astrology into four groups based on their primary qualities (hot/cold, dry/moist) and their beneficial or harmful effects. The first group: Sun and Mars are hot and dry, but the Sun is beneficial whereas Mars is harmful. The second group: Jupiter and the Head (ascending lunar node) are hot and moist; Jupiter is very beneficial, the Head less so. The third group: Venus and the moon are cold and moist; Venus is more beneficial. The fourth group: Saturn, Mercury, and the Tail (descending node) are cold and dry; Mercury is beneficial, Saturn and the Tail harmful. This classification is essential for the practitioner choosing appropriate times and planets for operations.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The qualities 'hot' and 'cold' refer to physical temperature.
Correction: In astrology, 'hot' and 'cold' are symbolic qualities related to elemental nature, not literal temperature.

Fixed Stars and the Color Method
Razi presents the difficulty and the first method by color.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why knowing the natures of fixed stars is considered difficult and how the first method—deducing from colors—works.

Core Idea
A star's color reveals its nature by matching a known planet.

When looking at the night sky, the fixed stars appear as points of light. But how can we know what they are made of or what influences they have? Razi explains that this is no easy task, but one clue lies in their color. By comparing a star's color to that of a wandering planet, scholars could assign a nature to it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice that the passage acknowledges difficulty before presenting the method.
The text is cut off, but the core idea is clear.
2
Identify the key claim
Identify what makes knowing the natures of fixed stars difficult. Why might it be harder than for planets?
3
Understand the color method
See how the method works: if a fixed star's color matches a planet's color, then its nature is considered similar. Think of examples: a reddish star like Aldebaran might be compared to Mars.
This is an astrological correspondence, not a physical one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الثوبت : فلا شك أن معرفة طبائعها صعبة وذكروا في طريق تحصيل هذه المعرفة وجوهاً : الطريق الأول : الاستدلال بألوانها على طبائعها . فكل كوكب يكون لونه مساوياً للون بعض السيارات ، أضافوا طبعه
As for the fixed stars, there is no doubt that knowing their natures is difficult. And they mentioned ways for acquiring this knowledge: The first way: deducing their natures from their colors. So every star whose color is equal to the color of some wandering planet, they assigned its nature (to that planet) ...
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage introduces a new topic: the fixed stars (al-thawābit). It acknowledges that knowing their natures is difficult. Then it mentions that there are multiple methods (wujuh), and presents the first method: inferring their natures from their colors. If a fixed star's color matches that of a known wandering planet, then that star is assigned the same nature as that planet. The text is cut off, but the idea is clear: color is an indicator of elemental composition and astrological influence.

Al-Razi's Classification of Planetary Natures
Al-Razi classifies planets by elemental qualities and moral effects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Razi classifies planets according to their elemental qualities (hot/cold, dry/moist) and their beneficial or harmful effects.

Core Idea
Planets are grouped by heat and moisture, but not all share the same moral effect.

In this passage, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi presents a detailed classification of the seven planets (including the sun, moon, and lunar nodes) based on their elemental qualities—hot/cold, dry/moist—and their beneficial or harmful nature. This reflects the intricate cosmology of the time, where celestial bodies were thought to influence earthly events. As you read, pay attention to how the same elemental combination can yield different moral effects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without dissecting it. Then read the translation to grasp the overall classification.
Notice that al-Razi uses pairs and triplets.
2
Identify the four categories
Al-Razi groups the planets into four sets based on elemental qualities (hot/cold, dry/moist). Find each group and note which planets belong.
3
Note the moral effect for each planet
For each planet, check whether al-Razi says it is muslih (beneficial) or mufsid (harmful). Some planets in the same elemental group have opposite effects.
4
Reflect on the pattern
Ask yourself: why are the sun and Mars both hot/dry but one is beneficial and the other harmful? What does this teach about al-Razi's approach?
This connects to the idea that each planet has its own specific nature beyond generic elements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما السيارات : فنقول : الشمس والمريخ حاران يابسان ، لكن الشمس بحرها ويبسها مصلحة والمريخ مفسد . وأما المشتري والرأس ، فهما حاران رطبان ، لكن المشتري في غاية الصلاح، والرأس ليس كذلك . وأما الزهرة والقمر فهما باردان رطبان ، لكن إصلاح الزهرة أكثر . وأما زحل وعطارد والذنب ، فهي باردة يابسة ، إلا أن عطارد مصلح ، وزحل والذنب مفسدان
As for the planets: we say: The sun and Mars are hot and dry, but the sun, in its heat and dryness, is beneficial, and Mars is harmful. As for Jupiter and the Head (Ras), they are hot and moist, but Jupiter is extreme in goodness, and the Head is not so. As for Venus and the moon, they are cold and moist, but the beneficence of Venus is greater. As for Saturn, Mercury, and the Tail (Dhanab), they are cold and dry, except that Mercury is beneficial, and Saturn and the Tail are harmful.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the seven planets (including the sun and moon, and the lunar nodes) according to their elemental qualities and moral effect. Al-Razi groups them into four pairs/triplets. First: the sun and Mars both hot and dry, but the sun's qualities are beneficial while Mars's are harmful. Second: Jupiter and the Head (the ascending lunar node) both hot and moist, but Jupiter is supremely beneficial while the Head is not. Third: Venus and the moon both cold and moist, with Venus being more beneficial. Fourth: Saturn, Mercury, and the Tail (the descending lunar node) are cold and dry, but Mercury is beneficial whereas Saturn and the Tail are harmful. The classification shows a nuanced view: not all hot/dry or cold/moist are alike; the specific nature and whether they are good or evil depend on the individual planet.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi classifies planets not only by elemental qualities but also by their specific beneficial or harmful effects, showing that identical elemental combinations can produce different moral outcomes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

What concrete step will you take this week to avoid lumping others into simplistic categories?
?
The sun is hot and dry yet beneficial. Consider a difficult or 'hot' trial in your life. Could it be that Allah is using it for your benefit, even if it seems harsh? How can you discern its specific purpose rather than assuming all hardships are purely harmful? What prayer or action can you offer to shift your perspective to that of a student seeking wisdom?
?
Al-Razi distinguishes between beneficial and harmful planets that share elemental qualities. In your daily judgments, do you often equate similar appearances with similar outcomes? Reflect on a time you misjudged someone based on a superficial resemblance. How can this lesson inspire you to seek deeper understanding before forming opinions? Will you ask Allah for insight before judging?

The Celestial Sphere Divided into Halves
Introduces first type of celestial division: halves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first type of celestial division: the sphere divided into halves in four different ways.

Core Idea
The celestial sphere is first divided into halves in four complementary pairs.

The author begins by stating that astrologers divided the celestial sphere into many types. The first type is the division into halves, which they considered in four distinct ways. This lesson explains that fundamental classification.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage from 'أعلم أنهم قسموا الفلك' to 'ما تحت الأرض'. Notice the concise enumeration.
2
Identify the four divisions
Find the four ways to divide the sphere into halves: east-west, north-south, ascending-descending, above-below.
Each pair represents a fundamental axis.
3
Understand the reasoning
Ask why astrologers would need these divisions. They provide a framework for interpreting celestial influences from different perspectives.
4
Connect to broader classification
This is the first of three types. Note that later divisions build on this halving concept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنوع الثالث : النقط التي تنتهي التسييرات إليها ، وقد اتفقوا على أن لها أيضاً آثار قوية . أعلم أنهم قسموا الفلك إلى أنواع كثيرة : فالنوع الأول : قسمته نصفين. وقد اعتبروا هذا النوع في القسمة على وجوه كثيرة منها : الأول : إن أحد نصفي الفلك شرقي والثاني غربي . والثاني : إن أحد نصفيه شمالي والثاني جنوبي . والثالث : الصاعد والهابط . والرابع : ما فوق الأرض وما تحتها . والنوع الثاني : قسمة الفلك إلى أربعة أقسام : الربيعي والصيفي والخريفي والشتوي. وذلك لأنهم وجدوا السنة تنقسم إلى الفصول الأربعة ، بسبب حصول الشمس في الأرباع الأربعة من الفلك ، فلا جرم قسموا أدوار الفلك بأربعة أقسام . ثم لما رأوا لكل فصل أولاً ووسطاً ونهاية : قسموا كل ربع إلى ثلاثة أقسام ، فالقسم الأول دور الفلك بأثني عشر قسماً . والقسم الثاني : أن الشيء الذي يحدث بعد العدم ، أو يظهر بعد الخفاء ، كالولد الذي ينفصل عن بطن الأم ، لابد وأن يطلع في تلك اللحظة درجة معينة من الفلك . فتلك الدرجة لما ظهرت بعد الخفاء ، كانت مشابهة لأحوال ذلك الولد الذي ظهر بعد الخفاء ، فجعلوا تلك الدرجة دليلاً على أحوال ذلك الحادث، ثم قسموا أدوار الفلك من تلك النقطة بأثني عشر قسماً . وهي البيوت الموجودة في صورة الطالع . والقسم الثالث : أنهم قسموا الفلك إلى المثلثات الأربعة وهي المثلثة : النارية والأرضية والهوائية والمائية . والنوع الثالث : قسمة كل برج إلى أقسام كثيرة . وهذا يقع على وجوه : الأول : قسمة البروج على منازل القمر . ويجب البحث عن خاصية كل واحد من تلك المنازل . لأن لها قوة شديدة في تركيب الأعمال السحرية . والثاني : معرفة بيوت الكواكب . والثالث : معرفة أشراف الكواكب . والرابع : الحدود، وهي قسمة كل برج بأقسام معينة ، وتخصيص كل واحد منها بكوكب معين . والخامس : الوجوه . والسادس : الذريحانات . والسابع : الاثنا عشريات . والثامن : النهبهرات . والتاسع : المفرح . العاشر : الحيز . والحادي عشر : الدستورية . والثاني عشر : الأقسام المذكرة والمؤنثة .
And the third type: the points to which the directions end, and they agreed that they also have strong effects. Know that they divided the celestial sphere into many types. The first type: its division into halves. They considered this type of division in many ways, including: first, one half of the sphere is eastern and the second is western; second, one half is northern and the second is southern; third, the ascending and the descending; fourth, what is above the earth and what is below it. The second type: division of the sphere into four sections: spring, summer, autumn, and winter. That is because they found the year divided into four seasons due to the sun's position in the four quarters of the sphere, so they divided the revolutions of the sphere into four sections. Then when they saw for each season a beginning, middle, and end, they divided each quarter into three sections, so the first section is the revolution of the sphere into twelve parts. And the second section: that a thing that occurs after non-existence, or appears after concealment, like a child that separates from the womb, inevitably at that moment a specific degree of the sphere rises. That degree, having appeared after concealment, resembles the states of that child that appeared after concealment, so they made that degree an indication of the states of that event. Then they divided the revolutions of the sphere from that point into twelve parts, which are the houses in the figure of the ascendant. And the third section: that they divided the sphere into four triplicities, which are the triplicities: fiery, earthly, airy, and watery. And the third type: the division of each zodiac sign into many parts. This occurs in ways: first, the division of the signs according to the lunar mansions; they must investigate the property of each of those mansions because they have strong power in composing magical works. Second, knowledge of the planetary houses. Third, knowledge of the exaltations of the planets. Fourth, the terms, which is the division of each sign into specific parts and the assignment of each to a specific planet. Fifth, the faces. Sixth, the decans. Seventh, the duodecatemories. Eighth, the [nahbaharat?] places. Ninth, the joyful. Tenth, the bound. Eleventh, the authoritative. Twelfth, the masculine and feminine divisions.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is a classification of celestial divisions used by astrologers. It begins by mentioning a third type related to points where directions end, which have strong effects, then proceeds to enumerate three main types of divisions of the celestial sphere (al-falak). The first type is division into halves (nisfayn) in four ways: east-west, north-south, ascending-descending, and above-below. The second type is division into four seasonal quarters (arbaʿ aqsām: spring, summer, autumn, winter) because the sun passes through four quadrants. Each quarter is further divided into three parts (start, middle, end) giving twelve parts; another division emerges from the degree rising at birth for a new event, and also from four triplicities (fire, earth, air, water). The third type divides each zodiac sign (burj) into many parts, listing twelve specific subdivisions: lunar mansions, planetary houses, exaltations, terms, faces, decans, duodecatemories, and others. The passage is descriptive, outlining the astrological framework.

Key Terms
فلك
نصف
شرقي
غربي
شمالي
جنوبي
صاعد
هابط
فوق الأرض
تحت الأرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These halves are the same as astronomical hemispheres like northern and southern.
Correction: These divisions are astrological conventions based on orientation, motion, and visibility, not purely astronomical.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many ways of dividing the sphere into halves are mentioned?
A) 2
B) 3
C) 4
D) 5

Key Takeaway
The first type of celestial division splits the sphere into halves in four key ways: east-west, north-south, ascending-descending, and above-below.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Just as the celestial sphere is divided into halves by different axes, consider the halves in your own life: the visible and the hidden, the times of ascent and descent. Which axis have you neglected to examine? How will you begin to give it your attention today?
?
The passage lists four ways to divide the sphere: east-west, north-south, ascending-descending, above-below. Which of these pairs most resonates with a current struggle in your spiritual state? Take a moment to write down one concrete step you will take to realign yourself.
?
The division into halves requires a reference point—each pair is seen from a different perspective. What is the reference point you use to judge the 'halves' of your own character? Have you considered that your perspective might be incomplete, and that what you see as 'above' might be 'below' from another angle? How will you seek a fuller view?

The Seasonal Quarters and Further Subdivisions
Describes second type: seasonal quarters and their subdivisions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second type of celestial division: into four seasons, each further divided into three parts, along with the ascendant houses and four triplicities.

Core Idea
The year's four seasons lead to quarters; each quarter splits into three, yielding twelve sections, plus ascendant houses and triplicities.

The second type of division is based on the sun's annual path through the four seasons. Astrologers then subdivided each quarter into three parts, giving twelve sections, and also used the degree rising at a birth to define twelve houses. They also recognized four triplicities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on second type
Read from 'والنوع الثاني' to 'المائية'. Note the three distinct sections.
2
Understand the seasonal division
The sphere is divided into four quarters corresponding to spring, summer, autumn, winter because of the sun's motion.
This is the base division.
3
Identify the three subdivisions of each quarter
Each quarter has a beginning, middle, end, so each quarter is split into three, totaling twelve parts. This is the first section.
4
Learn about the ascendant houses
The degree rising at a birth divides the sphere into twelve houses from that point, representing different life areas.
This is the second section.
5
Recognize the four triplicities
The sphere is also divided into four triplicities based on elements: fire, earth, air, water.
This is the third section.

And the second section: that a thing that occurs after non-existence, or appears after concealment, like a child that separates from the womb, inevitably at that moment a specific degree of the sphere rises. That degree, having appeared after concealment, resembles the states of that child that appeared after concealment, so they made that degree an indication of the states of that event. Then they divided the revolutions of the sphere from that point into twelve parts, which are the houses in the figure of the ascendant. And the third section: that they divided the sphere into four triplicities, which are the triplicities: fiery, earthly, airy, and watery. And the third type: the division of each zodiac sign into many parts. This occurs in ways: first, the division of the signs according to the lunar mansions; they must investigate the property of each of those mansions because they have strong power in composing magical works. Second, knowledge of the planetary houses. Third, knowledge of the exaltations of the planets. Fourth, the terms, which is the division of each sign into specific parts and the assignment of each to a specific planet. Fifth, the faces. Sixth, the decans. Seventh, the duodecatemories. Eighth, the [nahbaharat?] places. Ninth, the joyful. Tenth, the bound. Eleventh, the authoritative. Twelfth, the masculine and feminine divisions.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is a classification of celestial divisions used by astrologers. It begins by mentioning a third type related to points where directions end, which have strong effects, then proceeds to enumerate three main types of divisions of the celestial sphere (al-falak). The first type is division into halves (nisfayn) in four ways: east-west, north-south, ascending-descending, and above-below. The second type is division into four seasonal quarters (arbaʿ aqsām: spring, summer, autumn, winter) because the sun passes through four quadrants. Each quarter is further divided into three parts (start, middle, end) giving twelve parts; another division emerges from the degree rising at birth for a new event, and also from four triplicities (fire, earth, air, water). The third type divides each zodiac sign (burj) into many parts, listing twelve specific subdivisions: lunar mansions, planetary houses, exaltations, terms, faces, decans, duodecatemories, and others. The passage is descriptive, outlining the astrological framework.

Correction: They are related but not identical; the twelve parts here are based on seasons, not the ecliptic constellations.

Lists twelve subdivisions of each zodiac sign

Core Idea
Each zodiac sign is subdivided into twelve different astrological systems.

The third type of celestial division focuses on subdividing each of the twelve zodiac signs into numerous smaller units. The passage lists twelve such subdivisions, each with its own astrological significance.

This is the only one elaborated upon.

The Fourth Type of Zodiac Division: Thirty Degrees and Ancient Narrations
Describes the fourth type of zodiac division into 30 degrees and cites three ancient narrations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth type of zodiac division into thirty degrees and the three ancient narrations that describe the properties and rituals associated with those degrees.

Core Idea
Ancient astrologers divided each zodiac sign into thirty degrees with specific properties and rituals.

This passage presents a classification of astrological knowledge, specifically the fourth type concerning the division of the zodiac into thirty degrees. It then enumerates three ancient narrations that describe the natures and effects of those degrees. These sources—from Ṭamṭam al-Hindī, Zoroaster, and the Babylonians—show the diversity of astrological traditions inherited by Islamic scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the literal translation to grasp the content. Notice the structure: it begins with the division and then lists three narrations.
The passage is straightforward and descriptive, not argumentative.
2
Identify the three narrations
The text explicitly names three narrations. Find each one: from Ṭamṭam al-Hindī, from Zardusht (Zoroaster), and from the Babylonians. Observe that each is introduced with 'الرواية الأولى/الثانية/الثالثة'.
3
Understand the first narration in detail
The first narration provides specific properties, names, incense, and effects for each degree. It also describes a ritual: when the sun enters a degree, one must burn incense and invoke the lord of that degree by name. This shows the practical astrological tradition of Ṭamṭam al-Hindī.
The other two narrations are briefly mentioned without details in this passage.
4
Reflect on the historical context
Consider that this passage is from an Islamic theological work (Al-Matalib al-Aliyah). It is likely recording these traditions for reference, not endorsing them. Understanding this helps avoid misinterpretation.
The common misunderstanding is to think the author believes in these practices; rather, he is describing them neutrally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنوع الرابع : قسمة البروج إلى ثلاثين درجة . ومعرفة طبائع تلك الدرجات وآثارها وكيفياتها . وللقدماء فيها روايات : إحداها : ما يروى عن طمطم الهندي ) فإنه يذكر لكل درجة خاصيتها وأسماءها وبخورها وأثرها . فإذا نزلت الشمس في تلك الدرجة ، وجب التبخير ، بذلك البخور ، ودعا صاحب تلك الدرجة بذلك الاسم ، وطلب ذلك الأثر منه . والرواية الثانية : خواص تلك الدرجات [ بحسب ما هو منقول عن و زردشت ) . والرواية الثالثة : خواصها (۱) ] بحسب ما هو منقول عن البابليين
And the fourth type: the division of the zodiac into thirty degrees. And knowledge of the natures of those degrees, their effects, and their qualities. And the ancients have narrations concerning them: One of them: what is related from Ṭamṭam al-Hindī, for he mentions for each degree its specific property, its names, its incense, and its effect. So when the sun enters that degree, incense must be burned with that incense, and one calls upon the lord of that degree by that name, and requests that effect from him. And the second narration: the properties of those degrees according to what is transmitted from Zardusht. And the third narration: their properties according to what is transmitted from the Babylonians.

Commentary
This passage presents a classification of astrological knowledge, specifically the fourth type concerning the division of the zodiac into thirty degrees, and the knowledge of the natures and effects of those degrees. It then enumerates three ancient narrations that describe these properties. The second narration is from Zoroaster (Zardusht), and the third from the Babylonians. The passage is a straightforward listing of sources, not a critique or theological analysis, but it shows the diversity of astrological traditions inherited by Islamic scholarship.

First Way of Dividing the Zodiac: Seasonal and Qualitative Reasoning
Presents the first way of dividing the zodiac into twelve signs based on seasons, cardinal points, and qualities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the zodiac was divided into twelve signs based on seasons and qualitative principles, and the reasoning behind assigning hot/cold/dry/moist natures to the cardinal signs and ordering the signs in alternating triads.

Core Idea
The zodiac division mirrors seasonal transitions and balances active and passive qualities.

This passage from al-Matalib al-Aliyah presents the first way of dividing the celestial sphere into twelve zodiacal signs. It begins with the observation that the year has four seasons, each with a beginning, middle, and end, leading to twelve parts. Then it explains how the intersection of the celestial equator and ecliptic defines equinoctial and solstitial points, which are assigned hot and cold natures based on their relation to equilibrium and excess. The text further argues for the precedence of dryness over moisture, and uses the seasonal transitions to assign natures to Aries, Libra, Cancer, and Capricorn. Finally, it introduces a dynamic principle that heat and cold must alternate to avoid extremes, while dryness and moisture should be grouped in pairs, resulting in a specific order of signs repeated in three groups of four.

Guided Path
1
Understand the seasonal basis
Read how the division into twelve arises from the four seasons each having three parts. This is the foundation.
The year's division into seasons is directly tied to the sun's motion.
2
Identify the cardinal points
Focus on the equinoctial points (Aries, Libra) and solstitial points (Cancer, Capricorn) and why equinoxes are considered nobler.
Equilibrium is valued over excess.
3
Learn the assignment of qualities
Note how heat, cold, dryness, and moisture are assigned to the four cardinal signs based on seasonal transitions.
Aries gets hot-dry, Libra hot-moist, etc.
4
Grasp the active-passive dynamics
Understand the rule that heat and cold (active) must alternate, while dryness and moisture (passive) come in pairs to avoid nullification.
This determines the order of signs in the zodiac.
5
Apply the pattern to all signs
See how the same pattern of four signs (hot-dry, cold-dry, hot-moist, cold-moist) repeats for the second and third groups of four signs.
The entire zodiac is structured by this qualitative logic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث في معرفة طبيعة الفلك : وانفقوا على قسمة الفلك من وجوه كثيرة : فالوجه الأول : قسمة الفلك باثني عشر قسماً . والسبب الأقوى فيه : أن الناس وجدوا السنة تنقسم إلى الفصول الأربعة بسبب حصول الشمس في الأرباع الأربعة من الفلك . فلهذا السبب قموا دور الفلك بأربعة أقام . ثم وجدوا لكل فصل من الفصول الأربعة : أولاً ووسطاً ونهاية ، فلا جرم ، صار دون الفلك مقسوماً باثني عشر فسماً . واعلم : أن هذا التقسيم يقع على وجهين : الأول : أن يعتبر حاله بسبب البروج. واعلم : أن بسبب تقاطع منطقة الفلك الأعظم ، ومنطقة البروج ؛ حصل نقطتان عليهما التقاطع . وهما نقطتا : الحمل والميزان . ونقطتان هما فاينا المباينة. وهما نقطتا : السرطان والجدي. والاعتدال أشرف من الإفراط ، فنقطتا التقاطع، أشرف من نقطتي الانقلاب. والحرارة أشرف من البرودة ، فجعلوا نقطتي الاعتدال حارتين ، ونقطتي الانقلاب باردتين . ثم إن اليبوسة أفضل من الرطوبة . لأن اليبوسة عبارة عن المنع من الانفعال، والرطوبة عبارة : عن الانفعال . فاليبوسة أشرف من الرطوبة . و معلوم : أن عند انتقال الشمس إلى الحمل ، ينتقل الزمان من الشتاء إلى الربيع ، فتحدث لكلية العالم : الحياة والبهجة . وعند انتقال الشمس من السنبلة إلى الميزان ، ينتقل الزمان من الصيف إلى الخريف ، وهو انتقال من الكمال إلى النقصان . فالحمل أشرف من الميزان . فلا جرم جعلوا الحمل حاراً يابساً ، والميزان حاراً رطباً . والجدي أشرف من السرطان ، لان عند انتقال الشمس من الجوزاء إلى السرطان، تأخذ في الهبوط ، ونقصان النهار ، وزيادة الليل ، وعند الانتقال من القوس إلى الجدي، تنتقل الشمس من الهبوط إلى الصعود ، ومن غاية انتقاص النهار إلى ازدياده . فالجدي أفضل من السرطان. فلهذا جعلوا الجدي بارداً يابساً . والسرطان بارداً رطباً . فصارت طبائع هذه البروج الأربعة : معلومة ثم نقول : الحرارة والبرودة فاعلتان . واليبوسة والرطوبة منفعلتان . والفاعل قوي ، والمنفعل ضعيف ، فلو توالى حاران ، أو باردان ، لعظم التسخين أو التبريد ، ولهلك العالم . فوجب أن يحصل برج حار ، ثم برج بارد ، ثم حار ، ثم بارد ، وأما المنفعلتان ، فلو حصل يابس ثم رطب ، لاعتدل كل واحد منهما بالآخر ، ولبطل تأثير كل واحد منها ، فالأصوب أن يحصل يابان ، ثم رطبان . وهكذا على الترتيب . وإذا ظهرت هذه المقدمات ، وجب أن يكون الأول حاراً يابساً ، والثاني بارد يابساً ، والثالث حاراً رطباً، والرابع بارداً رطباً . وكذا القول في الأربعة الثانية والثالثة
The third section on knowing the nature of the sphere: And they agreed on the division of the sphere from many aspects. So the first aspect: the division of the sphere into twelve parts. And the strongest reason for it is that people found the year to be divided into four seasons due to the sun's presence in the four quarters of the sphere. For this reason they made the cycle of the sphere into four parts. Then they found for each of the four seasons a beginning, a middle, and an end, so inevitably the sphere became divided into twelve parts. And know that this division occurs in two ways: the first: that one considers its state by means of the signs. And know that due to the intersection of the plane of the great sphere and the plane of the signs, two points of intersection occur. They are the points of Aries and Libra. And two points are the points of extreme divergence. They are the points of Cancer and Capricorn. And equilibrium is nobler than excess, so the two points of intersection are nobler than the two points of solstice. And heat is nobler than cold, so they made the two equinoctial points hot, and the two solstitial points cold. Then dryness is better than moisture, because dryness is the prevention of passivity, and moisture is passivity. So dryness is nobler than moisture. And it is known that when the sun moves to Aries, the season moves from winter to spring, and life and joy occur for the whole world. And when the sun moves from Virgo to Libra, the season moves from summer to autumn, and it is a transition from perfection to deficiency. So Aries is nobler than Libra. So inevitably they made Aries hot and dry, and Libra hot and moist. And Capricorn is nobler than Cancer, because when the sun moves from Gemini to Cancer, it begins to descend, the day decreases, and the night increases, and when moving from Sagittarius to Capricorn, the sun moves from descent to ascent, and from the utmost decrease of day to its increase. So Capricorn is better than Cancer. So for this they made Capricorn cold and dry, and Cancer cold and moist. So the natures of these four signs become known. Then we say: Heat and cold are active, and dryness and moisture are passive. The active is strong, the passive is weak. If two hot [signs] or two cold [signs] were consecutive, the heating or cooling would be extreme, and the world would perish. So it was necessary that there be a hot sign, then a cold sign, then hot, then cold. As for the two passive [qualities], if a dry [sign] then a moist [sign] occurred consecutively, each would be balanced by the other, and the effect of each would be nullified. So the most correct is that there be two dry [signs], then two moist [signs], and so on in order. And when these premises are clear, it is necessary that the first be hot and dry, the second cold and dry, the third hot and moist, the fourth cold and moist. And likewise for the second and third groups of four.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage presents the first way of dividing the sphere into twelve parts, the method based on the seasons and the qualities of the signs. It begins by stating that the division of the sphere into twelve is agreed upon, and the strongest reason is that the year has four seasons, each with a beginning, middle, and end, giving twelve parts. Then it notes that the division can be considered in terms of the zodiacal signs. It discusses the two equinoctial points (Aries and Libra) and the two solstitial points (Cancer and Capricorn), asserting that equilibrium is nobler than excess, and heat is nobler than cold, so the equinoctial signs are assigned heat and the solstitial signs cold. It then argues that dryness is better than moisture because dryness resists passivity. Based on the seasonal transitions, Aries is associated with life and joy, Libra with decline, so Aries is hot-dry and Libra hot-moist. Capricorn is associated with ascent of the sun, Cancer with descent, so Capricorn is cold-dry and Cancer cold-moist. This establishes the natures of the four cardinal signs. Next, the text introduces a dynamic principle: heat and cold are active, dryness and moisture passive. To avoid extreme heating or cooling from two hot or two cold signs in succession, hot and cold must alternate. For the passive qualities, two dry signs in a row would neutralize each other's effect, so it is better to have two dry then two moist. Applying these premises, the order of the first four signs is determined: first hot-dry (Aries), second cold-dry (Taurus), third hot-moist (Gemini), fourth cold-moist (Cancer). The same pattern applies to the second group of four (Leo, Virgo, Libra, Scorpio) and the third group (Sagittarius, Capricorn, Aquarius, Pisces).

بروج
فصول
اعتدال
انقلاب
حرارة
برودة
يبوسة
رطوبة
فاعل
منفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This is purely astrological rather than a philosophical/theological reasoning about celestial order.
Correction: The passage uses qualitative physics (active/passive) to explain sign natures, reflecting medieval cosmological reasoning, not predictive astrology.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the effect if two hot signs or two cold signs were consecutive?
A) The world would become balanced
B) The world would perish
C) The seasons would be disrupted
D) There would be no effect

Key Takeaway
The zodiac's twelve signs are derived from seasonal divisions and qualitative balances, with active qualities alternating and passive qualities grouped in pairs to maintain cosmic equilibrium.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Reflect on a relationship or responsibility in your life: are you taking on too much of an active role, leaving no room for others to act? Or are you too passive, letting circumstances dictate your faith? What does this cosmic principle teach you about your own posture before Allah?

How might this awareness affect your trust in Allah's decree during times of apparent chaos?

The Second Division of the Zodiac: Astrological Houses
Describes the second way of dividing the zodiac into twelve houses based on the ascendant, with meanings for four principal houses and two additional.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classification of the twelve astrological houses based on the ascendant, as described in Al-Matalib al-Aliyah.

Core Idea
The astrological houses are determined by analogy between celestial positions and earthly life.

This passage presents the second method of dividing the zodiac into twelve parts: the astrological houses derived from the ascendant. The author explains the meanings and significations of the four principal houses and two additional houses linked by trine, using analogical reasoning. Although this material is part of a critique of astrology, it is important to understand the system being described.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
Recognize that this is a description of astrological beliefs, not an endorsement. The author is explaining the system he criticizes elsewhere.
2
Identify the four principal houses
Note the ascendant (1st), 4th, 7th, and 10th houses and their meanings as explained.
3
Understand the analogical methodology
See how the author explains each house by similarity to earthly matters (e.g., ascendant like birth).
4
Examine the fifth and ninth houses
Note how they are connected by trine, and their different significations due to position above or below earth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الثاني : في قسمة الفلك باثني عشر قسماً : القسمة المبنية على الطالع . وما رأيت لأحد في تعيين هذه البيوت : عملة مناسبة . والذي حصلته أن نقول : إن أربعة منها : وهي الطالع والرابع والسابع والعاشر . أما الطالع فإنه يدل على الابتداء في كل شيء . ويقال له : بيت الحياة والنفس . والسبب فيه : أن درجة الطالع ظهرت بعد الخفاء، كما أن الولد ظهر في هذا العالم بعد الخفاء ، فلما حصلت المشابهة بينهما من هذا الوجه ، لا جرم جعل الطالع دليلا عليه واعلم : أن البرهان الأعظم في علم النجوم : هو كون أحدهما مشابها للآخر من بعض الوجوه وأما الوتد الثاني وهو الرابع فإنه وتد الأرض ، لأجل أنه تحت الأرض . وله صفات : أحدها : أنه وتد الأرض ، يشبه الأصل الذي منه يظهر الطالع ، ومنه يتولد فلا جرم جعل دليلاً على الأباء والأجداد ، ومشايخ أهل البيت . وثانيها : أنهم نسبوا الأملاك والعقارات إليه . وثالثها : أنه لما كان في غاية الخفاء ، نسبوا إليه عواقب الأمور ، لكن العواقب تخفية غير معلومة . وأما الوند الثالث : وهو السابع. فهو بيت مقابل للطالع ، وهو يدل على المقابل . فلهذا يقال : إنه بيت الأضداد والشركاء والأزواج . وأما الوتد الرابع ، وهو العاشر ، فهو أرفع بيت في الفلك فلهذا يقال : إنه بيت للسلطان والقوة. ولما كان العاشر مسابع والرابع ، وكان الرابع دليلا على الأباء ، كان العاشر دليلاً على الأمهات. فهذا هو الحكم على هذه البيوت الأربعة واعلم : أنه حصل بيتان أخوان ينظر الطالع إليهما من التثليث . وهذا النظر يفيد كمال المحبة والخير، وهما الخامس والتاسع ، لكن الخامس تحت الأرض ، والتاسع فوق الأرض . والذي يكون تحت الأرض أقل شرفاً مما يكون فوق الأرض . والجسماني أقل طرقاً من الروحاني ، والأشرف منسوب إلى الأشرف ، فلا جرم جعلوا الخامس دليلاً على ما يفيد الفرج ، بسبب الروحانيات ، فصار الخامس بيت الأولاد والرسل والأخيار والهدايا وغلة البضائع ، وصار التاسع بيت الدين والنبوة والعلم والأفعال الصائبة ، وهو أيضاً بيت الاسفار الطويلة . إلا أن هذه الأسفار قد تفيد المنافع العظيمة ، وتفيد تهذيب الأخلاق ورياضة النفس ، والوقوف على الحقائق الخفية
And the second way of dividing the sphere into twelve parts: the division based on the ascendant. And I have not seen for anyone in determining these houses a suitable procedure. And what I have obtained is that we say: Four of them are the ascendant, the fourth, the seventh, and the tenth. As for the ascendant, it indicates the beginning in everything, and it is called the house of life and the soul. The reason for that is that the degree of the ascendant appeared after concealment, just as the child appeared in this world after concealment. So when similarity occurred between them from this aspect, inevitably they made the ascendant a sign for it. And know that the greatest proof in the science of the stars is that one of them is similar to the other in some respects. As for the second pillar, which is the fourth, it is the pillar of the earth, because it is under the earth. It has characteristics: one of them is that it is the pillar of the earth, resembling the origin from which the ascendant appears and from which it is generated, so inevitably they made it a sign for fathers, grandfathers, and the elders of the household. The second: that they attributed properties and estates to it. The third: since it is in utmost concealment, they attributed to it the outcomes of matters, but outcomes are hidden and not known. As for the third pillar, which is the seventh, it is a house opposite the ascendant, and it indicates the opposite. For this reason it is called the house of opposites, partners, and spouses. As for the fourth pillar, which is the tenth, it is the highest house in the sphere, so for this reason it is called the house of sultanate and power. And since the tenth is opposite the seventh and the fourth, and the fourth is a sign for fathers, the tenth is a sign for mothers. This is the ruling on these four houses. And know that there are two houses that are brothers which the ascendant looks at by trine; this aspect yields complete love and good. They are the fifth and the ninth. However, the fifth is under the earth and the ninth is above the earth. What is under the earth is less honorable than what is above the earth. The physical is lower in rank than the spiritual, and the more honorable is attributed to the more honorable. So inevitably they made the fifth a sign for what brings joy, due to spiritual things, so the fifth became the house of children, messengers, the righteous, gifts, and profit of merchandise; and the ninth became the house of religion, prophecy, knowledge, correct actions, and it is also the house of long journeys. However, these journeys may yield great benefits, and yield refinement of character, discipline of the soul, and knowledge of hidden realities.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage presents the second way of dividing the sphere into twelve parts based on the astrological houses (the ascendant and its related houses). It first identifies four principal houses: the ascendant (1st), the 4th, the 7th, and the 10th. The ascendant indicates beginnings and is likened to the birth of a child from concealment, so it signifies life and soul. The fourth house is under the earth, representing the origin, fathers, estates, and hidden outcomes. The seventh house is opposite the ascendant, signifying opposites, partners, and spouses. The tenth house is the highest, signifying sultanate and power, and since it is opposite the fourth, it signifies mothers. The text then explains two additional houses, the fifth and ninth, which are in trine aspect to the ascendant, bestowing love and good. The fifth under the earth is assigned to children, messengers, gifts, and profit, while the ninth above is assigned to religion, prophecy, knowledge, and long journeys. The commentary notes that the underlying method is analogy (similarity between celestial and earthly phenomena). This passage is a straightforward exposition of astrological house meanings, framed as the author's own understanding ('what I have obtained').

Classification of Signs and Angular Houses
Al-Razi classifies signs into movable, fixed, and dual, and introduces the twelve houses based on the ascendant.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's classification of the twelve signs into movable, fixed, and dual categories, and his identification of the four angular houses based on the ascendant.

Core Idea
The zodiac signs are divided into movable, fixed, and dual; houses are defined by the ascendant.

Al-Razi begins by summarizing the classification of the twelve signs into three categories of four: movable (beginnings of seasons), fixed (middles), and dual. He then turns to the division of the celestial sphere into twelve houses based on the ascendant, noting that only four of them—the angular houses—are fundamental.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style and the mention of a possible corruption in 'عملة'.
2
Identify the three categories of signs
Find where al-Razi describes the movable, fixed, and dual signs, and note how they correspond to the seasons.
Movable signs are at the beginnings of seasons, fixed signs at the middles, and dual signs are the remaining ones.
3
Understand the angular houses
Notice his statement about four houses (ascendant, fourth, seventh, tenth) and his comment about the lack of a proper cause from others.
These four angular houses are the most important in house division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا عرفت هذا فنقول : قد عرفت : أن أربعة منها منقلبة، وهي أوائل الفصول . والأربعة الثانية : ثابتة ، وهي أوساط الفصول، والأربعة الثالثة ذوات الجسدين . والوجه الثاني : في قسمة الفلك باثني عشر قسماً : القسمة المبنية على الطالع . وما رأيت لأحد في تعيين هذه البيوت : [عملة؟] مناسبة . والذي حصلته أن نقول : إن أربعة منها : وهي الطالع والرابع والسابع والعاشر .
When you know this, we say: You have known that four of them are movable (munqaliba), and they are the beginnings of the seasons. The second four are fixed (thābita), and they are the middles of the seasons. The third four are dual (dhāt al-jasadayn). And the second aspect: the division of the sphere into twelve sections: the division based on the ascendant (al-ṭāliʿ). I have not seen from anyone regarding the determination of these houses an appropriate [cause?]. What I have obtained is that we say: Four of them - namely the ascendant, fourth, seventh, and tenth.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage classifies the twelve signs into three groups of four: movable (the cardinal signs marking beginnings of seasons), fixed (the signs marking the middle of seasons), and dual (the mutable signs). Then it introduces the second aspect: the division of the celestial sphere into twelve houses based on the ascendant. The author notes he has not seen from anyone an appropriate cause for the determination of these houses, but he presents his own result: four houses are angular (awtād) – the ascendant (1st), fourth, seventh, and tenth.

The Four Angular Houses and Their Significations
Al-Razi explains the astrological meanings of the four angular houses: ascendant, fourth, seventh, tenth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Razi uses the principle of similarity to assign meanings to the four angular houses in astrology.

Core Idea
The angles signify earthly matters by celestial similarity.

In this passage, al-Razi lays out the astrological meanings of the four cardinal points of the horoscope: the ascendant, fourth, seventh, and tenth houses. He grounds each signification in the principle that celestial bodies resemble earthly phenomena, making them reliable indicators. Understanding these assignments requires seeing the logical parallels he draws.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the sequence and how each house is introduced.
The text uses the term 'watad' for angle.
2
Identify the four houses
Note the order: ascendant (first angle), fourth (second angle), seventh (third angle), tenth (fourth angle). Each is described with its attributes.
3
Understand the principle of similarity
Al-Razi explicitly states that the greatest proof in astrology is similarity (mushābaha). Look for how each house's signification is derived from a resemblance to something earthly.
For example, the ascendant is like a child emerging from concealment.
4
Trace each house's signification
For each house, note what it indicates and the reason given. Ascendant: beginnings. Fourth: earth, fathers, property, outcomes. Seventh: opposites, partners. Tenth: authority, mothers.
The tenth's connection to mothers comes via its relation to the fourth and seventh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما الطالع فإنه يدل على الابتداء في كل شيء . ويقال له : بيت الحياة والنفس . والسبب فيه : أن درجة الطالع ظهرت بعد الخفاء، كما أن الولد ظهر في هذا العالم بعد الخفاء ، فلما حصلت المشابهة بينهما من هذا الوجه ، لا جرم جعل الطالع دليلا عليه واعلم : أن البرهان الأعظم في علم النجوم : هو كون أحدهما مشابها للآخر من بعض الوجوه وأما الوتد الثاني وهو الرابع فإنه وتد الأرض ، لأجل أنه تحت الأرض . وله صفات : أحدها : أنه وتد الأرض ، يشبه الأصل الذي منه يظهر الطالع ، ومنه يتولد فلا جرم جعل دليلاً على الأباء والأجداد ، ومشايخ أهل البيت . وثانيها : أنهم نسبوا الأملاك والعقارات إليه . وثالثها : أنه لما كان في غاية الخفاء ، نسبوا إليه عواقب الأمور ، لكن العواقب تخفية غير معلومة . وأما الوتد الثالث : وهو السابع. فهو بيت مقابل للطالع ، وهو يدل على المقابل . فلهذا يقال : إنه بيت الأضداد والشركاء والأزواج . وأما الوتد الرابع ، وهو العاشر ، فهو أرفع بيت في الفلك فلهذا يقال : إنه بيت للسلطان والقوة. ولما كان العاشر مسابع والرابع ، وكان الرابع دليلا على الأباء ، كان العاشر دليلاً على الأمهات. فهذا هو الحكم على هذه البيوت الأربعة
As for the ascendant (al-ṭāliʿ), it indicates the beginning of everything. It is called the house of life and soul. The reason for this is that the degree of the ascendant appeared after concealment, just as the child appeared in this world after concealment. Since similarity occurred between them in this aspect, necessarily the ascendant was made a proof for it. Know that the greatest proof in the science of the stars (ʿilm al-nujūm) is that one is similar to the other in some respects. As for the second angle (al-watad al-thānī), which is the fourth, it is the angle of the earth, because it is below the earth. It has attributes: one: that it is the angle of the earth, resembling the origin from which the ascendant appears and is generated, so it was made a proof for fathers, grandfathers, and elders of the household. Two: they related properties and real estate to it. Three: since it was in extreme concealment, they related to it the outcomes of affairs, but outcomes are hidden and unknown. And as for the third angle, which is the seventh, it is a house opposite the ascendant, and it indicates the opposite. Therefore it is said that it is the house of opposites, partners, and spouses. As for the fourth angle, which is the tenth, it is the highest house in the sphere, so it is said that it is the house of sultanate and power. And since the tenth is [related to?] the seventh and fourth, and the fourth indicates fathers, the tenth indicates mothers. This is the ruling on these four houses.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage explains the astrological significations of the four angular houses. The author uses the principle of similarity (mushābaha) as the basis: the ascendant appears after being hidden as a child appears; the fourth, being below earth, indicates earth and origins; the seventh opposes the ascendant, so opposites and partnerships; the tenth is highest, thus authority. He also notes the relationship between fourth (fathers) and tenth (mothers) due to the tenth being related to the fourth and seventh.

Significations of the Trine Houses: Fifth and Ninth
Al-Razi explains the meanings of the fifth and ninth houses, which trine the ascendant.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Razi distinguishes between the fifth and ninth astrological houses based on their relative positions and spiritual significance.

Core Idea
The ninth house is more noble than the fifth because it is above earth and spiritual.

Al-Razi continues his discussion of the astrological houses by examining the two houses that trine the ascendant: the fifth and ninth. He explains that while both are benefic, they differ in nobility and the types of things they signify. Understanding this distinction is crucial for interpreting the influences of these houses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get a sense of Al-Razi's explanation.
Notice the contrast between 'below earth' and 'above earth'.
2
Identify the two houses
The passage mentions the fifth and ninth houses. Note that they both trine the ascendant, but have different positions.
3
Understand the distinction
Al-Razi states that what is below earth is less noble than what is above, and the corporeal is inferior to the spiritual. The fifth is below and corporeal, the ninth above and spiritual.
This explains why different significations are assigned.
4
List the significations
The fifth signifies children, messengers, good people, gifts, profit; the ninth signifies religion, prophethood, knowledge, correct actions, and long journeys.
The ninth's significations are more elevated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم : أنه حصل بيتان أخوان ينظر الطالع إليهما من التثليث . وهذا النظر يفيد كمال المحبة والخير، وهما الخامس والتاسع ، لكن الخامس تحت الأرض ، والتاسع فوق الأرض . والذي يكون تحت الأرض أقل شرفاً مما يكون فوق الأرض . والجسماني أقل طرقاً من الروحاني ، والأشرف منسوب إلى الأشرف ، فلا جرم جعلوا الخامس دليلاً على ما يفيد الفرج ، بسبب الروحانيات ، فصار الخامس بيت الأولاد والرسل والأخيار والهدايا وغلة البضائع ، وصار التاسع بيت الدين والنبوة والعلم والأفعال الصائبة ، وهو أيضاً بيت الاسفار الطويلة . إلا أن هذه الأسفار قد تفيد المنافع العظيمة ، وتفيد تهذيب الأخلاق ورياضة النفس ، والوقوف على الحقائق الخفية .
Know that there are two brother houses that the ascendant looks at with a trine aspect (al-tathlīth). This aspect yields perfect love and good, and they are the fifth and the ninth. But the fifth is below the earth, and the ninth is above the earth. That which is below the earth is less noble than that which is above the earth. The corporeal (al-jismānī) is less in way than the spiritual (al-rūḥānī), and the nobler is attributed to the nobler. Therefore they made the fifth a proof for what brings joy (faraj) due to spiritualities (al-rūḥāniyyāt), so the fifth became the house of children, messengers, good people, gifts, and profit of goods. The ninth became the house of religion, prophethood, knowledge, correct actions, and it is also the house of long journeys. However, these journeys may bring great benefits, refinement of morals, discipline of the soul, and knowledge of hidden realities.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage explains the fifth and ninth houses, which form a trine aspect with the ascendant. The author contrasts their positions: fifth below earth (less noble, corporeal), ninth above earth (more noble, spiritual). Consequently, the fifth indicates material and social joys (children, gifts, profit) while the ninth indicates higher spiritual and intellectual matters (religion, knowledge, prophethood). The ninth also includes long journeys, which are beneficial for moral refinement.

Key Terms
التثليث (trine)
الخامس (fifth)
التاسع (ninth)
الروحانيات (spiritualities)
الجسماني (corporeal)
الروحاني (spiritual)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Both the fifth and ninth houses are equally beneficial and signify similar things.
Correction: Al-Razi clearly states that the ninth is more noble than the fifth because it is above earth and spiritual. The fifth signifies corporeal and social matters, while the ninth signifies higher spiritual and intellectual matters.

Checkpoint
What does the ninth house primarily signify according to al-Razi?
A) Children and gifts
B) Wealth and property
C) Religion, prophethood, and knowledge
D) Enemies and death

Key Takeaway
The fifth and ninth houses both trine the ascendant, but the ninth is more noble and signifies spiritual and intellectual matters like religion and knowledge, while the fifth signifies worldly joys.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that the ninth house is more noble because it is above earth and spiritual. In your own life, are you prioritizing the 'ninth house' (religion, knowledge, soul refinement) over the 'fifth house' (worldly joys like children, gifts, profit)? What specific change can you make today to shift your focus upward?
?
The passage says long journeys in the ninth house bring 'refinement of morals, discipline of the soul, and knowledge of hidden realities.' When was the last time you undertook a journey—physical or intellectual—with the explicit intention of disciplining your soul? If you haven't, what is holding you back from seeking such a journey?
?
Al-Razi distinguishes between corporeal and spiritual, saying the spiritual is nobler. Honestly examine your daily habits: which do you feed more—your corporeal desires or your spiritual growth? Will you commit to one concrete action this week that affirms the spiritual over the corporeal?

Significations of the Sextile Houses: Third and Eleventh
Al-Razi explains the meanings of the third and eleventh houses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meanings of the third and eleventh houses as described by Al-Razi and why their significations are mixed and limited.

Core Idea
Sextile aspects yield only limited good; third and eleventh houses reflect mixed joy and incomplete spiritual joy.

Al-Razi continues his analysis of the astrological houses by focusing on the two houses that sextile the ascendant: the third and eleventh. These houses are considered 'brother houses' and, despite their beneficial aspect, they only bring a little good. This passage explains how each house's position (below or above earth) influences its significations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal English translation. Pay attention to the key terms and the overall structure.
2
Understand the third house
Note that the third house is below earth. It signifies brothers, sisters, relatives, and in-laws. These bring joy but also harm, reflecting the limited good of the sextile.
The passage explicitly says 'these things may bring a type of joy but they may also bring types of harm.'
3
Understand the eleventh house
The eleventh house is above earth. It indicates spiritual joy that is not complete. Therefore it is the house of hope, brothers, and friends.
The incomplete spiritual joy explains why the eleventh is associated with hope and friendship rather than full fulfillment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم : أنه حصل بيتان أخوان ، ينظر الطالع إليهما من التسديس . فأحدهما ؛ وهو الثالث تحت الأرض . والثاني : وهو الحادي عشر فوق الأرض. وهذا النظر يفيد خيراً قليلا . فلا جرم جعلوا الثالث دليلا على الأخوة والأخوات والأقارب والأصهار ، لأن هذه الأشياء قد تفيد نوعا من السرور إلا أنها قد تفيد أيضاً أنواعاً من المكارة. وأما الحادي عشر ، فلأجل كونه فوق الأرض . يدل على البهجة الروحانية التي لا تكون كاملة ، فلهذا جعلوه بيت الرجاء والأخوان والأصدقاء .
Know that there are two brother houses that the ascendant looks at with a sextile aspect (al-tasdīs). One of them - the third is below the earth, and the second - the eleventh is above the earth. This aspect yields a little good. Therefore they made the third a proof for brothers, sisters, relatives, and in-laws, because these things may bring a type of joy but they may also bring types of harm. As for the eleventh, because it is above the earth, it indicates spiritual joy (al-bahja al-rūḥāniyya) that is not complete, so they made it the house of hope, brothers, and friends.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage explains the third and eleventh houses, which form a sextile aspect with the ascendant. The author notes this aspect yields only a little good. The third, being below earth, signifies relatives and in-laws, which bring mixed joy and harm. The eleventh, above earth, indicates incomplete spiritual joy, hence it is the house of hope and friends.

Key Terms
التسديس
الثالث
الحادي عشر
البهجة الروحانية
السرور
المكارة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sextile aspects guarantee strong positive outcomes.
Correction: Al-Razi explicitly says sextile yields only a little good, and both houses have mixed or incomplete benefits.

Checkpoint
Why is the third house associated with both joy and harm?
A) Because it is below the earth
B) Because it is adjacent to the ascendant
C) Because it represents relatives and in-laws
D) Because it is a cadent house

Key Takeaway
The third and eleventh houses, despite being in sextile, only provide limited good: the third brings mixed joy/harm from relatives, and the eleventh indicates incomplete spiritual joy and hope.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever placed your hope for complete joy in friendships or family, only to find them mixed with harm? Where in your life are you expecting 'complete spiritual joy' from an 'incomplete' source?
?
This passage teaches that the sextile aspect yields only a little good. Reflect on your closest relationships: Do you expect them to give you perfect happiness? How can you adjust your expectations to align with this truth?
?
The eleventh house is about hope and friends, yet its joy is incomplete. Are you clinging to hopes that are ultimately incomplete? What would it mean for you to seek the only complete joy—from your Creator—while still appreciating the limited good from others?
