The Second House: Signification of Wealth
Al-Razi explains the signification of the second house as wealth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the second house, despite being cadent, signifies wealth due to its adjacency to the ascendant.

Core Idea
Even a cadent house can have a positive meaning if it is adjacent to a noble angle.

In this passage, Al-Razi explains the significations of the four cadent houses that are not aspected by the ascendant. He begins with the second house, which he notes is adjacent to the ascendant, the noblest angle. This adjacency grants it a unique, relatively positive signification: wealth. Let's read how the author justifies this.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the four houses
Read the Arabic passage once, noting that it first lists the four cadent houses, then focuses on the second.
The second house is the first to be explained.
2
Notice the adjacency to the ascendant
Al-Razi says the second is adjacent to the noblest angle (the ascendant). This is key to its positive meaning.
3
Understand the reasoning for wealth
The author explains that humans need wealth to accomplish important matters, hence the connection.
The reasoning is practical and grounded in human needs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقد ذكرنا حكم هذه البيوت الثمانية بقيت أربعة أخرى، لا ينظر الطالع إليها . وهي الثاني والسادس والثامن والثاني عشر . فنقول : أما الثاني - وإن كان ساقطاً - إلا أنه لا يلي أشرف الأوتاد ، وهو الطالع ، فجعلوه بيت المال ، لأن الإنسان إذا أحدث ، فإنه يحتاج إلى المال الذي به يقدر على تحصيل المهمات . وأما السادس فهو ساقط ، وليس في جوار بيت شريف ، فجعلوه دليلا على الضعف والمرض ، ولأنه في جوار الخامس ، فيدل على أن أشخاص يشبهون الأولاد . إلا أنهم يكونون في غاية السقوط ، وهم العبيد والدواب وأما الثامن فهو ساقط ، وفي جوار بيت الأضداد ، فيدل على الموت والهلاك . وأيضاً : لما جعلنا السادس دليلا على أول الشر ، وهو المرض ، وجب جعل الثامن دليلا على تمام حصول الشر ، وهو الموت، وأيضاً : فالثامن بيت مال الضد والعدو ، وذلك يناسب موت الإنسان . وأما الثاني عشر ، فهو ساقط ومع ذلك فهو آخر البيوت . ونهايتها . والشيء عند بلوغه إلى آخر مراتبه : يضعف ويحصل له الهموم . فعلمنا : أنه بيت الأعداء والمخالفين ، والغموم والسجن ، والسفلة والدواب .
We have mentioned the ruling on these eight houses. Four remain, which the ascendant does not look at: the second, sixth, eighth, and twelfth. We say: As for the second - although it is cadent (sāqiṭ), it is adjacent to the noblest of angles (al-awtād), which is the ascendant, so they made it the house of wealth, because when a person originates, he needs wealth by which he can accomplish important matters. As for the sixth, it is cadent and not in the vicinity of a noble house, so they made it a proof for weakness and illness. And because it is adjacent to the fifth, it indicates persons resembling children, but they are in extreme lowness: slaves and animals. As for the eighth, it is cadent and adjacent to the house of opposites (the seventh), so it indicates death and destruction. Also, since we made the sixth a proof for the beginning of evil (al-sharr), which is illness, it was necessary to make the eighth a proof for the complete attainment of evil, which is death. Also, the eighth is the house of wealth of the opposite and enemy, and that suits the death of a person. As for the twelfth, it is cadent, and moreover it is the last of the houses and their end. And a thing when it reaches its final stages becomes weak and acquires worries. So we know that it is the house of enemies, opponents, grief, prison, lowly people, and animals.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage explains the four cadent houses (second, sixth, eighth, twelfth) that do not receive aspects from the ascendant. The author assigns each a negative signification based on adjacency: second adjacent to ascendant (wealth for life's needs), sixth next to fifth (illness, slaves), eighth next to seventh (death), and twelfth at the end (enemies, grief). The logic is based on positional symbolism and sequential progression from lesser to greater evil.

Key Terms
ساقط (cadent)
الثاني (second)
المال (wealth)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All cadent houses are purely negative.
Correction: The second house is cadent but signifies wealth due to its adjacency to the ascendant, showing that not all cadent houses are negative.

Checkpoint
Why does Al-Razi consider the second house to signify wealth?
A) Because it is the house of money.
B) Because it is adjacent to the ascendant, the noblest angle.
C) Because it is the second house.
D) Because it is cadent.

Key Takeaway
The second house's signification of wealth stems from its adjacency to the ascendant, demonstrating that cadent houses can have positive meanings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pursue wealth, do you treat it as an ultimate goal or as a means to accomplish important matters? How would your priorities change if you truly lived by the principle that wealth is only for achieving noble ends?
?
Consider your own life: what are the 'important matters' (المهمات) that you are striving to achieve? Be specific. Are you using your resources, including wealth, intentionally toward those matters, or are they being diverted to trivial pursuits?
?
The lesson shows that even a weak position (cadent house) can gain strength from proximity to something noble. Is there an area in your life that feels 'fallen' or weak, yet is adjacent to a source of strength or goodness? How can you tap into that noble influence to transform that area?

The Sixth House: Signification of Illness and Lowliness
Al-Razi explains the signification of the sixth house as illness and lowliness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the sixth house signifies weakness, illness, slaves, and animals.

Core Idea
A cadent house not near a noble angle indicates lowliness and illness.

Al-Razi now turns to the sixth house, which is also cadent but lacks proximity to a noble angle. Instead, it is adjacent to the fifth house, associated with children. This adjacency, combined with its cadent nature, leads to significations of weakness and servitude. Let's examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for the sixth house
Read the Arabic passage, noting that the sixth house is cadent and not near a noble house.
2
Observe its adjacency to the fifth house
The sixth is adjacent to the fifth, which represents children. This connection leads to significations of persons resembling children but in extreme lowness.
3
Identify the specific significations
The passage mentions weakness, illness, slaves, and animals as the meanings of the sixth house.

Source Text

The Eighth House: Signification of Death
Al-Razi explains the signification of the eighth house as death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the eighth house signifies death and destruction.

Core Idea
The eighth house, adjacent to the seventh (house of opposites), indicates death as the completion of evil.

Al-Razi now explains the eighth house, which is cadent and adjacent to the seventh, the house of marriage and partnerships. Because the seventh represents the opposite, the eighth takes on significations of death and destruction. The author also links it logically as the completion of the illness signified by the sixth. Let's see the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for the eighth house
Read the Arabic passage, noting the eighth's adjacency to the seventh house of opposites.
2
Understand the logical progression
The author relates the eighth to the sixth: sixth is the beginning of evil (illness), eighth is its completion (death).
3
Note the additional reason
The eighth is also the house of wealth of the enemy, which suits death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقد ذكرنا حكم هذه البيوت الثمانية بقيت أربعة أخرى، لا ينظر الطالع إليها . وهي الثاني والسادس والثامن والثاني عشر . فنقول : أما الثاني - وإن كان ساقطاً - إلا أنه لا يلي أشرف الأوتاد ، وهو الطالع ، فجعلوه بيت المال ، لأن الإنسان إذا أحدث ، فإنه يحتاج إلى المال الذي به يقدر على تحصيل المهمات . وأما السادس فهو ساقط ، وليس في جوار بيت شريف ، فجعلوه دليلا على الضعف والمرض ، ولأنه في جوار الخامس ، فيدل على أن أشخاص يشبهون الأولاد . إلا أنهم يكونون في غاية السقوط ، وهم العبيد والدواب وأما الثامن فهو ساقط ، وفي جوار بيت الأضداد ، فيدل على الموت والهلاك . وأيضاً : لما جعلنا السادس دليلا على أول الشر ، وهو المرض ، وجب جعل الثامن دليلا على تمام حصول الشر ، وهو الموت، وأيضاً : فالثامن بيت مال الضد والعدو ، وذلك يناسب موت الإنسان . وأما الثاني عشر ، فهو ساقط ومع ذلك فهو آخر البيوت . ونهايتها . والشيء عند بلوغه إلى آخر مراتبه : يضعف ويحصل له الهموم . فعلمنا : أنه بيت الأعداء والمخالفين ، والغموم والسجن ، والسفلة والدواب .
We have mentioned the ruling on these eight houses. Four remain, which the ascendant does not look at: the second, sixth, eighth, and twelfth. We say: As for the second - although it is cadent (sāqiṭ), it is adjacent to the noblest of angles (al-awtād), which is the ascendant, so they made it the house of wealth, because when a person originates, he needs wealth by which he can accomplish important matters. As for the sixth, it is cadent and not in the vicinity of a noble house, so they made it a proof for weakness and illness. And because it is adjacent to the fifth, it indicates persons resembling children, but they are in extreme lowness: slaves and animals. As for the eighth, it is cadent and adjacent to the house of opposites (the seventh), so it indicates death and destruction. Also, since we made the sixth a proof for the beginning of evil (al-sharr), which is illness, it was necessary to make the eighth a proof for the complete attainment of evil, which is death. Also, the eighth is the house of wealth of the opposite and enemy, and that suits the death of a person. As for the twelfth, it is cadent, and moreover it is the last of the houses and their end. And a thing when it reaches its final stages becomes weak and acquires worries. So we know that it is the house of enemies, opponents, grief, prison, lowly people, and animals.

The Twelfth House: Signification of Enemies and Grief
Al-Razi explains the signification of the twelfth house as enemies and grief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the twelfth house signifies enemies, grief, prison, and lowly persons.

Core Idea
The last house of the chart, being the end, brings weakness, worries, and enmity.

Finally, Al-Razi addresses the twelfth house, the last of the houses. Its position at the end makes it signify decline, worry, and enemies. He concludes the discussion of the cadent houses with this explanation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for the twelfth house
Read the Arabic passage, noting that the twelfth is cadent and the last house.
2
Understand the reasoning of finality
Things at their final stage become weak and acquire worries. This applies to the twelfth house.
3
List the specific significations
The passage mentions enemies, opponents, grief, prison, lowly people, and animals.

فقد ذكرنا حكم هذه البيوت الثمانية بقيت أربعة أخرى، لا ينظر الطالع إليها . وهي الثاني والسادس والثامن والثاني عشر . فنقول : أما الثاني - وإن كان ساقطاً - إلا أنه لا يلي أشرف الأوتاد ، وهو الطالع ، فجعلوه بيت المال ، لأن الإنسان إذا أحدث ، فإنه يحتاج إلى المال الذي به يقدر على تحصيل المهمات . وأما السادس فهو ساقط ، وليس في جوار بيت شريف ، فجعلوه دليلا على الضعف والمرض ، ولأنه في جوار الخامس ، فيدل على أن أشخاص يشبهون الأولاد . إلا أنهم يكونون في غاية السقوط ، وهم العبيد والدواب وأما الثامن فهو ساقط ، وفي جوار بيت الأضداد ، فيدل على الموت والهلاك . وأيضاً : لما جعلنا السادس دليلا على أول الشر ، وهو المرض ، وجب جعل الثامن دليلا على تمام حصول الشر ، وهو الموت، وأيضاً : فالثامن بيت مال الضد والعدو ، وذلك يناسب موت الإنسان . وأما الثاني عشر ، فهو ساقط ومع ذلك فهو آخر البيوت . ونهايتها . والشيء عند بلوغه إلى آخر مراتبه : يضعف ويحصل له الهموم . فعلمنا : أنه بيت الأعداء والمخالفين ، والغموم والسجن ، والسفلة والدواب .
We have mentioned the ruling on these eight houses. Four remain, which the ascendant does not look at: the second, sixth, eighth, and twelfth. We say: As for the second - although it is cadent (sāqiṭ), it is adjacent to the noblest of angles (al-awtād), which is the ascendant, so they made it the house of wealth, because when a person originates, he needs wealth by which he can accomplish important matters. As for the sixth, it is cadent and not in the vicinity of a noble house, so they made it a proof for weakness and illness. And because it is adjacent to the fifth, it indicates persons resembling children, but they are in extreme lowness: slaves and animals. As for the eighth, it is cadent and adjacent to the house of opposites (the seventh), so it indicates death and destruction. Also, since we made the sixth a proof for the beginning of evil (al-sharr), which is illness, it was necessary to make the eighth a proof for the complete attainment of evil, which is death. Also, the eighth is the house of wealth of the opposite and enemy, and that suits the death of a person. As for the twelfth, it is cadent, and moreover it is the last of the houses and their end. And a thing when it reaches its final stages becomes weak and acquires worries. So we know that it is the house of enemies, opponents, grief, prison, lowly people, and animals.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage explains the four cadent houses (second, sixth, eighth, twelfth) that do not receive aspects from the ascendant. The author assigns each a negative signification based on adjacency: second adjacent to ascendant (wealth for life's needs), sixth next to fifth (illness, slaves), eighth next to seventh (death), and twelfth at the end (enemies, grief). The logic is based on positional symbolism and sequential progression from lesser to greater evil.

Key Terms
الثاني عشر (twelfth)
الأعداء (enemies)
الغموم (grief)
السجن (prison)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does Al-Razi say about things when they reach their final stages?
A) They become strong
B) They become weak and acquire worries
C) They become wealthy
D) They become healthy

Key Takeaway
The twelfth house, being the last, signifies enemies, grief, and all kinds of adversity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How do you typically respond when you sense hidden opposition or grief in your life? Do you confront it or avoid it? What would it look like to face your 'twelfth house' with courage today?
?
The twelfth house represents the end and weakness. In what area of your life are you feeling at an end or weak right now? How might acknowledging that vulnerability actually be a step toward strength?
?
If the twelfth house is unavoidable for everyone, what is one enmity or grief you have been pretending doesn't exist? What is one small action you can take this week to address it honestly?

Making a Talisman for Enmity (Using Mercury)
Example of talisman for enmity using Mercury

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the astrological process for creating a talisman to cause enmity, including the selection of planet, stone, engraving, and incenses.

Core Idea
Talismans for enmity are made by targeting Mercury at a suitable degree and using a lapis lazuli or khumāhan stone engraved with fighting men.

This passage details the practical steps for making a talisman specifically to cause enmity between people. It assumes the reader already knows the astrological basics and focuses on the materials and actions required, including the choice of stone and the image to engrave.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the enmity talisman
Read the Arabic and translation for the enmity example. Note the sequence: choosing the planet (Mercury), the stone (lapis lazuli or khumāhan), engraving, and using incenses.
The passage also mentions a stone with special property (khumāhan) for enmity.
2
Identify the key components
List the required elements: suitable degree of Mercury, stone (lapis lazuli or khumāhan), image of two fighting men, and incenses of Mercury.
3
Understand the rationale
Why does the author mention lapis lazuli? Because Mercury indicates it. Why use khumāhan? Because it has a special property for enmity.
The author assumes divine/hidden properties in stones.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Consider what this reveals about the worldview: talismans are believed to harness astrological and mineral properties to affect human affairs.
This is not a condemnation but a description of the method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مناسبة له فعند طلوع تلك الدرجة ، يجب أن يتخذ فيه تمثال من الجنس الذي يناسب ذلك الكوكب من الأجساد السبعة ، ويبالغ في تجويد صنعته . وطريق ذلك : أن يكون قد هيأ بين يديه آلة التفريغ ، وإذابة الجسد . فإذا حضر الوقت المعين ، أفرغه في القالب الذي أعده له ، وليكن ذلك الإنسان عند ذلك العمل منفرداً لا يكون معه غيره ، وليبخر بالبخورات المختصة بذلك الكوكب وإن أردت عمل خاتم فليكن فصه من جوهر ذلك الكوكب ، ومما له خاصية في تحصيل ذلك المطلوب . ومثاله : إذا أردت عمل طلسم لإيقاع العداوة ، فقصدت عطارد في برج مناسب ، ودرجة مناسبة ] ونظير من كوكب مناسب لهذا العمل ، ولما علمت : أن عطارد يدل على [ حجر اللازورد فاتخذ من الفصوص ما كان أزرق في اللون ، وعلمت : أن حجر الخماهن له خاصية في إيقاع العداوة ] فاتخذ الفص منه ، وانقش عليه الصورة المناسبة لذلك المطلوب . وهي : صورة إنسانين يقتتلان ، ثم استعمل بخورات عطارد فيه وإن أردت عمل طلسم لإيقاع بلاء بإنسان وتمريضه ، فاطلب حلول زحل في الدرجات المناسبة لهذا العمل، واتخذ تمثالاً على هيئة ذلك الإنسان ، واعتمد في ذلك الوقت أن تفسد عضواً من أعضائه ، وموضعاً من جسده فإنك إذا فعلت ذلك ، فسد ذلك العضو من ذلك الإنسان فذلك هو الكلام في اتخاذ التماثيل والخواتيم
Suitability for it: when that degree rises, one must make an image (tamthāl) from the genus that suits that planet among the seven bodies, and excel in perfecting its craft. Its method: he should have prepared before him the tool of casting and melting the body. When the appointed time arrives, he pours it into the mold he prepared for it, and let that person at that work be alone, not with anyone else, and let him fumigate with the incenses specific to that planet. If you want to make a ring, let its stone be from the gem of that planet, and from what has a special property in achieving that desired aim. Its example: if you wish to make a talisman (ṭilasm) for causing enmity, you target Mercury (ʿUṭārid) in a suitable sign and a suitable degree, and a counterpart from a planet suitable for this work. When you know that Mercury indicates the stone lapis lazuli, so take from the stones what is blue in color, and you know that the stone khumāhan has a special property in causing enmity, so take the stone from it, and engrave on it the image suitable for that desired aim, which is the image of two men fighting. Then use Mercury's incenses on it. If you want to make a talisman for inflicting affliction on a person and making him ill, seek the arrival of Saturn (Zuḥal) in the degrees suitable for this work, and make an image in the likeness of that person, and rely at that time to corrupt an organ of his organs and a place of his body. For if you do that, that organ of that person becomes corrupted. That is the speech about making images and rings.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage describes the method for making talismans to achieve specific effects, like causing enmity or illness. It begins by stating that when an astrological degree rises, one must create an image from a material that corresponds to the planet (among the seven planets). The process involves careful preparation: having the tools for casting, being alone during the work, and using specific incenses. If a ring is desired, its stone must come from the planet's gem. Then two examples are given: First, for enmity, one uses Mercury in a suitable astrological sign and degree, and chooses a stone like lapis lazuli (blue) or khumāhan (which has a property for enmity). The engraving should depict two men fighting. Second, for inflicting illness, one uses Saturn at suitable degrees, creates an image of the target, and intends to corrupt a specific organ. The passage concludes that this is the full account of making images and rings.

عداوة (ʿadāwa)
عطارد (ʿUṭārid)
درجة (daraja)
فص (faṣṣ)
جوهر (jawhar)
خاصية (khāṣṣiyya)
بخور (bakhūr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The passage is a condemnation of talisman-making.
Correction: The passage neutrally describes the method and assumes its efficacy; it does not judge it.

Checkpoint

A) Lapis lazuli
B) Khumāhan

Key Takeaway
To make a talisman for enmity, use Mercury's stone (lapis lazuli or khumāhan) engraved with two fighting men and incense.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This passage describes with precision how to cause enmity through a talisman. Have you ever wished harm on someone, even secretly? What does this detailed instruction reveal about the human heart’s potential for devising ways to act on that enmity? How will you guard your own heart from such desires?
?
The author assumes that stones and incenses have inherent powers to bring about enmity. Consider your own daily routines: are there things you rely on—perhaps unconsciously—as 'tools' to achieve your desires, forgetting that only Allah has true power? What would it take to shift your trust fully to Him?
?
If you were faced with the opportunity to use such a talisman against someone who wronged you, would you be tempted? What does your answer reveal about your iman? Commit today to a specific dua or action you will take the next time you feel enmity toward someone.

Making a Talisman for Illness (Using Saturn)
Example of talisman for illness using Saturn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the astrological process for creating a talisman to inflict illness on a person, including targeting Saturn, making an image of the victim, and corrupting a specific organ.

Core Idea
Talismans for illness are made by targeting Saturn at a suitable degree, creating a likeness of the victim, and intending to corrupt a specific body part.

This passage provides a second example of talisman-making, this time to cause illness. The method involves Saturn, the malefic planet, and focuses on creating an image of the intended victim. The practitioner is to focus on a particular organ to corrupt.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the illness talisman
Read the Arabic and translation for the illness example. Note the steps: seek Saturn in suitable degrees, make an image of the person, and during the process intend to corrupt an organ.
The passage does not specify which organ; it leaves it to the practitioner.
2
Understand the astrological basis
Saturn is chosen because it is associated with affliction and illness. The degrees must be suitable for the intended harm.
3
Identify the key actions
List: (1) Find Saturn in appropriate degrees. (2) Create a image resembling the target. (3) At the time of making, intend to corrupt a specific organ.
The belief is that corruption of the image's organ will affect the real person.
4
Reflect on the underlying theory
This assumes a sympathetic connection between the image and the person, a common idea in talismanic magic.
The passage does not justify this; it simply presents the method.

Objection and Refutation on Talisman-Making
Presents an objection that talisman-making is futile and Jabir's refutation by analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key objection to talisman-making and Jabir's refutation using the analogy of birth under a planetary ascendant.

Core Idea
Talisman-making is defended by analogy to astrological influences at birth.

This passage presents a direct challenge to the efficacy of talisman-making, calling it futile. In response, the renowned alchemist Jabir ibn Hayyan offers a powerful analogy, comparing the creation of a talisman under a planetary ascendant to the birth of a child under the same conditions. This analogy serves to ground the practice in a familiar astrological framework.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Identify the two specific criticisms: that the work is vain (ʿabath) and that astrological correspondences and psychological fancies are sufficient.
2
Read Jabir's refutation
Focus on the analogy: the occurrence of the image at the planet's rising is like the birth of a child at that rising.
Note the parallel structure: just as the planet's power flows into the newborn, it flows into the talisman.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider how this argument shifts the burden back to the objectors. If they accept astrological influences on birth, they must accept similar influences on talismans.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن الناس من طعن في هذا النوع من العمل . وقال : إنه عبث لا فائدة فيه . بل الاقتصار على المناسبات النجومية ، والأوهام النفسانية : كافية . قال جابر بن عبد الله بن حيان : ( هذا الطعن غلط ، لأن حدوث تلك الصورة عند طلوع ذلك الكوكب يجري مجرى ولادة الولد ، عند طلوع الكوكب ، فكما أن هناك تسري قوة الكوكب الطالع ، والدرجة الطالعة في ذلك المولود ، فكذا ههنا تسري قوتهما في تلك الصورة المنقوشة والتمثال المفروغ )
And among the people, some have criticized this type of work, saying: 'It is vain, with no benefit. Rather, limiting oneself to astrological correspondences and psychological fancies is sufficient.' Jabir ibn Abdullah ibn Hayyan said: 'This criticism is wrong, because the occurrence of that image at the rising of that planet is analogous to the birth of a child at the rising of the planet. Just as there the power of the ascendant planet and the ascendant degree flow into the newborn, so here their power flows into that engraved image and the cast statue.'
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage presents an objection to talisman-making and its refutation. The objectors claim that such work is futile and that only astrological correspondences and psychological imaginations are needed. In response, Jabir ibn Abdullah ibn Hayyan argues that the criticism is mistaken. He draws an analogy: the creation of the image at the moment of a planet's rising is like the birth of a child under an astrological ascendant. Just as in birth, the power of the ascendant planet and degree flows into the newborn, so in talisman-making, that same power flows into the engraved image or cast statue. Thus, the talisman is not empty; it channels planetary influence.

Key Terms
طعن (ṭaʿn)
عبث (ʿabath)
مناسبات نجومية (munāsabāt nujūmiyya)
أوهام نفسانية (awhām nafsāniyya)
جابر بن حيان (Jābir ibn Ḥayyān)
ولادة (wilāda)
قوة (quwwa)
كوكب طالع (kawkab ṭāliʿ)
درجة طالعة (daraja ṭāliʿa)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author endorses astrology and talisman-making as genuine practices.
Correction: The author is reporting Jabir's opinion; he does not necessarily endorse it.

Checkpoint

A) The growth of plants
B) The birth of a child under a planet
C) The effect of medicine on the body
D) The influence of the moon on tides

Key Takeaway
Jabir defends talisman-making by comparing it to astrological influences at birth, arguing that celestial power flows into the talisman just as it does into a newborn.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about practices that seem strange or superstitious, do you dismiss them immediately or pause to consider the reasoning behind them? Jabir listened to the objection and gave a thoughtful analogy. What would it take for you to genuinely engage with ideas you instinctively reject?
?
The critics relied on 'astrological correspondences and psychological fancies' as sufficient explanations. Are there areas in your own life where you accept superficial or comfortable explanations instead of seeking deeper truth? How might that be affecting your relationship with Allah?
?
Jabir's analogy suggests that the world is interconnected in ways we cannot always see—celestial power flowing into both a newborn and a talisman. How does this challenge your understanding of cause and effect? Do you truly believe that Allah works through means, or do you subtly deny His control by attributing things to mere chance or natural law?

The Worker's Conditions for Talisman Efficacy
Specifies four conditions for the talisman worker.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific conditions the worker must fulfill when crafting a talisman to maximize its effect.

Core Idea
The worker's garments, speech, and heart must align with the planet.

This passage from al-Matalib al-‘Aliyah details the practical requirements for a talisman worker. Before the physical act of casting or engraving, the worker must harmonize his external and internal states with the celestial forces. This lesson unpacks those conditions and explains why their combination strengthens the talisman's effect.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on worker conditions
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, focusing on the four conditions: garment, state, speech, and heart.
Notice that these conditions are simultaneous, not sequential.
2
Identify the four conditions
List the four things the worker must do: wear suitable garment, be collected in suitable states, recite praise, and have his heart present.
Each condition relates to a different aspect: clothing, demeanor, speech, and intention.
3
Understand the unifying principle
The passage says combining these conditions makes the effect stronger. Reflect on why each condition contributes to the overall harmony.
This reflects the macrocosm-microcosm correspondence.

واعلم أن عند فراغ ذلك الصنم في القالب ، وعند النقش في ذلك الحجر ، يجب أن يكون العامل له لابساً ثوباً يناسب ذلك الكوكب ، ويكون مستجمعاً لجميع الأحوال المناسبة لذلك الكوكب ، ويكون قائلاً باللسان : الثناء اللائق بذلك الكوكب ، ويكون قلبه مستحضراً للأحوال اللائقة بذلك الكوكب . فإن [ هذه الأحوال ] إذا اجتمعت ، كان التأثير أقوى . النوع الثاني من الأمور المعتبرة في هذا الباب : تلطيخ تلك التماثيل بالأدوية المناسبة لتلك الأغراض والمقاصد . قال و جابر بن حيان » : « المقصود من الطلسم : إما الجلب ، وإما الدفع. أما الجلب فلا يتم إلا بجميع الأشياء [ المشاكلة . والدفع لا يتم إلا بجميع الأشياء] المضادة . والدليل عليه : إجماع الأطباء على أن الصحة تحفظ بالمماثل . والمرض يزال بالضد ، ثم يقول : ( وهذان الوجهان إما أن يعتبرا في الأسباب الفلكية ، وهي طبائع النجوم والبروج ، أو في الأسباب السفلية ، وهي طباع الأودية والعقاقير ) واعلم : أن الأشياء المشاكلة [ على ثلاث مراتب : فالمرتبة الأولى : حصول المشاكلة ] في الكيفيتين ، أعني الفاعلة والمنفعلة ، كالحار واليابس [ مع الحار واليابس ] وهذا النوع أقوى أنواع المشابهة ، والمرتبة الثانية : أن تكون المشاكلة حاصلة في إحدى الكيفيتين فقط . لكنها هي الفاعلة ، فإنها أقوى من المنفعلة ، مثل الحار الرطب مع الحار اليابس . والمرتبة الثالثة : أن تكون المشاكلة حاصلة في إحدى الكيفيتين فقط ، وهي المنفعلة [ مثل : اليابس
Know that when casting that idol in the mold, and when engraving on that stone, the worker must be wearing a garment that suits that planet, and be collected in all states suitable for that planet, and be saying with his tongue the praise befitting that planet, and his heart be present with the states befitting that planet. For if these states are combined, the effect is stronger. The second type of matters considered in this chapter: smearing those images with drugs suitable for those purposes and aims. Jabir ibn Hayyan said: 'The purpose of the talisman is either attraction (jalb) or repulsion (dafʿ). As for attraction, it is only completed by all things that are similar (mushākila). And repulsion is only completed by all things that are opposite (muḍādda). The proof for it is the consensus of physicians that health is preserved by what is similar, and illness is removed by what is opposite.' Then he says: 'These two aspects are to be considered either in the celestial causes, which are the natures of stars and zodiacal signs, or in the terrestrial causes, which are the natures of remedies and drugs.' Know that things that are similar (mushākila) are of three ranks: The first rank is the occurrence of similarity in both qualities, I mean the active and the passive, like hot and dry with hot and dry. This type is the strongest kind of similarity. The second rank is that similarity occurs in only one of the two qualities, but it is the active, for it is stronger than the passive, like hot and wet with hot and dry. The third rank is that similarity occurs in only one of the two qualities, and it is the passive, like dry...
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage covers conditions for talisman efficacy and a classification of similarity. First, it states that when casting or engraving, the worker must wear a garment suitable to the planet, be in a suitable state, recite praise, and have his heart present. Combining these strengthens the effect. Then it introduces the second type of considerations: smearing the images with suitable drugs. Next, Jabir ibn Hayyan explains that the talisman's purpose is either attraction or repulsion. Attraction requires things that are similar; repulsion requires things that are opposite. He supports this with medical consensus: health is preserved by similar things, illness removed by opposite. He notes that these principles apply to both celestial causes (stars and signs) and terrestrial causes (drugs). Finally, similarity is classified into three ranks: (1) similarity in both active and passive qualities (strongest), (2) similarity in the active quality only (medium), and (3) similarity in the passive quality only (weakest). The text cuts off at the third rank.

ثوب (thawb)
أحوال (aḥwāl)
تأثير (taʾthīr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception: One might think only the physical act of casting matters, not the worker's state.
Correction: The passage shows that the worker's attire, speech, and inner presence are essential for maximum efficacy.

The talisman worker must align his garment, state, speech, and heart with the planet to achieve the strongest effect.

Purpose of Talisman: Attraction and Repulsion
Explains the purpose of talismans and the principles of similarity and opposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the dual purpose of talismans (attraction and repulsion) and how they rely on similarity and opposition, with a proof from medical consensus.

Core Idea
Talismans attract by similarity and repel by opposition.

After discussing the worker's conditions, the text moves to the theoretical foundation of talismanic magic. Here, Jabir ibn Hayyan explains that all talismans aim either to attract something beneficial or repel something harmful. This lesson examines the principles of similarity and opposition, their proof from medicine, and how they apply to celestial and terrestrial causes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on jalb and daf
Read from 'النوع الثاني' to 'العقاقير' in Arabic and translation.
Notice the shift from practical conditions to theoretical principles.
2
Identify the two purposes and their means
Jalb requires similarity (mushākala), daf requires opposition (muḍādda). Note the logical structure.
3
Analyze the medical analogy
The proof is from medicine: health is preserved by similar, illness removed by opposite. Consider why this analogy is persuasive.
This establishes a natural law parallel.
4
Understand the two realms of application
The principles apply to both celestial causes (stars/signs) and terrestrial causes (drugs).
This bridges astrology and pharmacology.

Three Ranks of Similarity
Classifies similarity into three ranks based on active and passive qualities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classification of similarity into three ranks based on active and passive qualities, and why the first rank is strongest.

Core Idea
Similarity strength depends on how many qualities are shared.

The final part of this source passage provides a detailed classification of similarity (mushākala) into three ranks. This taxonomy is essential for determining the efficacy of talismanic operations: the more qualities that align, the stronger the effect. This lesson unpacks each rank and explains the distinction between active and passive qualities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on three ranks
Read from 'واعلم أن الأشياء المشاكلة' to the end of the provided text.
The text cuts off at the third rank; use the translation to complete.
2
Distinguish the two qualities
Identify the active (fāʿila) and passive (munfaʿila) qualities. Active qualities are those like hot and dry; passive are like wet and cold.
These are Aristotelian categories.
3
Understand each rank
Rank 1: similarity in both qualities (strongest). Rank 2: similarity in active only (medium). Rank 3: similarity in passive only (weakest).
The text ranks them by strength.
4
Reflect on the underlying principle
Consider why sharing both qualities is strongest. It implies more complete harmony.
This mirrors the idea of perfect correspondence.

Conditions for Effective Talisman Work
Lists four conditions for the talisman maker to maximize effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four conditions that the talisman worker must fulfill to maximize the effect of the talisman.

Core Idea
The talisman's effect depends on the worker's holistic harmony with the planetary influences.

This passage from the Islamic occult tradition outlines specific criteria for the practitioner performing talisman work. It emphasizes that the worker's outer and inner states must align with the planetary spirit they intend to invoke. Let's examine the four conditions and their purpose.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the translation. Get a sense of the author's concise style.
Notice the parallel structure in listing the conditions.
2
Identify the four conditions
Find each of the four conditions mentioned: clothing, general state, verbal praise, and mental focus. Understand what each entails.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Consider why the author says gathering these conditions makes the effect stronger. Think about the underlying principle of correspondence.
This connects to the learning objective.

For if these conditions are gathered, the effect is stronger.

Commentary
This passage gives instructions for the ritual preparation of the talisman maker. It lists four conditions: appropriate clothing, emotional state, verbal praise, and mental focus. The conclusion is that these together strengthen the effect.

Second Type: Smearing Statues with Drugs
Presents the second type of talisman practice and quotes Jabir ibn Hayyan on attraction and repulsion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second type of talisman practice and how Jabir ibn Hayyan justifies it through medical principles of similarity and opposition.

Core Idea
Talismans work by natural attraction and repulsion, not by magic.

This passage presents a specific talisman method: applying drugs to statues to achieve desired effects. The renowned alchemist Jabir ibn Hayyan explains that talismans aim to attract or repel, and these operations rely on the principles of similarity and opposition, supported by a medical analogy.

Guided Path
1
Read and identify the practice
Read the passage carefully. Note that it describes the second type of talisman: smearing statues with drugs suited to the purpose.
The passage is concise but contains a classification and a proof.
2
Understand the two purposes
Jabir states that every talisman is for either attraction (jalb) or repulsion (daf'). Attraction requires similar things; repulsion requires opposite things.
This is a key principle linking talisman to natural philosophy.
3
Examine the medical proof
Jabir supports his claim by citing consensus of physicians: health is preserved by similars, illness cured by opposites. This shows the talisman principle is grounded in empirical observation.
This analogy makes talisman seem rational rather than magical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Jabir ibn Hayyan said: 'The purpose of the talisman is either attraction or repulsion. As for attraction, it is not completed except with all similar things. And repulsion is not completed except with all opposite things. The proof for it is the consensus of physicians that health is preserved by the similar, and illness is removed by the opposite.'
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage presents the second type of talismanic practice: applying appropriate drugs to statues. It quotes Jabir ibn Hayyan, who defines the two functions of talisman: attraction and repulsion. He then gives a proof from medicine: similarity preserves health, opposition cures disease. This is a classification and a proof by analogy.

Three Ranks of Similarity
Classifies similarity into three ranks based on shared qualities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three ranks of similarity and how they are distinguished by active and passive qualities.

Core Idea
Similarity is graded by which qualities are shared, from strongest to weakest.

This lesson introduces a foundational concept in the study of similarity: the three ranks based on shared qualities. Understanding these ranks helps in analyzing how things resemble each other in terms of active and passive properties. The author presents a clear classification with examples.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the classification.
Pay attention to the examples.
2
Identify the three ranks
Notice that the first rank shares both qualities, the second shares only the active, the third shares only the passive. Compare their strengths.
The author states which is strongest and weakest.
3
Reflect on the logic
Understand why sharing the active quality is stronger than sharing the passive.
Active qualities are considered more influential.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم : أن الأشياء المشاكلة على ثلاث مراتب : فالمرتبة الأولى : حصول المشاكلة في الكيفيتين ، أعني الفاعلة والمنفعلة ، كالحار واليابس مع الحار واليابس وهذا النوع أقوى أنواع المشابهة ، والمرتبة الثانية : أن تكون المشاكلة حاصلة في إحدى الكيفيتين فقط . لكنها هي الفاعلة ، فإنها أقوى من المنفعلة ، مثل الحار الرطب مع الحار اليابس . والمرتبة الثالثة : أن تكون المشاكلة حاصلة في إحدى الكيفيتين فقط ، وهي المنفعلة مثل : اليابس الحار ، واليابس البارد . وهذه المرتبة دون ما قبلها . لأن الكيفية المنفعلة أضعف من الفاعلة .
And know: that similar things are of three ranks. The first rank: the occurrence of similarity in both qualities, I mean active and passive, like hot and dry with hot and dry, and this type is the strongest of types of similarity. The second rank: that similarity occurs in only one of the two qualities, but it is the active one, for it is stronger than the passive, like hot moist with hot dry. The third rank: that similarity occurs in only one of the two qualities, and it is the passive one, like dry hot and dry cold. And this rank is lower than the one before it because the passive quality is weaker than the active.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage classifies similarity into three ranks based on how many of the two primary qualities (active and passive) are shared. The first rank shares both, strongest. The second shares only the active quality, medium. The third shares only the passive, weakest.

Key Terms
مشاكلة
مراتب
كيفية فاعلة
كيفية منفعلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think similarity is simply present or absent, a binary property.
Correction: This passage shows similarity has degrees: it can be strong (both qualities), medium (active only), or weak (passive only).

Checkpoint
Which rank of similarity is strongest?
A) Sharing only passive quality
B) Sharing both qualities
C) Sharing only active quality
D) Sharing no qualities

Key Takeaway
Similarity is not merely yes or no; it has degrees determined by which qualities are shared.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your relationships with others, do you focus more on shared active qualities (like values and intentions) or passive qualities (like hobbies and preferences)? Which of these similarities feels stronger to you, and why? How can you strengthen the deeper similarities?
?
Think of a time you felt a strong connection with someone. Did you share both active and passive qualities? Now consider a weaker connection. Was it only one type? What does this teach you about how you form bonds? Commit to seeking out people who share your active qualities.

Three Ranks of Opposition
Classifies opposition into three ranks, but text likely has a scribal error.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three ranks of opposition in Islamic logic and identify a likely scribal error in the transmitted classification.

Core Idea
Opposition has three ranks, but the text's third rank may be corrupted.

This passage from al-Matālib al-ʿĀliyah attempts to classify opposition (muḍāddah) into three ranks. However, as you will see, the second and third ranks are described identically, which is almost certainly a scribal error. Understanding the intended classification and recognizing such errors is part of critical engagement with classical texts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text and its translation carefully. Notice the repetition between the second and third ranks.
The passage is short but dense.
2
Identify the three ranks
The text lists three ranks. The first is clear: opposition in both active and passive qualities. The second and third both mention 'the two passive qualities only.' Mark this repetition.
This repetition is the scribal error.
3
Consider the intended classification
Typically, the ranks are: 1) both qualities, 2) only active qualities, 3) only passive qualities. Reflect on which qualities might be meant for the third rank.
The error likely occurred in copying.
4
Understand the implications
Recognizing manuscript errors is part of scholarly work. This passage shows the importance of textual criticism in Islamic logic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الأشياء المضادة. فهي أيضاً على ثلاث مراتب . فالمرتبة الأولى : أن يكون التنافي حاصلاً في الكيفيتين معاً . مثل : الحار اليابس مع البارد الرطب . والمرتبة الثانية - وهي المتوسطة - أن يكون التنافي حاصلا في الكيفيتين المنفعلتين فقط . والمرتبة الثالثة - وهي الأخيرة - أن يكون التنافي حاصلاً في الكيفيتين المنفعلتين فقط
As for opposite things, they also are of three ranks. The first rank: that opposition occurs in both qualities together, like hot dry with cold moist. The second rank - which is the intermediate - that opposition occurs in the two passive qualities only. The third rank - which is the last - that opposition occurs in the two passive qualities only.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage attempts to classify opposition into three ranks. The first rank: opposition in both active and passive qualities. The second and third ranks are both described as opposition in the two passive qualities only, which is likely an error. Normally, the second rank would be opposition in the active qualities only, and the third in the passive. The text as given is corrupt.

Key Terms
مضادة
تنافي
كيفية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The text as transmitted is correct as is.
Correction: The repetition of the second and third ranks indicates a scribal error; the intended classification likely distinguishes between active-only and passive-only opposition.

Checkpoint
What is the first rank of opposition according to the passage?
A) Opposition in both qualities
B) Opposition in passive only
C) Opposition in active only
D) No opposition

Key Takeaway
Opposition is classified into three ranks, but the manuscript contains an error where the second and third ranks are identical; the intended classification distinguishes between opposition in active-only and passive-only qualities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a contradiction or repetition in a trusted text, do you automatically assume you have misread it, or do you consider the possibility of a transmission error? How can you cultivate the balance between reverence for tradition and critical thinking in your own study?
?
A single scribal error can distort a logical classification for centuries. How does this reality challenge your own diligence when transmitting knowledge—whether teaching, writing, or even speaking? Are you as careful to preserve truth as you would want others to be with knowledge they pass on to you?

Applies similarity classification to astrology, focusing on trine aspects.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
In astrology, complete similarity occurs through trine aspects, with a clear ranking of strength among the signs.

Having established the general principle of similarity classification, the author now applies it to the celestial realm. This passage demonstrates how complete similarity—sharing both primary qualities—manifests in the astrological concept of triplicity (trine aspects). You will see how the fire signs serve as an example and how they are ranked in strength.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the overall flow. Note the technical terms like تثليث (triplicity).
The passage is short but dense.
2

Notice that complete similarity is defined by triplicity—the 1st, 5th, and 9th signs from a given sign. These form a triangle of 120° aspects.
This is an application of a prior classification to astrology.
3
Analyze the example and ranking
The fire signs (Aries, Leo, Sagittarius) are given as an example. Observe the ranking: Leo is strongest, then Sagittarius, then Aries. Consider why Leo might be central.
The ranking is explicitly stated, not derived from other principles here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا عرفت هذا ، فيجب أن تعتبر هذه الأحوال في الكواكب وفي الأدوية . وأما اعتبار المشاكلة في الفلكيات . فنقول : المشاكلة التامة حاصلة بالتثليث ، وهو الأول والخامس والتاسع . لأن البروج المتناظرة بحسب التثليث تكون متشاكلة في الكيفيتين معاً . مثل الحمل والأسد والقوس ، إلا أن أقواها هو الأوسط ، وهو الأسد ، ثم الأخير وهو القوس ، ثم الأول وهو الحمل . وإذا عرفت الحال في هذا المثال ، فقس البواقي عليه

And as for considering similarity in the celestial bodies, we say: complete similarity occurs by triplicity, which is the first, fifth, and ninth. Because the signs corresponding according to triplicity are similar in both qualities together, like Aries, Leo, and Sagittarius, except that the strongest of them is the middle, which is Leo, then the last, which is Sagittarius, then the first, which is Aries. And if you know the situation in this example, then analogize the rest to it.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage applies the classification of similarity to astrology. It states that complete similarity (sharing both qualities) occurs when planets are in trine aspect (120 degrees apart). It gives the example of fire signs: Aries, Leo, Sagittarius, with Leo being the strongest.

Two Investigations on Unknown Recitations
Posing two questions about unknown recitations and presenting two opinions on their origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two key questions about unknown incantations and the first opinion regarding their origin.

Core Idea
The origin and benefit of unknown recitations are debated among scholars.

This passage from al-Matalib al-Aliyah raises two critical questions about incantations whose meanings are unknown. It then presents the first of two opinions on their origin, linking them to spiritual exercises and pure spirits. The second opinion is introduced but the text cuts off, leaving it incomplete.

Read the passage and translation

These questions set the agenda for the discussion.
3
Examine the first opinion

The passage does not endorse this opinion; it merely reports it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بحثان: وأما الرقى التي لا يفهم منها شيء، ولا يحصل الوقوف على معانيها ففيها الأول: إن الذي نظم تلك الكلمات، ورتبها في أول الأمر. من كان؟ والثاني: إنه أي فائدة لنا في قراءتها وذكرها؟ فنقول: أما المقام الأول. فللناس فيه قولان: الأول: وهم الذين يبالغون في تعظيم تلك الكلمات المجهولة، الذين يقولون: إن المتقدمين لما بالغوا في الرياضات انكشفت لهم الأرواح الطاهرة القوية، القاهرة. فألقت عليهم العزائم والرقي. والقول الثاني: إن حسن الظن يقتضي أن تلك الكلمات المجهولة.
Two investigations: As for the incantations from which nothing is understood, and the understanding of their meanings is not obtained, there are in them: First: Who was it that composed those words and arranged them in the beginning? Second: What benefit is there for us in reciting and mentioning them? And the second opinion: that good assumption requires that those unknown words...
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage introduces two investigations (بحثان) regarding the unknown kind of recitations. The first question asks about the originator: who composed and arranged these words initially? The second asks about the benefit: what advantage do we gain from reciting and mentioning them? The author then addresses the first question, stating that people have two opinions. The first opinion, held by those who greatly venerate these unknown words, claims that the ancient practitioners, through intense spiritual exercises, had pure, strong, and overpowering spirits revealed to them, which then dictated the incantations and recitations to them. The second opinion is cut off in the text, but it begins with 'that good assumption requires that those unknown words...', likely arguing for some inherent value or caution. The passage ends abruptly.

Incantations: Known Words and Their Effect
The author divides incantations and explains the mechanism of known words.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
The soul's influence grows with knowledge of planetary attributes.

Guided Path
1

Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Note that the author first states the fifth type and its two divisions.
The author gives his own opinion for known words.
2
Identify the two divisions
Find the phrase that divides incantations into known and unknown words.
3
Understand the mechanism of known words
Notice the causal chain: knowledge of planetary attributes leads to better enumeration of perfection attributes, which increases soul influence, attraction to the planet's spirit, and ultimately the ability to effect.
This is a psychological-cosmological explanation.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider that the author's view ties incantation effectiveness to the reciter's knowledge, not just the words themselves.

النوع الخامس من الأمور المعتبرة في هذا الباب : قراءة الرقي . واعلم أنها على قسمين : منها : كلمات معلومة . ومنها : كلمات غير معلومة . أما الكلمات المعلومة . فالحق عندي : أن الإنسان كلما كان وقوفه على صفات الكوكب المعين أكثر ، وعلمه بأفعاله المخصوصة أتم ، كانت قدرته على إحصاء صفات كماله أتم ، وانفعال نفسه عند ذكر تلك الصفات أتم وكلما كان ذلك الانفعال أكمل ، كان انجذاب نفسه إلى روح ذلك الكوكب أكمل ، فكانت قدرته على التأثير أقوى . بحثان : وأما الرقى التي لا يفهم منها شيء ، ولا يحصل الوقوف على معانيها فقيها الأول : إن الذي نظم تلك الكلمات ، ورتبها في أول الأمر . من كان ؟ والثاني : إنه أي فائدة لنا في قراءتها وذكرها ؟ فنقول : أما المقام الأول . فللناس فيه قولان : الأول : وهم الذين يبالغون في تعظيم تلك الكلمات المجهولة ، الذين يقولون : إن المتقدمين لما بالغوا في الرياضات انكشفت لهم الأرواح الطاهرة القوية ، القاهرة . فألقت عليهم العزائم والرقي . والقول الثاني : إن حسن الظن يقتضي أن تلك الكلمات المجهولة . تدل على صفات ذلك الكوكب ، أو على صفات ذلك الروح بلغة غريبة أجنبية . والمقصود من قراءتها غير معلوم ، لأن من قرأ شيئاً ، ولا يعرف معناه ، وكان عظيم الاعتقاد فيه ، فإنه يحصل في قلبه خوف وفزع ، فيكون انفعال نفسه أتم وأقوى ، وذلك هو المقصود . فهذا ما عندنا في هذا الباب
The fifth type of matters considered in this chapter: reading incantations. Know that they are of two divisions: some are known words, and some are unknown words. As for the known words, the truth in my view is that the more a person's knowledge of the attributes of a particular planet is extensive, and his knowledge of its specific actions is more complete, his ability to enumerate its attributes of perfection is more complete, and the influence of his soul upon mentioning those attributes is more complete. And the more complete that influence is, the more complete is his soul's attraction to the spirit of that planet, and thus his ability to effect is stronger. Two investigations: As for incantations from which nothing is understood and their meanings are not known, first: who composed those words and arranged them in the first instance? Second: what benefit is there for us in reciting and mentioning them? We say: As for the first station, people have two sayings: First: those who exaggerate in magnifying those unknown words say that when the predecessors exaggerated in spiritual exercises, the pure, strong, and overpowering spirits were unveiled to them and they cast upon them the incantations and spells. The second saying: good opinion requires that those unknown words indicate the attributes of that planet, or the attributes of that spirit, in a strange foreign language. The purpose of reciting them is unknown, because the person who recites something without understanding its meaning while having great belief in it, fear and terror occur in his heart, so his soul's influence is more complete and stronger, and that is the purpose. This is what we have in this chapter.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth type of consideration: reading incantations (قراءة الرقي). The author first divides incantations into two categories: known words and unknown words. For known words, the author gives his opinion: the more one knows the attributes and actions of a specific planet, the more his soul is affected by mentioning them, leading to a stronger attraction to the spirit of that planet and thus greater power. For unknown words, the author raises two inquiries (بحثان): first, who originally composed these words? Second, what benefit do we gain from reciting them? In response to the first inquiry, he presents two views among people: one view holds that the predecessors, through intense spiritual exercises, had spirits reveal these incantations to them. The other view suggests that the unknown words are descriptions of planetary or spiritual attributes in a foreign language. The author then addresses the second inquiry by explaining that reciting unknown words with strong belief induces fear and awe in the heart, which intensifies the soul's influence, and that is the intended benefit. The passage concludes with 'This is what we have in this chapter.' The author's tone is descriptive, explaining the rationale behind incantation practices.

Key Terms
الرقي (incantations)
كلمات معلومة (known words)
كلمات غير معلومة (unknown words)
الأرواح (spirits)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what happens when a person has more knowledge of a planet's attributes?
A) His ability to effect becomes weaker
B) His soul's influence becomes more complete
C) He can control the planet
D) He stops using incantations

Key Takeaway
The effect of known incantations depends on the reciter's knowledge of planetary attributes and the resulting attraction to the planet's spirit.

?

The Two Inquiries About Unknown Incantations
The author addresses two inquiries about unknown incantations and their benefit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two inquiries (origin and benefit) regarding unknown incantations and the two opinions about their origin.

Core Idea
Unknown incantations induce fear, which strengthens the soul's influence.

The author now turns to incantations composed of unknown words. He raises two questions: Who first composed them? What benefit do we get? He presents two views on the first question and then explains the benefit through the psychological effect of reciting with strong belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the two inquiries
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note the two questions and the response.
The passage begins with 'بحثان' (two investigations).
2
Identify the two questions
Find the first question about the originator of the words, and the second about the benefit.
3
Understand the two opinions on the first question
The first opinion attributes the words to spirits revealed through spiritual exercises. The second suggests they describe planetary attributes in a foreign language.
The author does not choose between them.
4
Grasp the answer to the second question
The benefit is that reciting unknown words with belief causes fear, which intensifies the soul's influence.
This is the author's own explanation.

Offerings and Bloodshed: The Sixth Type
The author describes the sixth type of talismanic action: offerings and bloodshed, with the requirement of burning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the practice of making offerings and bloodshed in talismanic traditions and the necessity of burning the sacrifice.

Core Idea
Offerings require burning to unlock their benefit — a practice rooted in ancient law.

In this passage, the author examines a specific type of action considered in talismanic arts: the offering of animals and the shedding of blood. He explains that practitioners believe such sacrifices must be burned to achieve full benefit, a practice that persisted as a law until the time of the Prophet Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the key elements: offerings, bloodshed, burning.
Notice the author's tone of wonderment.
2
Identify the practitioners' doctrine
The passage states 'the doctrine of the owners of talismans' and explains their view on burning. Identify the reason given for burning the animals.
Burning is said to bring 'complete benefit'.
3
Reflect on the author's conclusion
The author notes that the benefit is not rationally known, yet experiments have indicated it. Ask yourself: what does this reveal about the author's approach to empirical evidence?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع السادس من الأعمال المعتبرة في هذا الباب : اتخاذ القرابين ، وإراقة الدماء . واعلم : أن مذهب أصحاب الطلسمات: أن تلك الحيوانات إذا ذبحت ، فإنه يجب إحراقها بالنار ، حتى يحصل كمال النفع بها . وهذه هي الشريعة الباقية إلى زمان مجيء رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. وهو أمر عجيب . فإنه لا يُعرف وجه المنفعة في الذبح ، ولا يدري أيضاً وجه المنفعة في ذلك الإحراق . وبالجملة : فهذه الأشياء يصعب وجه النفع بها ، إلا أنه لما دلت التجارب عليها وجب المصير إليها .
The sixth type of actions considered in this chapter: making offerings and shedding blood. Know that the doctrine of the owners of talismans is that when those animals are slaughtered, they must be burned with fire so that complete benefit is obtained from them. And this is the remaining law until the time of the coming of the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace. And it is a wondrous matter, for the benefit of slaughter is not known, nor is the benefit of that burning known. In summary: the benefit of these things is difficult, but since experiences have indicated them, it is necessary to resort to them.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth type of action: making offerings and shedding blood (اتخاذ القرابين وإراقة الدماء). The author states that according to the practitioners of talismans (أصحاب الطلسمات), when animals are slaughtered, they must be burned with fire to achieve complete benefit. The author remarks that this practice was the remaining law until the advent of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). He finds it wondrous because the benefit of neither the slaughter nor the burning is known. Nevertheless, he concludes that since experiments (التجارب) have indicated their efficacy, one must follow them. The author seems to be reporting the practice and its rationale without necessarily endorsing it.

Key Terms
القرابين (offerings)
إراقة الدماء (bloodshed)
الطلسمات (talismans)

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) They are left to rot

Key Takeaway
In talismanic practice, slaughtered animals must be burned for their benefit to be fully realized, a practice that persisted until prophetic times, accepted due to empirical evidence despite its unknown rationale.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Planetary Hours for Sunday
The author lists the planetary hours for Sunday.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the astrological assignment of planetary hours for Sunday as presented in the passage.

Core Idea
Each hour of Sunday is ruled by a planet in a fixed sequence.

In this passage, the author presents the seventh type of action: mentioning the names of spirits, which includes the astrologers' system of planetary hours. He provides the sequence for Sunday, showing which planet governs each hour. This lesson will walk you through that sequence and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once without analysis to get the flow.
Notice the author's straightforward listing style.
2
Identify the planetary sequence
List the planets in the order they appear for each hour from the first to the thirteenth hour.
The sequence repeats after the seventh hour.
3
Reflect on the pattern
Observe that the seven planets cycle through the hours, starting with the sun for the first hour.
This pattern likely applies to other days, but the passage only covers Sunday.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع السابع من الأعمال المعتبرة في هذا الباب : ذكر أسماء الأوراح : واعلم : أن المنجمين ذكروا : أن الساعة الأولى من يوم الأحد للشمس .. والثانية للزهرة. والثالثة لعطارد . والرابعة للقمر . والخامسة لزحل . والسادسة للمشتري . والسابعة للمريخ. ثم تعود الثامنة إلى الشمس والتاسعة للزهرة . والعاشرة لعطارد . والحادية عشر للقمر. والثانية عشر لزحل . والثالثة عشر للمريخ.
The seventh type of actions considered in this chapter: mentioning the names of spirits. Know that the astrologers mentioned that the first hour of Sunday belongs to the sun, the second to Venus, the third to Mercury, the fourth to the moon, the fifth to Saturn, the sixth to Jupiter, the seventh to Mars. Then the eighth returns to the sun, the ninth to Venus, the tenth to Mercury, the eleventh to the moon, the twelfth to Saturn, the thirteenth to Mars.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh type of action: mentioning the names of spirits (ذكر أسماء الأرواح). The author reports that the astrologers (المنجمين) have assigned each hour of the day to a specific planet. He gives the sequence starting from Sunday: the first hour belongs to the sun, then Venus, Mercury, moon, Saturn, Jupiter, Mars, and then the cycle repeats. The list continues for thirteen hours, which is likely the daylight hours. The passage is purely enumerative, providing the planetary hour correspondences.

المنجمون
الساعات

The Sixth Type: Sacrifices and Burning
Describes the sixth type: sacrifices and burning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the talisman practitioners' practice of animal sacrifice and burning, and the author's skeptical stance on its rational basis.

Core Idea
Sacrifice in talismanry: an ancient practice whose benefit is known only by experience.

This passage describes the sixth type of talismanic work: offering sacrifices and burning them. The author explains the practitioners' method and his own astonishment at its lack of rational benefit.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on sacrifices
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the author's description of the method and his comment on its obscurity.
2
Reflect on the author's stance
Consider why the author finds this practice 'astonishing' and how he justifies its use based on experience.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The sixth type of works considered in this chapter: taking sacrifices and spilling blood. Know that the doctrine of the talisman practitioners: that when those animals are slaughtered, it is necessary to burn them with fire, so that complete benefit is obtained from them. And this is the remaining law until the time of the coming of the Messenger of God (peace be upon him). And it is an astonishing matter. For the aspect of benefit in slaughtering is not known, nor is the aspect of benefit in that burning known either. In short: these things are difficult in terms of the aspect of benefit, except that since experiences have indicated them, it is necessary to resort to them. The seventh type of works considered in this chapter: mentioning the names of the spirits. Know that the astrologers mentioned: that the first hour of Sunday is for the sun, the second for Venus, the third for Mercury, the fourth for the moon, the fifth for Saturn, the sixth for Jupiter, the seventh for Mars. Then the eighth returns to the sun, the ninth for Venus, the tenth for Mercury, the eleventh for the moon, the twelfth for Saturn, the thirteenth for Jupiter, the fourteenth for Mars. Then the fifteenth hour returns to the sun, then the sixteenth hour returns to Venus, the seventeenth for Mercury, the eighteenth for the moon, the nineteenth for Saturn, the twentieth for Jupiter, the twenty-first for Mars, and the twenty-second for the sun, and the twenty-third for Venus, and the twenty-fourth for Mercury. And the twenty-four hours have been completed. Consequently, the first hour of Monday fell to the moon. And by this arrangement, the knowledge of the lords of the hours is obtained in the complete week. And when you know this, it becomes apparent that each hour has a specific lord. So it is not unlikely that from the total spirit of the specific planet there are generated celestial spirits that are its branches and results. And each of them has a greater specificity with a specific hour from those hours. Then the practitioners of magic and talismans sometimes claim knowledge of the lords of the hours and knowledge of their names, so they consider in magic the observance of the lords of the hours in which the performance of those acts is desired. And the eighth type: that the astrologers attribute each town to a specific zodiac sign and to a specific planet. And it is necessary in magical works to consider those states. These are matters that whoever undertakes this craft must not be heedless of, so that his works may be closer to correctness and further from error. And God is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage enumerates three types of practices considered by astrologers and talisman practitioners in the chapter on talismans. The author describes each type in a neutral, factual manner without explicit approval or disapproval. The sixth type involves sacrifices and bloodshed: the animals must be slaughtered and then burned for full benefit. The author finds this strange since the benefit is unknown, but notes that empirical experience has led to its adoption. The seventh type concerns mentioning the names of spirits and the assignment of planets to the hours of the day. The author provides a detailed list of the planetary hours for Sunday, showing the sequence of planets in a 24-hour cycle. He explains how the first hour of Monday is determined by continuing the cycle (the moon). From this, it follows that each hour has a specific planetary lord, and from the total spirit of a planet, subordinate spirits are generated. Magicians claim knowledge of these lords and their names, and they consider them in their rites. The eighth type involves astrologers attributing each town to a specific zodiac sign and planet, and magical works must take these associations into account. The author concludes that anyone practicing this craft must be aware of all these factors to attain correctness.

Key Takeaway

?

?

The Seventh Type: Lords of the Hours and Celestial Spirits
Enumerates the seventh type: planetary hours and spirit names.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the astrologers' system of planetary hours and how talisman practitioners invoke spirits associated with each hour.

Core Idea
Each hour of the week is ruled by a planet, generating specific celestial spirits.

The seventh type concerns the names of spirits and planetary hours. The author details the 24-hour cycle starting Sunday, showing how the first hour of Monday is derived. He then explains how from the total spirit of a planet, subordinate spirits are generated, which magicians invoke at specific hours.

Guided Path
1
Read the planetary hour list
Read the Arabic passage detailing the hours for Sunday and the subsequent cycle. Follow the pattern of planet assignments.
The order is: Sun, Venus, Mercury, Moon, Saturn, Jupiter, Mars; then repeat.
2
Understand the derivation of Monday's first hour
Notice that after the 24th hour, the cycle continues so that Monday's first hour is ruled by the Moon. This demonstrates the system.
3
Grasp the generation of spirits
Read the part about the total spirit generating celestial spirits, each with specific hour association. Magicians claim knowledge of these spirits for their rites.
This links astrology to talismanic practice.

Principles of Astrological Magic: Planetary Attribution
Outlines the first condition for astrological magic: requiring a specific planet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the text describes the first condition for astrological magic operations, which is attributing each work to a specific planet, and why it is important to recognize this as a description of forbidden practices.

Core Idea
Astrological magic demands each operation be tied to a specific planet — a false and prohibited belief.

This passage comes from a volume discussing astrological magic. While the text may appear instructional, it is likely presented either as a description of what practitioners claim or as a warning. In this lesson, we will examine the first condition: that every magical operation must be attributed to a particular planet. The example of Saturn illustrates how such attributions are made.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the passage carefully, noting the key terms like 'كوكب معين' and 'زحل'. Try to understand the structure: it begins by stating a general rule, then gives a specific example.
Pay attention to the footnote markings and brackets indicating uncertain readings.
2
Understand the first condition
Identify that the first condition for planetary magic is that each desired work must be 'مضافاً إلى كوكب معين' — attributed to a specific planet.
The example given is Saturn for works of separation and hatred.
3
Note the practical instructions
Observe the astrological details: Saturn should be in certain houses or aspects, and the Moon should be connected or conjunct.
These specifics show the complexity of such beliefs.
4
Reflect on the Islamic stance
Consider that this passage is describing a practice that is forbidden in Islam. The author may be listing principles to refute them later. Recognize the importance of distinguishing between description and endorsement.
If studying this text, always keep in mind the overall purpose of the work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في التنبيه على أصول أخرى يجب مراعاتها في هذه الأعمال البروج. اعلم : أن تلك الأصول إما أن تكون معتبرة في الكواكب، أو في (أ) أما في الكواكب: ففيه شرائط: الأول: اعلم: أن كل واحد من هذه الأعمال المطلوبة في السحر، لا بد وأن يكون مضافاً إلى كوكب معين. النجومي فجميع أحوال الفرقة والبغض مضافة إلى زحل. فإذا أردت [هذا العمل؟] فاعمل وزحل في أحد بيتيه: الجدي [أو الدلو؟] والدلو أقوى، أو في تثليثهما، أو تسديسها. ويكون القمر متصلاً به من أحد هذه المواضع، أيها كان. أو مقارناً له، وهو الجيد الذي لا شيء بعده. وليكن الطالع...
In warning about other principles that must be observed in these zodiacal works. Know: that these principles either apply to the planets, or in (a) As for the planets: it has conditions: The first: Know: that each one of these desired works in magic must be attributed to a specific planet. The astrologer: all states of separation and hatred are attributed to Saturn. So if you want [this work?], work while Saturn is in one of its two houses: Capricorn [or Aquarius?] and Aquarius is stronger, or in their trine, or their sextile. And let the Moon be connected to it from one of these positions, whichever it may be. Or conjunct with it, and that is excellent beyond which nothing is better. And let the ascendant be...
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage appears to be part of a larger discussion on the principles (أصول) that must be observed in astrological magic (السحر). The author first announces that these principles are either considered in relation to the planets or something else (the text breaks). Then, focusing on the planets, he lists conditions. The first condition states that each magical operation must be attributed to a specific planet. He gives an example: all workings of separation and hatred are attributed to Saturn. He then gives practical instructions: when performing such a work, Saturn should be in one of its two houses (Capricorn or Aquarius, with Aquarius being stronger), or in trine or sextile aspect to its own houses. Additionally, the Moon should be connected to Saturn from one of these positions, or ideally in conjunction with it, which is described as the best configuration. The passage ends abruptly with 'Let the ascendant be...', indicating further conditions follow.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This passage teaches how to perform astrological magic.
Correction: The passage is likely describing principles of astrological magic for the purpose of refutation or warning, not as instruction. In Islamic theology, such practices are forbidden.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Where in your own life do you look for signs or omens from creation—like checking horoscopes or reading into coincidences—instead of placing your trust fully in Allah?
