Two Types of Planetary Conjunction
States two types of conjunction: real and by alignment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two types of conjunction between planets and fixed stars and why real conjunction is considered stronger.

Core Idea
Planetary conjunction has two forms: real and by alignment, with real being more powerful.

In talismanic astrology, the conjunction of planets with fixed stars is not a single phenomenon. The author distinguishes between actual physical proximity and mere visual alignment. Understanding this distinction is crucial for assessing the strength of astrological effects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation to grasp the author's classification.
Notice the use of 'أما' (as for) to introduce each type.
2
Identify the two types
The passage explicitly states two types: real (في الحقيقة) and by alignment (في المسامتة). Understand what each means.
Real conjunction occurs when the planet is on the path of fixed stars; alignment when the fixed star is far from the orbit.
3
Compare their strength
The author concludes that the first type (real) is stronger. Reflect on why physical proximity might have greater influence.
This distinction matters for talismanic practices.
4
Reflect on implications
Consider why this classification is important for talismanic astrology. How would one determine which type applies?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن اتصال السيارات بالثوابت على قسمين : تارة في الحقيقة : وأخرى في المسامتة . أما الحقيقة : فهي في الكواكب التي تكون على ممر هذه السيارات . وأما الذي تكون بحسب المسامتات فهو ما إذا كان الكوكب الثابت : بعيداً عن عمر هذه السيارات. وأنت تعلم أن الأول أقوى .
Know that the conjunction of the planets with the fixed stars is of two types: sometimes in reality, and sometimes in alignment. As for reality: it is concerning the planets that are on the path of these planets. As for what is by alignment: it is when the fixed star is far from the orbit of these planets. And you know that the first is stronger.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage defines two types of conjunction between planets and fixed stars relevant to talismans. The first is real conjunction (fi al-haqiqah), which occurs when a planet is physically on the path of the fixed stars. The second is alignment (al-musamatah), which happens when the fixed star is far from the planet's orbit but aligned along the same line of sight. The author notes that the real conjunction is stronger in effect.

This passage explains the third condition for creating a talisman. Core Idea
Place the planet of need in the ascendant for power.

This lesson presents the fourth condition for talisman construction. It specifies that the planet representing the desired outcome must be placed in the ascendant at the starting time, while other helpful planets occupy the remaining angular houses. Additionally, if that planet also holds essential dignities like bound, face, triplicity, and other lots, the talisman becomes even more effective.

Three Levels of Planetary Love and Hate
Classifies planetary love and hate into three levels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three levels of planetary love and hate—innate, based on house aspects, and from mixtures—and why it matters for astrological practice.

Core Idea
Planetary friendships and enmities have three distinct causes, from innate nature to accidental mixtures.

In astrological theory, planets are not neutral toward each other; they have affinities and hostilities. This condition explains that these relationships come in three types, ranging from deep, inherent ties to more superficial ones. Understanding these levels helps astrologers know how to strengthen or weaken planetary influences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Notice the three-part classification (أعلاها, أوسطها, أدناها).
2
Identify the three levels
Spot each level: highest (innate nature), middle (house aspects), lowest (mixtures). Notice the examples given for the highest level.
The examples show Sun-Saturn hate and Sun-Jupiter love as innate.
3
Understand the practical advice
The last sentence gives a rule: when using a planet, remove its enemies to avoid weakness. This connects the classification to actual practice.
4
Reflect on the hierarchy
Consider why innate nature is considered highest, and mixtures lowest. The text does not elaborate, but you can infer that innate is strongest, mixtures weakest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرط السادس : إن الكواكب بعضها متحابة ، وبعضها متباغضة ، والحب والبغض على أقسام ثلاثة : فأعلاها : أن يكون بحب الطبيعة الذاتية . مثل : البغض الذي بين الشمس وزحل ، ومثل : المحبة التي بين الشمس وبين المشتري ، وأوسطها : الواقعة بحسب مناظرات البيوت وأدناها : الحاصلة بسبب الممازجات فإذا استعنت بكوكب ، وبالغت في تقويته ، فاسقط عنه أعداءه . لأن نظر الضد : يوجب الضعف والفتور .
The sixth condition: Planets are some loving and some hating, and love and hate are of three types: The highest: that which is by innate nature, such as the hate between the Sun and Saturn, and like the love between the Sun and Jupiter. The middle: that which occurs according to the aspects of houses. The lowest: that which results from mixtures. So if you seek help from a planet and you exaggerate in strengthening it, then drop its enemies from it. Because the opposition's aspect causes weakness and languor.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This condition explains planetary affinities and hostilities. Love (mahabbah) and hate (bughd) among planets are categorized into three levels: highest is based on inherent nature (e.g., Sun vs Saturn hate, Sun-Jupiter love), middle is based on house aspects (manazarat al-buyut), and lowest is from mixtures (mumazajat). When using a planet, one should avoid its enemies to prevent weakness from opposition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Planetary enmity is always based on personal will or temperament.
Correction: Enmity (and friendship) can be due to innate nature, but also house aspects and mixtures; it is not always a matter of personal disposition.

Planetary Rules for Excitement and Love Talismans
Enumeration of beneficial and harmful planets for excitement talismans.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which planets are recommended and which are avoided for excitement and love talismans.

Core Idea
Only benefic planets are used for love; malefics cause harm.

This lesson covers the first part of the seventh condition for talismans aimed at excitement (tahyiij) and love. The practitioner must choose planets carefully, starting with benefic ones and avoiding malefic ones. The passage lists the suitable and forbidden planets explicitly.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the lists
The passage gives two lists: planets to start with (Venus, Mercury, Jupiter, Sun) and planets to beware of (Mars, Saturn, Moon). Read carefully to distinguish them.
2
Understand the terms for planets
The Arabic names are used: الزهرة (Venus), عطارد (Mercury), المشتري (Jupiter), الشمس (Sun), المريخ (Mars), زحل (Saturn), القمر (Moon). Note that the Sun and Moon are included on opposite sides.
Sun is benefic here, Moon is malefic.
3
Ask why certain planets are selected
Reflect on the astrological associations: Venus and Jupiter are traditionally benefic, Mercury is associated with communication, Sun with vitality. Mars and Saturn are malefic, Moon with sleep/enmity.
This connects to broader astrological traditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرط السابع : قالوا : إذا أردت التهييج ، فعليك البدء بالزهرة وعطارد ، والمشتري والشمس، واحذر المريخ وزحل والقمر ، وقالوا أيضاً : الساعات الصالحة للحب : هي ساعات تلك الأربعة . وأما ساعات المريخ والقمر ، فلعقد النوم وساعات زحل فللعداوة والبغض وقالوا أيضاً : إن كانت المحبة على وفق العفة ، والصلاح ، فابتدىء بها في ساعة المشتري ، وإن كانت على وفق الفساد فابتدىء بها في ساعة الزهرة، وأما عقد اللسان وعقد النوم ففي ساعة عطارد .
The seventh condition: They said: If you want excitement, then start with Venus, Mercury, Jupiter, and the Sun, and beware of Mars, Saturn, and the Moon. And they also said: The suitable hours for love are the hours of those four. As for the hours of Mars and the Moon, for inducing sleep. And the hours of Saturn for enmity and hatred. And they also said: If the love is according to chastity and righteousness, then start with it in the hour of Jupiter. And if it is according to corruption, then start with it in the hour of Venus. Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This condition gives detailed guidelines for talismans aimed at excitement (tahyi) or love. The suitable planets are the benefics: Venus, Mercury, Jupiter, and Sun; malefics Mars, Saturn, Moon are to be avoided. Each set of planetary hours serves different purposes: the four benefics' hours are for love, Mars and Moon hours for sleep inducement, Saturn hours for enmity. Moreover, the moral nature of the desired love determines the planet: if chaste, use Jupiter's hour; if corrupt, use Venus's hour. Mercury is associated with binding the tongue and sleep.

الشرط السابع : قالوا : إذا أردت التهييج ، فعليك البدء بالزهرة وعطارد ، والمشتري والشمس، واحذر المريخ وزحل والقمر ، وقالوا أيضاً : الساعات الصالحة للحب : هي ساعات تلك الأربعة . وأما ساعات المريخ والقمر ، فلعقد النوم وساعات زحل فللعداوة والبغض وقالوا أيضاً : إن كانت المحبة على وفق العفة ، والصلاح ، فابتدىء بها في ساعة المشتري ، وإن كانت على وفق الفساد فابتدىء بها في ساعة الزهرة، وأما عقد اللسان وعقد النوم ففي ساعة عطارد .
The seventh condition: They said: If you want excitement, then start with Venus, Mercury, Jupiter, and the Sun, and beware of Mars, Saturn, and the Moon. And they also said: The suitable hours for love are the hours of those four. As for the hours of Mars and the Moon, for inducing sleep. And the hours of Saturn for enmity and hatred. And they also said: If the love is according to chastity and righteousness, then start with it in the hour of Jupiter. And if it is according to corruption, then start with it in the hour of Venus. As for the binding of the tongue and binding of sleep, in the hour of Mercury.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This condition gives detailed guidelines for talismans aimed at excitement (tahyi) or love. The suitable planets are the benefics: Venus, Mercury, Jupiter, and Sun; malefics Mars, Saturn, Moon are to be avoided. Each set of planetary hours serves different purposes: the four benefics' hours are for love, Mars and Moon hours for sleep inducement, Saturn hours for enmity. Moreover, the moral nature of the desired love determines the planet: if chaste, use Jupiter's hour; if corrupt, use Venus's hour. Mercury is associated with binding the tongue and sleep.

Core Idea
The ascendant must align with the planet's sign for maximum talismanic power.

This lesson introduces the eighth condition for talismanic operations, which concerns celestial timing and alignment. The author emphasizes that the ascendant should be in a house or sign where the relevant planet has strength and lot. He illustrates with the example of a love talisman, specifying Venus's day and hour. Understanding this condition helps practitioners maximize the effectiveness of their work.

Effects of Planetary Retrogradation on Talismans
Lists talismanic uses based on planetary retrogradation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how planetary retrogradation (ruju'at) determines the specific purpose of a talisman for each planet according to this text.

Core Idea
A planet's motion—retrograde or direct—dictates its talismanic function.

The ninth condition delves into the effects of planetary retrogradation on talismanic practices. The author provides specific instructions for Saturn, Jupiter, the Sun, and begins Venus. This lesson walks through these rules, highlighting how each planet's motion determines the talisman's purpose.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully to grasp the overall structure and content.
The passage is part of a longer list; focus on the pattern.
2
Identify the planets and their states
Notice the two states for each planet: for Saturn and Jupiter, retrograde vs. direct; for the Sun, free from malefics vs. malefic; for Venus, only retrograde is mentioned.
3
Note the talismanic purposes
For each planet and state, the text specifies a talisman purpose: separation, hatred, ruin, army rectification, meeting sultans, evil works, and (implied for Venus) likely something similar.
4
Reflect on the principle
Consider that retrogradation does not simply make a planet 'bad' or 'good'; it changes the nature of its influence, leading to different talismanic objectives.
This connects to the common misunderstanding about retrogradation.

Commentary
This condition discusses the effects of planetary retrogradation (ruju'at) on talismanic work. For each planet, retrograde versus direct motion indicates different purposes: Saturn retrograde for separation, direct for hatred; Jupiter retrograde for property ruin, direct for army betterment; Sun free from malefics for meeting rulers, malefic for evil deeds. Conditions for the Moon in Magical Operations (Part 2)
Lists eight prohibitions for the moon in magical practice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the remaining eight astrological conditions (sixth to thirteenth) that practitioners imposed on the moon for magical operations, and the reasoning behind each prohibition.

Core Idea
The moon's position and aspects determine its suitability for magic.

In this passage, the author continues enumerating the conditions required for the moon when performing magical operations. Each condition is a prohibition based on astrological symbolism: the moon's place in the zodiac, its aspects with planets like Saturn and Mercury, and its speed. As you read, note how each condition is justified by analogies or planetary characteristics. This reveals the elaborate framework that underlay medieval magical practices.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of all eight conditions.
2
Group the conditions by type
Note that some conditions concern the moon's position in the zodiac (beginnings/ends, specific signs), others concern its aspects with planets (Saturn, Mercury), and others its motion (ascending/descending, slow).
3
Analyze the reasoning
For each prohibition, identify the astrological rationale given (e.g., similarity to a man at the door, malefic planets, knots, etc.). This helps understand the logic of astrological magic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسادس : أن لا يكون صاعداً ولا هابطاً . والسابع : أن لا يكون في أوائل البروج ، ولا في أواخرها . أما الأوائل فلأنه يشبه الرجل الذي وضع رجله في الدار ، ولم يستقر فيها بعد ، وأما الأواخر فلأنه يشبه من قام ، ووصل إلى باب الدار ، ليخرج منها . وأيضاً : أواخر البروج : حدود النحوس . والثامن : أن لا يكون في مقابلة زحل ومقارنته وتربيعه وأنصاف تربعه لأنه كوكب نحس ، فيهون العمل . والتاسع : أن لا يكون مع الرأس والذنب ، لأنهما عقدتان . فكرهوا القمر في العقدة . ثم إن الذنب أردأ . والعاشر : أن لا يكون بطيء السير . لأن هذه الحالة تبطيء المقصود والحادي عشر : أن لا يكون في مقابلة عطارد ، ولا في مقارنته ، وذلك لأن القمر إذا اتصل بعطارد ، اتصالاً محموداً ، صارت حالة كل واحد منهما محمودة ، وأما إذا تقابلا ، أو تقارنا : تضادا ، فتضادت أحوالهما . والأحوال الإنسانية أكثرها متعلقة بعطارد ، ولا سيما هذه الأعمال السحرية ، فلا جرم وجب الاعتناء فيها بصلاح حال عطارد ، وأن لا يكون بينه وبين القمر اتصال رديء . والثاني عشر : يكره كون القمر في الميزان ، أو في العقرب . لأنهما برجا هبوط النيرين وهذا شرط واجب الرعاية . والثالث عشر : أن لا يكون القمر في سادس برج الأسد ، ولا في سادس برج الجوزاء ، وذلك لأن أحدهما بهبوط القمر ، والآخر ببيت زحل .
The sixth: that it (the moon) should not be ascending nor descending. The seventh: that it should not be in the beginnings of the signs nor in their ends. As for the beginnings, because it resembles a man who has placed his foot in the house but has not yet settled in it. And as for the ends, because it resembles one who has stood up and reached the door of the house to go out from it. Also: the ends of the signs are the boundaries of the malefics. The eighth: that it should not be in opposition, conjunction, or square with Saturn, nor in its semi-square, because it is a malefic planet, which makes the work weak. The ninth: that it should not be with the head and the tail (lunar nodes), because they are two knots. So they disliked the moon in the knot. Moreover, the tail is worse. The tenth: that it should not be slow in motion, because this state slows down the desired. The eleventh: that it should not be in opposition with Mercury nor in conjunction with it, because when the moon is connected with Mercury by a praiseworthy connection, the state of each of them becomes praiseworthy. But if they are in opposition or conjunction, they oppose each other, and their states oppose one another. Human affairs are mostly related to Mercury, especially these magical works. So necessarily, one must take care in them to improve Mercury's condition, and that there be no bad connection between it and the moon. The twelfth: it is disliked that the moon be in Libra or in Scorpio, because they are the signs of the fall of the two luminaries. This is a condition that must be observed. The thirteenth: that the moon should not be in the sixth of Leo nor in the sixth of Gemini, because one of them is the fall of the moon, and the other is the house of Saturn.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is a list of conditions that astrologers consider necessary for the moon when performing magical operations. It continues a previous enumeration. Each condition is expressed as a prohibition. The reasoning is based on astrological symbolism: the moon in the beginnings of signs is unstable, while in the ends it is about to leave. Conjunctions with Saturn weaken the work because Saturn is malefic. The lunar nodes are considered knots that impede. Opposition or conjunction with Mercury creates disharmony. Being in Libra or Scorpio is avoided because they are the signs of the fall of the moon and sun. The sixth of Leo and Gemini are also avoided due to the moon's fall and Saturn's house. The passage shows the elaborate astrological framework that underlay magical practices.

Misconception: The author endorses these conditions as valid for magical operations.
Correction: The author is merely describing the beliefs of astrologers-magicians, not necessarily endorsing them. Later in the text, he interjects a critical remark.

Moon-Planet Conjunctions and the Author's Critique
Lists planetary conjunctions with the moon and the author's critical objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the traditional magical associations of moon-planet conjunctions and the author's rational objection based on the moon's phase.

Core Idea
The moon's phase matters: conjunctions with the sun render it invisible and unsuitable for magical work.

This passage presents a catalog of magical uses for each planetary conjunction with the moon, followed by a critical interjection. The author points out a fundamental astronomical flaw: when the moon conjoins the sun, it is in its new moon phase (mahq) and thus unfit for any operation. This lesson explores both the system and the critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to get an overview. Notice the list format and the interruption with 'وأقول'.
The passage is in two voices: the traditional claims and the author's critique.
2
List the planets and their effects
Write down each planet (Saturn, Jupiter, Mars, Sun, Venus, Mercury, Lunar Node) and what the tradition says they are used for.
The effects range from destruction to prestige to love.
3
Analyze the author's objection
Focus on the sentence 'وأقول: هذا فيه نظر' and the following explanation. Why does the author say the moon is unsuitable? What astronomical fact does he use?
The moon is in mahq (new moon) during conjunction with the sun, meaning it is invisible.
4
Reflect on the critique's scope
Does the objection apply only to the sun conjunction? Or does it undermine the whole list? Consider that all conjunctions involve the moon, but only the sun conjunction causes invisibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثاني من اعتبار حال القمر : الأحوال المتعلقة بقران الكوكب مع القمر : فنقول : إذا كان القمر على قرآن زحل : يعمل فيه لهلاك الأعداء . وعلى قرآن المشتري يعمل فيه للسلاطين والجاه والتجارة . وعلى قران المريخ لفتح الحصون والقلاع، ولقاء الجند والأمراء والكتب لهم . وعلى قران الشمس للجاه والسلطان . وأقول : هذا فيه نظر . لأنه في هذه الحالة يكون في المحاق ، وهو لا يصلح لعمل . قال : وعلى قران الزهرة لعمل النير نجات والعطوف والخواتيم والطلمسات. وعلى قران عطارد للعطف ، ولقاء الكتاب . وعلى قران الرأس لهلاك الأعداء ، والفرقة والبغض ، وما أشبه ذلك .
The second type concerning the condition of the moon: the states related to the conjunction of a planet with the moon. We say: If the moon is in conjunction with Saturn, one works with it for the destruction of enemies. And in conjunction with Jupiter, one works with it for rulers, prestige, and trade. And in conjunction with Mars, for the conquest of fortresses and castles, and for meeting soldiers, commanders, and letters for them. And in conjunction with the Sun, for prestige and sultanate. And I say: This requires consideration, because in this state it (the moon) is in the new moon phase, and it is not suitable for work. He said: And in conjunction with Venus, for making talismans, amulets, rings, and sigils. And in conjunction with Mercury, for love and for meeting scribes. And in conjunction with the Head (lunar node) for the destruction of enemies, separation, hatred, and the like.

Commentary
This passage presents the second type of considerations: the effects of planetary conjunctions with the moon. The author first lists the traditional beliefs: each conjunction yields specific results for magical operations. Then the author interjects a critical remark ('وأقول: هذا فيه نظر'). His objection is based on a simple astronomical fact: when the moon is in conjunction with the sun, it is in its invisible phase (المحاق), which makes it unsuitable for any work. This is a rational critique grounded in observable reality. Then the passage continues to list further conjunctions with Venus, Mercury, and the lunar head, but this time prefaced with 'قال', possibly quoting another authority. The author's objection stands as a challenge to the entire framework.

The Moon’s Magical Effects by Zodiac Sign
Enumeration of moon’s effects per zodiac sign

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reported magical effects of the moon in various zodiac signs according to the third type of lunar considerations.

Core Idea
The moon’s sign and planetary connection determine its alleged magical power.

This passage presents the third type of lunar considerations: the moon’s position in the zodiac signs and its connection to specific planets. For each sign-planet combination, practitioners claim a particular effect, from love talismans to binding tongues. The author reports these without endorsement, as indicated by the closing phrase.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the pattern: if the moon is in sign X, connected to planet Y, it is suitable for effect Z.
Notice the repetition of 'إن كان في ... متصلاً بـ ... صلح لـ'
2
List the six signs with their planets and effects
Create a mental or written table of the six combinations: (Aries, Mars) for love/hate talismans, (Taurus, Venus) for meeting authorities, (Gemini, Mercury) for binding tongues, (Cancer, no planet) for affection, (Leo, Sun) for provocation/affection, and (Virgo, Mercury) for seeking work.
Cancer is the only sign without a mentioned planet; the effect is simply 'affection'.
3
Analyze the closing phrase
Examine the phrase 'إلى آخر ما ذكره أصحاب هذه الأعمال'. This indicates the author is only summarizing a longer list from practitioners, not inventing or endorsing these claims.
This frames the passage as a report, not a prescription.
4
Consider the author’s stance
Reflect on whether the author believes these effects are real. The lack of any objection or affirmation suggests he is merely documenting beliefs held by others, possibly for critical analysis elsewhere.
This aligns with the common misunderstanding that the author endorses these.

النوع الثالث من اعتبار حال القمر : الأحوال المتعلقة بكونه في البروج : إذا كان القمر في الحمل ، متصلاً بالمريخ ؛ صلح لنيـرنـجـات الحب والبغض ، بحسب اختلاف أحوال الكواكب المنضمة إليه . وإن كان في الثور ، متصلاً بالزهرة : صلح للقاء السلاطين والجند . وإن كان في الجوزاء متصلاً بعطارد : صلح لعقد اللسان ، وللمنع من الإباق . وإن كان في السرطان : صلح للعطف . وإن كان في الأسد متصلاً بالشمس : صلح للتهيج والعطف . وإن كان في السنبلة متصلاً بعطارد : صلح لطلب العمل والتفويض . إلى آخر ما ذكره أصحاب هذه الأعمال .
The third type concerning the condition of the moon: the states related to its being in the signs. If the moon is in Aries, connected to Mars, it is suitable for talismans of love and hatred, according to the varying states of the planets joined to it. And if it is in Taurus, connected to Venus, it is suitable for meeting sultans and soldiers. And if it is in Gemini, connected to Mercury, it is suitable for binding the tongue and preventing running away. And if it is in Cancer, it is suitable for affection. And if it is in Leo, connected to the Sun, it is suitable for provocation and affection. And if it is in Virgo, connected to Mercury, it is suitable for seeking work and delegation. Up to the end of what the practitioners of these works have mentioned.

Commentary
This passage gives the third type of considerations: the moon's position in each zodiac sign when connected to a particular planet. For each combination, the moon is deemed effective for a specific purpose: talismans for love/hate in Aries-Mars, meeting authorities in Taurus-Venus, binding the tongue in Gemini-Mercury, affection in Cancer, provocation/affection in Leo-Sun, and seeking work in Virgo-Mercury. The listing ends with 'إلى آخر ما ذكره أصحاب هذه الأعمال', indicating the author is only summarizing. He does not add his own objection here, but the critical tone from the previous section may carry over.

The Moon in the Zodiac Signs for Talismanic Works
Enumeration of moon's zodiac positions with talismanic uses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the moon's position in each zodiac sign, combined with specific planetary conjunctions, determines the suitability for various talismanic purposes.

Core Idea
The moon's zodiac sign and planet conjunction dictate talismanic outcomes.

This passage from al-Matalib al-'Aliyah presents a detailed astrological system used in talismanic magic. It specifies for each of the twelve zodiac signs the appropriate talismanic operation when the moon is in that sign and conjunct a particular planet. This showcases the intricate interplay of lunar and planetary positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get a complete overview of the twelve zodiac signs and their associated planets and talismanic purposes.
Notice the repeated phrase 'صلح لـ' (suitable for) which introduces each purpose.
2
Identify the planet-sun connections
For each sign, note which planet is mentioned (e.g., Mars for Aries, Venus for Taurus). Notice that some planets repeat across signs.
Mars, Venus, Mercury, Sun, Jupiter, Saturn appear multiple times.
3
Group by talismanic purpose
Group the signs by the type of talismanic operation: love/hatred, meetings, controlling speech, affection, profit, reconciliation, or harm.
For example, Aries and Scorpio both involve Mars but different purposes.
4
Reflect on the system's logic
Consider how the author's system assigns specific effects to each sign-planet pair, reflecting a coherent astrological framework.
This shows the sophistication of Islamic talismanic traditions.

النوع الثالث من اعتبار حال القمر :
الأحوال المتعلقة بكونه في البروج :
إذا كان القمر في الحمل ، متصلاً بالمريخ ؛ صلح لنيرنجات الحب والبغض ، بحسب اختلاف أحوال الكواكب المنضمة إليه . وإن كان في الثور ، متصلاً بالزهرة : صلح للقاء السلاطين والجند . وإن كان في الجوزاء متصلاً بعطارد : صلح لعقد اللسان ، وللمنع من الإباق .
وإن كان في السرطان : صلح للعطف . وإن كان في الأسد متصلاً بالشمس : صلح للتهيج والعطف . وإن كان في السنبلة متصلاً بعطارد : صلح لعمل الربح في المكاسب ، والزيادة في المال، وإن كان في الميزان متصلاً بالزهرة صلح للعطف المبني على عمل النار والهواء . وإن كان في العقرب متصلا بالمريخ : صلح للعطوف النارية والمائية . وإن كان في القوس متصلا بالمشتري : صلح لإزالة الوحشة ، وتحصيل الصلح . وإن كان في الجدي متصلا بزحل : صلح لأن تكتب فيه الكتب المدفونة في مقابر اليهود ، للفرقة والبغض . وإن كان في الدلو ، متصلاً بزحل : صلح لما ذكرناه في الجدي . وإن كان في الحوت متصلاً بالمشتري : صلح للعطف
The third type of consideration of the state of the moon: the conditions related to it being in the zodiac signs. If the moon is in Aries, connected to Mars: it is suitable for talismans of love and hatred, according to the different states of the planets joined to it. And if it is in Taurus, connected to Venus: it is suitable for meeting sultans and troops. And if it is in Gemini, connected to Mercury: it is suitable for tying the tongue and preventing running away. And if it is in Cancer: suitable for affection. And if it is in Leo, connected to the Sun: suitable for agitation and affection. And if it is in Virgo, connected to Mercury: suitable for making profit in earnings and increase in wealth. And if it is in Libra, connected to Venus: suitable for affection based on the work of fire and air. And if it is in Scorpio, connected to Mars: suitable for fiery and watery amulets. And if it is in Sagittarius, connected to Jupiter: suitable for removing estrangement and achieving reconciliation. And if it is in Capricorn, connected to Saturn: suitable for writing books buried in Jewish cemeteries, for separation and hatred. And if it is in Aquarius, connected to Saturn: suitable for what we mentioned in Capricorn. And if it is in Pisces, connected to Jupiter: suitable for affection.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage lists the third type of lunar consideration: the moon's position in each of the twelve zodiac signs along with its connection to a specific planet. For each sign, it states what kind of talismanic work is suitable. For example, Aries with Mars is for love/hate talismans; Taurus with Venus for meeting authorities; Gemini with Mercury for controlling speech and preventing escape; Cancer alone for affection; Leo with Sun for agitation and affection; Virgo with Mercury for profit; Libra with Venus for affection via fire and air; Scorpio with Mars for fiery and watery amulets; Sagittarius with Jupiter for reconciliation; Capricorn with Saturn for writing harmful books buried in Jewish cemeteries for separation and hatred; Aquarius with Saturn like Capricorn; Pisces with Jupiter for affection. The passage shows a detailed system of astrological correspondences used in talismanic magic.

Days Strengthened by Lunar Planetary Conjunctions
States which days are strengthened based on the moon's planetary conjunction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which day each planetary conjunction of the moon strengthens talismanic work, as per the fourth type of lunar conditions.

Core Idea
Each day has a specific planet whose conjunction with the moon empowers work.

This passage presents the fourth type of lunar conditions: the days of the week on which certain planetary conjunctions with the moon strengthen talismanic operations. Each day is paired with a specific planet—from the Sun on Sunday to Saturn on Saturday. Understanding this correspondence is essential for timing ritual work.

Guided Path

Both Monday and Friday are paired with Venus. This is unusual.

4

This short passage presents the fourth type: the days of the week on which talismanic work becomes stronger, based on which planet the moon is connected to. It assigns each day a planetary ruler: Sunday-Sun, Monday-Venus, Tuesday-Mars, Wednesday-Mercury, Thursday-Jupiter, Friday-Venus (again), Saturday-Saturn. The moon's connection to that planet on that day strengthens the work. Note that Monday and Friday both attribute to Venus, which may indicate a textual variation or intentional repetition.

First Condition for Talismanic Work: Choosing the Ascendant Sign and House
Explains the first condition and gives a marriage example with planetary ray effects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first condition for talismanic work: selecting a zodiac sign and house compatible with the desired outcome, and see how planetary rays affect the result.

Core Idea
The right sign and house are essential; planetary rays then determine the strength of the outcome.

This passage introduces the first condition for talismanic work: the ascendant must be a sign compatible with the work and a house suitable for it. Using marriage as an example, it then explains how the qualities of the sign and the rays of the planets Saturn and Venus influence the success or weakness of the intended purpose. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once. Notice how the author first states the condition, then gives an example.
Pay attention to the terms for signs, houses, and planetary rays.
2
Identify the first condition
Find the sentence that states the first condition: making the ascendant a sign compatible with the work and a house suitable for it.
The condition is general; the example illustrates it.
3
Follow the marriage example
The example uses marriage to show how the seventh house and its sign (Capricorn or Aquarius) are evaluated. Note the effects of Saturn and Venus rays on each case.
Capricorn is unsuitable; Saturn nullifies, Venus gives weakness, both increase weakness. Aquarius with Venus gives strength.
4
Reflect on the logic
Think about why sign qualities (like cold/dry) and planetary rays matter. The combination determines the outcome's strength.
This shows a complex astrological reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما في الأحوال المعتبرة في البروج والبيوت : ففيه وجوه من الشرائط : الأول : أن تجعل الطالع برجاً موافقاً للعمل ، وبيتاً مناسباً له . ومثاله : أنه إذا كان المطلوب أمر النكاح كان برجه هو السابع . فإن كان السابع هو الجدي فهو غير صالح له. لأن الجدي برج أرضي بارد يابس ، فإنه وقع عليه شعاع زحل ، بطل هذا المقصود بالكلية ، وإن وقع عليه شعاع الزهرة ، حصل المقصود على نوع من الضعف وإن اجتمع فيه شعاعهما قوي الضعف بسبب البرج ، وشعاع زحل فحصل المقصود مع الضعف بسبب شعاع الزهرة ، وأما إن كان السابع هو الدلو ، فإن وقع عليه شعاع الزهرة ، حصلت قوة قوية
As for the conditions considered in the signs and houses: it contains several conditions. The first: that you make the ascendant a sign compatible with the work, and a house suitable for it. An example: if the desired matter is marriage, its sign is the seventh. If the seventh is Capricorn, it is not suitable for it, because Capricorn is an earthy, cold, dry sign. If the ray of Saturn falls upon it, this purpose is completely nullified. And if the ray of Venus falls upon it, the purpose is achieved with some weakness. And if the rays of both combine on it, the weakness is strengthened because of the sign and the ray of Saturn, so the purpose is achieved with weakness due to the ray of Venus. But if the seventh is Aquarius, and the ray of Venus falls upon it, strong strength is achieved.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions for talismanic work concerning the zodiac signs and houses. It begins by stating that there are several conditions, and then elaborates on the first: the ascendant (طالع) must be a sign compatible with the work and a house appropriate for it. It gives an example: for marriage, the relevant house is the seventh (the house of partnership). If the seventh sign is Capricorn (earthy, cold, dry), it is unsuitable. The example further explains how the rays of Saturn and Venus affect the outcome: Saturn's ray nullifies, Venus's ray gives weak result, both together increase weakness. But if the seventh is Aquarius, Venus's ray brings strong strength. This demonstrates a complex astrological reasoning involving sign qualities and planetary influences.

السابع (the seventh house)
الجدي (Capricorn)
الدلو (Aquarius)
شعاع (ray)
زحل (Saturn)
الزهرة (Venus)

Key Takeaway
The first condition for talismanic work is to select a sign and house appropriate to the goal; the example of marriage shows how sign quality and planetary rays determine success or weakness.

Love Spells: Astrological Conditions
Magicians' second condition for love spells: astrological requirements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific astrological conditions magicians prescribe for love spells as part of their second condition.

Core Idea
Magicians require precise astrological alignments for love spells, not Islamic means.

This lesson examines the love spell branch of the magicians' second condition. It details requirements for the ascendant, Venus as hour lord, and lunar aspects. Understanding these false claims is essential to refute them from an Islamic standpoint.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on love spells
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the specific conditions listed.
2
Identify the required astrological elements
Look for the ascendant sign type, the hour lord planet, and the aspects between Venus and the moon, and the moon and sun.
Double-bodied signs are Gemini, Sagittarius, Pisces.
3
Understand the conditions for Venus
Venus must be aspecting the ascendant and moon, not retrograde, and not malefic.
These conditions aim for harmony.
4
Reflect on the Islamic perspective
Consider why such practices are forbidden in Islam and how they contradict tawakkul.
This prepares for refutation later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرط الثاني : قالوا : إذا أردت رقية للحب ، أو عملاً يتعلق باثنين ، فاعمله والطالع برج ذو جسدين ، ورب الساعة الزهرة ، وهي ناظرة إلى الطالع وإلى القمر ، ولا تكون راجعة ولا منحوسة بشيء من وجوه المناحس ، ولينظر القمر إلى الشمس من التثليث أو التسديس . وإذا أردت الإفساد بين إثنين ، فليكن الطالع برجاً منقلباً ، والقمر كذلك في برج منقلب ، والمريخ وزحل ناظران إلى القمر ، وخاصته زحل ، ولتكن الساعة لزحل ، وهو في وسط السماء ، ويكون قوياً، وينظر إليه النيران . وأسقط النيرين بعضهما عن البعض
The second condition: They said: If you want a ruqyah for love, or a work concerning two, then perform it while the ascendant is a double-bodied sign, and the lord of the hour is Venus, and it is aspecting the ascendant and the moon, and it is neither retrograde nor malefic in any way of malefics, and let the moon aspect the sun by trine or sextile. And if you want to cause discord between two, then let the ascendant be a mutable sign, and the moon likewise in a mutable sign, and Mars and Saturn aspecting the moon, and its characteristic is Saturn, and let the hour be for Saturn, and it is in midheaven, and be strong, and the two luminaries look at it. And drop the two luminaries from each other.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage reports the second condition prescribed by magicians for love spells and spells of discord. The condition is highly astrological. For love, the ascendant must be a double-bodied sign (like Gemini, Sagittarius, Pisces), Venus must be the hour lord and well-aspecting, the moon must trine or sextile the sun. For discord, the ascendant and moon must be in mutable signs (like Gemini, Virgo, Sagittarius, Pisces), Mars and Saturn must aspect the moon, Saturn must be the hour lord and in midheaven, strong. The phrase 'drop the two luminaries from each other' likely means to separate them in the chart. The author is likely reporting these claims to later refute their validity from an Islamic perspective, but here he simply states them.

طالع
برج ذو جسدين
رب الساعة
زهرة
ناظرة
تثليث
تسديس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That love spells with these astrological conditions actually work.
Correction: Islamic creed holds that only Allah has power over hearts; such practices are superstitious and forbidden.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

الشرط الثاني : قالوا : إذا أردت رقية للحب ، أو عملاً يتعلق باثنين ، فاعمله والطالع برج ذو جسدين ، ورب الساعة الزهرة ، وهي ناظرة إلى الطالع وإلى القمر ، ولا تكون راجعة ولا منحوسة بشيء من وجوه المناحس ، ولينظر القمر إلى الشمس من التثليث أو التسديس . وإذا أردت الإفساد بين إثنين ، فليكن الطالع برجاً منقلباً ، والقمر كذلك في برج منقلب ، والمريخ وزحل ناظران إلى القمر ، وخاصته زحل ، ولتكن الساعة لزحل ، وهو في وسط السماء ، ويكون قوياً، وينظر إليه النيران . وأسقط النيرين بعضهما عن البعض
The second condition: They said: If you want a ruqyah for love, or a work concerning two, then perform it while the ascendant is a double-bodied sign, and the lord of the hour is Venus, and it is aspecting the ascendant and the moon, and it is neither retrograde nor malefic in any way of malefics, and let the moon aspect the sun by trine or sextile. And if you want to cause discord between two, then let the ascendant be a mutable sign, and the moon likewise in a mutable sign, and Mars and Saturn aspecting the moon, and its characteristic is Saturn, and let the hour be for Saturn, and it is in midheaven, and be strong, and the two luminaries look at it. And drop the two luminaries from each other.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage reports the second condition prescribed by magicians for love spells and spells of discord. The condition is highly astrological. For love, the ascendant must be a double-bodied sign (like Gemini, Sagittarius, Pisces), Venus must be the hour lord and well-aspecting, the moon must trine or sextile the sun. For discord, the ascendant and moon must be in mutable signs (like Gemini, Virgo, Sagittarius, Pisces), Mars and Saturn must aspect the moon, Saturn must be the hour lord and in midheaven, strong. The phrase 'drop the two luminaries from each other' likely means to separate them in the chart. The author is likely reporting these claims to later refute their validity from an Islamic perspective, but here he simply states them.

Key Terms
إفساد
برج منقلب
مريخ
زحل
نيران
أسقط النيرين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That discord spells with these astrological conditions actually cause separation.
Correction: Islamic creed holds that only Allah controls hearts and affairs; such practices are false and forbidden.

Checkpoint
According to the magicians' second condition, what type of ascendant sign is required for discord spells?
A) A double-bodied sign
B) A mutable sign
C) A fixed sign
D) A cardinal sign

Key Takeaway
The magicians' second condition for discord spells relies on malefic planets and mutable signs, which is a superstitious practice rejected in Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever, even momentarily, thought that a 'lucky' or 'unlucky' star sign influenced your mood or relationships? This lesson exposes the detailed but empty claims of astrologers. Will you actively remind yourself that only Allah has power over hearts and events, and reject such superstitions from your heart?
?
Imagine you hold a grudge against someone. Do you ever wonder if the stars 'conspired' to create that enmity? This passage shows that magicians try to tap into that belief. But the truth is that enmity arises from your own soul and Shaytan. What step will you take today to purify your heart from hatred and reliance on false causes?
?
This lesson describes the specific conditions magicians use to cause discord. It reveals how detailed and elaborate their false system is. Are you willing to examine your own life for any subtle attachment to astrology, horoscopes, or 'good luck' charms—even as fun or harmless? How will you actively guard your tawheed against such hidden shirk?

The Third Condition: Matching Gender of Signs
The author states the third condition for gender matching of ascendant signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third condition for selecting ascendant signs in astrological magic, including the rule for domination and the underlying principle of like strengthening and opposite weakening.

Core Idea
Opposite genders weaken; same gender strengthens—key for domination magic.

This passage presents the third condition governing the gender of astrological signs in magical operations. The author explains that for beneficial work, the sign's gender should match the subject's, but for domination, it should be opposite. The underlying principle is that like strengthens and opposites weaken, a concept reported from the practitioners of astrological magic.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the two distinct cases presented.
2
Identify the two rules
Find the rule for beneficial work and the rule for domination. Note that one rule matches gender, the other inverts it.
3
Understand the principle
The passage ends with a general principle: 'the thing is strengthened by what agrees with it and weakened by the opposite'. Reflect on how this explains the rules.
This principle is used by magicians to justify the gender inversion for domination.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرط الثالث : إن كان عملك للإناث، فليكن الطالع برج أنثى ، وإن كان للذكور ، فبرج ذكر وأما المسلط عليه ، فالبضد . فإن كان ذكراً ، اجعل طالع العمل الموجب للتسليط عليه : أنثى وإن أنثى ، اجعل الطالع : ذكراً . وأيضاً : إن كان صاحب الطالع المسلط عليه : ذكراً ، اجعل طالع عمل التسليط عليه : أنثى . وبالضد . وذلك لأن الشيء يقوى بالموافق ، ويضعف بالضد .
The third condition: If your work is for females, then let the ascendant be a female sign, and if for males, then a male sign. As for the one who is dominated, then the opposite. For if he is male, make the ascendant of the work causing domination over him female, and if female, make the ascendant male. And also: if the owner of the ascendant of the dominated is male, make the ascendant of the work of domination over him female. And the opposite. That is because the thing is strengthened by what agrees with it, and weakened by the opposite.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage explains the third condition regarding the gender of the astrological sign. The magician must match the gender of the subject's sign to the work: for a female subject, use a female sign; for a male subject, use a male sign. However, when the goal is to dominate someone, the rule is inverted: to dominate a male, use a female sign, and to dominate a female, use a male sign. This is based on the principle that like strengthens like, while opposites weaken. The author reports this as part of the magicians' claims.

Key Terms
أنثى
ذكر
مسلط عليه
يقوى بالموافق
يضعف بالضد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that gender matching in astrology is based on essential cosmic principles rather than arbitrary magical rules.
Correction: The passage reports the magicians' claim that like strengthens and opposites weaken, but this is not a divinely ordained principle. Islamic creed rejects such causation.

Checkpoint
According to the third condition, why should you use a female ascendant for a male subject when aiming to dominate him?
A) To strengthen him
B) To weaken him
C) To make him love
D) To cause discord

Key Takeaway
The third condition requires gender matching for beneficial work and gender inversion for domination, based on the principle that like strengthens and opposites weaken.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about magicians carefully matching genders and signs to gain power over others, do you feel any subtle pull to think that there might be hidden forces besides Allah? How can you guard your heart from such whispers?
?
The magicians rely on the rule 'like strengthens, opposite weakens.' In your own life, what do you rely on for strength? Is it your plans, your connections, or Allah? Where does your trust actually lie when you face a challenge?
?
If someone offered you a 'sure method' using astrology to achieve success in love or work, would you be tempted to try it—even secretly? What does that temptation reveal about your faith in Allah's control over all outcomes?
